PL further observes that when her advice does not have the desired effect she goes a step further - she corrects the Lord by winning Him by her beautiful form and she puts the **jīvas** in the right by her overwhelming compassion.[^78_83]

In his other works also which are popularly known as Rahasyas PL brings out the **Puruṣakāratva** of Lakṣmī on several occasions. In his **Śriyappatipadi**, in the section on Dvaya he observes that as **Puruṣakāra** between man and God she has close relationships with both -- as the mother with **jīvas** and as the consort with the Lord. Explaining the word "Śrī" etymologically as **Śṛṇoti** (one who listens) and **Śrāvayati** (one who makes the Lord listen), PL argues that Lakṣmī listens to the piteous appeals of the erring living beings and makes the Lord

[^78_83]: See Sūtras 11, 12 and 13, pp. 215-231. "upadiśattāle miḻādapoḍu, cetananai aruḷāle tiruttum; Īśvaranai aḻagāle tiruttum" (Sūtra 13).

***
[[P79]]
67

also listen to them, shed his anger, and take pity upon the **jīvas**. This is in keeping with her nature as **Puruṣakāra**. He also observes that one has to do **śaraṇāgati** to the Lord only in the presence of Lakṣmī; otherwise the desired effect of **śaraṇāgati** may not be attained in full.[^79_84]

In his **Parandapaḍi**, section on Dvaya, explaining the stem "**Śrīmat**", PL points out that both the **Puruṣakāra** and **nityayoga** of Lakṣmī are implied here. The term 'Śrī' is explained through two etymologies "**Śrīyate**" (she who is resorted to) and '**śrayate**' (she who resorts to). The qualities which are expected of a Puruṣakāra are very well brought out in this work. One important quality is **ubhaya-sambandha**, that she is related to both the beings and God. She is related to the beings as their 'Mother' and to the Lord as His consort. Because she is the Mother of all the beings, she is all the time approachable by them, even without any recourse to her role as **Puruṣakāra**. Being related to the Lord as His eternal and inseparable consort she always serves Him spontaneously without any recourse to her **Puruṣakāratva**. The other interpretations of the term Śrī are **Śṛṇoti** (she listens to) and **Śrāvayati** (she makes the Lord listen to). The **jīva**, because of

[^79_84]: See **Śriyappatipaḍi**, p. 231.

***
[[P80]]
68

his crimes perpetuated from time immemorial, and being apprehensive of the Lord's anger who says, "I will throw them into hell" ( क्षिपामि )[^80_85] and 'I will not tolerate ( न क्षमामि )'[^80_86] will naturally turn to the Mother for necessary help. The Goddess listens to their appeals and passes them on to the Lord also for favour of his consideration.[^80_87]

In his Tanidvayam, '**Pūrvavākya**', PL points out that **Śrī** is not **similar** either to the **jīvas** or to the Lord. Explaining that the term 'Śrī' brings out her specific role as '**Puruṣakāra**' through the two etymologies '**Śṛṇoti**' and '**Śrāvayati**' as interpreted earlier, PL declares that the essential nature of the Lord is one of unlimited pervasion, whereas the essential nature of Lakṣmī which is very subtle like an **aṇu** (atom) becomes 'great' as the '**bhogya**' (object of enjoyment) of the Lord. Lakṣmī combines in herself two qualities -- **vaṁinitva** - with reference to the world of Cit and Acit, and also **patnītva** with reference to the Lord, both being sanctioned by **pramāṇas**. There is a passage "**puṁspradhāneśvareśvarī**" (Lakṣmī Sahasranāma) where she is said to be the ruler of not only the **jīvas**

[^80_85]: Bhagavadgītā, 16-19.
[^80_86]: Varāhapurāṇa.
[^80_87]: See Parandapaḍi, dvayaprakaraṇa, 196 ff.

***
[[P81]]
69

and Material Nature but also of the Lord. PL states out that this passage points to the total dependence of the Lord on the love of Lakṣmī because she is so attractive. Therefore there is no contradiction in the statements that although she is **aṇu** in nature, her glory is 'all-pervasive' like the Lord's. PL brings in the analogy of two flowers red in colour of which one is bereft of fragrance and the other is of natural fragrance. The glory of Lakṣmī is comparable to the latter, points out PL.[^81_88] 'If Lakṣmī is said to be superior to the Lord by virtue of her inherent qualities, what else is there to be discussed?' he asks.

The universe being subordinate to both Viṣṇu and Lakṣmī, she becomes an object of worship to the universe. She also becomes adorable to the Lord because of Her lovable character which is inherent in Her very nature. One and the same lady may be the mistress to her children and at the same time subordinate to her husband. Her husband in turn will also be subordinate to her because

[^81_88]: See PL's Tanidvayarahasyam, p.234:
"maṟukkāmpūvukkum, seṅgaḻunīrppūvukkuṁ niram ottirukkaccade, tanakku viśeṣamāṉapariṁaḷattāle seṅgaḻunīr peruvilaiyanāyitteṉṟāl veroṉṟāle vundā utkarṣamāgādire".

[[P82]]
70

of Her personal charm. This does not in any way affect the independence of the Lord. The concept of **Puruṣakāra** is also a matter of day to day experience says PL. Because of her affable character a woman becomes the protector of her children. The father, a strict disciplinarian, may sometimes behave harsh towards his children, of course in their own interest. But still they seek shelter under their Mother and she argues with her husband that the offences committed by them are very minor and that they do not deserve any serious punishment. The **Puruṣakāratva** of Lakṣmī is similar to this, concludes PL. She always abides by the Lord with the only view that she can always function as **Puruṣakāra** between Him and the creatures. The Lord is **sarvajña** (omnicient) and the **jīvas** are **sāparādha** (full of offence). Therefore the presence of **Puruṣakāra** between them is required for eternity.

Thus from the works of PL we may conclude that according to him (a) Lakṣmī is a **jīva** and hence **aṇu** (atomic) in size. This is her **svarūpa**; (b) She is always associated with the Lord as His consort; (c) She is always the kind and compassionate mother of all the beings. She therefore is superbly suited to act as the **Puruṣakāra** between them; (d) the Lord Himself, though **vibhu** by his

***
[[P83]]
71

essential nature, is always subordinate to her, being charmed by her love and affection. She forms the **śeṣiṇī** for the entire universe and thus becomes its object of adoration. She also becomes the chief object of love to her Lord because of her exquisite charm and wonderful love.

Meghanādāri Sūri (MS) probably a senior contemporary of Vedānta Deśika, in his work **Nayadyumaṇi** (ND) discusses the position of Lakṣmī.[^83_89] He is of the view that Lakṣmī is not mentioned in the Upaniṣads as the cause of the universe. Therefore she has to be included among the **Nityamuktas**. Nowhere the Vedāntas speak of two causes of the Universe. In the **Vedārthasaṁgraha**, Rāmānuja refers to Lord Nārāyaṇa alone as the **jagatkāraṇa** and establishes that he has consorts, entourage and the like. Otherwise, if the mere presence of Lakṣmī alone constitutes the causality, he would have mentioned the couple as **jagatkāraṇa**. But this is not so. The Upaniṣads too have not stated that a couple constitutes the cause. On the other hand, texts like the **Puruṣa Sūkta**

[^83_89]: See Nayadyumaṇi (ND) (GOML edn), pp. 255-256.

***
[[P84]]
72

speak of the creation as emanating from one Puruṣa as a result of his saṅkalpa. The passage 'adbhyaḥ saṁbhūtaḥ'[^84_90] refers to this and the succeeding passage "hrīśca te lakṣmīśca patnyau"[^84_91] ascribes to Him the consortship of Lakṣmī and Hrī. That is to say, He has three wives but not one since we already know Earth as the other consort of Viṣṇu through passages like 'mahīṁ devīṁ viṣṇupatnīm'.[^84_92] The word "hrī" of the Puruṣa Sūkta text must refer to another wife, namely Nīḷā. Śrī Rāmānuja also says 'evambhūtā-bhūminīḷānāyaka' etc.[^84_93]

Inspite of this declaration one cannot fix a single couple as the cause of the universe. The word 'couple' refers to one husband and one wife. Since there are three wives here, we cannot refer to all of them as forming the couple with the Lord. Nor is any one of these three consorts specifically referred to in any authoritative text as forming the couple with the Lord for purposes of

[^84_90]: Mahānārāyaṇopaniṣad, 6-11.
> अद्भ्यःसंभूतो हिरण्यगर्भ इत्यष्टौ
[^84_91]: Taittirīya Āraṇyaka, III. 13.2.
[^84_92]: Cf. Bhūsūkta, p.14 5
[^84_93]: Śaraṇāgatigadya (ŚG), p.151.

***
[[P85]]
73

creation, maintenance and dissolution of the universe. On the contrary, from passages like 'viṣṇoḥ sakāśāt udbhūtam' (VP. 1-1-31) it is clear that Viṣṇu alone, to the exclusion of any of His consorts, forms the cause of the Universe.[^85_94]

Meghanādāri Sūri then takes up the statements found in some of the stotras which attribute causality to the divine couple and discusses their little credibility. For example, there is a statement 'tvaṁ mātā sarvalokānāṁ devadevo Hariḥ pitā', where a couple seems to be the cause. The author answers in the negative, stating that in the given context Śrī alone forms the subject of praise as the Mother of the entire universe and that as such, no importance need be attached to the couple as the **jagatkāraṇa**. As for the passage quoted earlier, viz., 'Viṣṇoḥ sakāśāt' this is found clearly in the context of cosmic causality, and hence it has to be accepted as a pramāṇa. Therefore if some of the stotras, seem to declare any divine person other than the Lord Viṣṇu (including the couple Lakṣmī-Nārāyaṇa) as the cause of the universe, they have to be taken

[^85_94]: See ND., p.255.

***
[[P86]]
74

as eulogising that particular person for the purposes of the **stotra**, but not as a serious statement regarding the causality of the world. For example, Balarāma who is an incarnation of Ādiśeṣa is praised as the **jagatkāraṇa** as the one in whom everything merges in the end:[^86_95]

'tadarcyate vetsi na kiṁ yadante tvayyeva viśvam'

Ādiśeṣa whose aspect Balarāma is, is one of the Ever-liberated souls, (**nityamukta**) who have no power with regard to cosmic activities.[^86_96] Therefore if the stotras are at variance with established **pramāṇas** we cannot accord primary significance to them.

It may be asked that if Lakṣmī is not the cause, how can she be referred to as the Mother. Meghanādāri answers that because she is the consort of the Supreme Brahman, she can be called the Mother of the universe. As a matter of fact, in day to day life too, the word 'mother' is very loosely used even with reference to the other wives of one's father, even though none of

[^86_95]: ND., p.256.
[^86_96]: Cf. Brahmasūtra, 4-4-17: jagadvyāpāra varyam' etc.

***
[[P87]]
75

them is actually the source of one's birth. The real and the direct Mother is the Lord alone and none else,[^87_97] contends Meghanādāri.

He is therefore in favour of Lakṣmī's being one among the ever-liberated souls and as such he implies that she is only **aṇu** in **parimāṇa**.[^87_98]

Vātsya Varadācārya (VV), a senior contemporary of Vedānta Deśika, in his **Prapannapārijāta** (PP), in Paddhati VI, tries to show that Lakṣmī is **vibhu** like Lord Viṣṇu. He relies upon the **Viśvaksena Saṁhitā**.[^87_99] for this purpose. This Āgama declares that the entire universe is pervaded by the Lord and Lakṣmī and in this aspect there is no difference at all between them.

[^87_97]: See ND., p.256; Cf. Bhagavad Gītā: 9-17: "pitā 'hamasya jagato mātā dhātā pitāmahaḥ"
[^87_98]: He does not discuss Lakṣmī's magnitude anywhere separately in this work.
[^87_99]: Viṣvaksena Saṁhitā. However, passages he quotes are not traceable to the available Viṣvaksena Saṁhitā published by Kendriya Sanskrit Vidyāpeeṭhā, Tirupati, 1972.

***
[[P88]]
76

**Vyāpti** (pervasion) can be from two standpoints: **guṇas** (qualities) and **svarūpa** (essential nature). Both kinds of **Vyāpti** are there in the case of Lakṣmī, as in the case of the Lord. She is pervaded by the Lord and the Lord is pervaded by Her. But the difference between them consists in this: although she is the ruler of all the beings, She is subordinate to Him and is His beloved too. The Lord is the Supreme ruler with reference to Lakṣmī as well as the universe. The entire universe consisting of both the **līlā** and **nitya vibhūtis** is subordinate to the Lord and Lakṣmī. As for His two other consorts Bhūmi and Nīlā, they are subordinate to the Lord. Their pervasion is only through knowledge but not through their essential nature (**svarūpa**).[^88_100] VV also quotes from the Lakṣmī Tantra and the **Viṣṇupurāṇa** of Parāśara in support of his view that Lakṣmī in all pervasive like the Lord.[^88_101]

[^88_100]: **Prapanna Pārijāta** (ed)., Uttamur Viraraghavacarya pp. 28-29.
[^88_101]: Ibid, pp. 29-31.

***
[[P89]]
77

Another characteristic of Lakṣmī which VV states in his work is her status as **Puruṣakāra**. This is possible on two grounds: Her **vāllabhya** (being the beloved of the Lord and **Vātsalya** (motherly action towards the living beings). When she acts as the Mediator and when the Lord becomes the **upāya**, she increases His qualities like Omniscience (**jñāna**) and Omnipotence (**Śakti**); and when the souls thus saved and liberated enjoy the Lord, Lakṣmī enhances the qualities such as **saundarya** and **mādhurya** of Her Lord.[^89_102]

* * *

Vedānta Deśika (VD) in his commentary on the Catuśślokī and the Gadyatraya, in independent stotras and works like the **Nyāyasiddhāñjana** (NS) and **Rahasyatrayasāra** discusses the nature of Lakṣmī in a very elaborate manner. Of all these, His **Catuḥślokī bhāṣya** (CŚB) may said to be the most important because here he has summed up the entire range of thought on Lakṣmī depicted in a variety of texts. It is also worth noting in this context that being the advocate of the Vaḍagalai school, he has declared the following points regarding the nature and status of Lakṣmī.

1. Śrī or Lakṣmī is coeval with Lord Viṣṇu at all aspects -- **svarūpa**, **rūpa**, **guṇa** **aiśvarya** etc.

[^89_102]: Gf. PP. p.31, vv. 82-14a.

***
[[P90]]
78

2. She is all-pervasive (**vibhu**) like the Lord himself and is therefore not **aṇu** like the rest of the creatures. She is, by the same token, not a **jīva**, not even a **nityamukta**.

3. She is the most beloved of the Lord among His three consorts, the other two being Bhūmi and Nīḷā.

4. She is the mother of all the living beings and is incapable of even a trace of **nigraha** (anger), being full of overwhelming love and compassion for them.

5. It is for these reasons that she becomes the most effective **Puruṣakāra** between the Lord and the erring beings.

6. Lakṣmī and Nārāyaṇa are associated eternally as an attribute and its substantive (**Viśeṣaṇa** and **Viśeṣya**).

7. That is the reason why Lakṣmī can also be construed as the **upāya**, the means of liberation.

8. Although she is not mentioned expressly in the first of the three major Mantras (called the Rahasyas) namely the **Aṣṭākṣarī** (OM Namo Nārāyaṇāya), her presence is implied in the personality of the Lord Himself referred

***
[[P91]]
79

to by the words 'a' (अ) and 'nāra' forming part of this **Tirumantra**. In the second Rahasya, namely the **Dvayamantra**, Her presence is explicitly mentioned, suggesting that **śaraṇāgati** done to the Lord must be preceded by **śaraṇāgati** to Lakṣmī.

9. By virtue of Her inseparable association with the Lord with whom she forms the Godhead, she becomes the **śeṣiṇī** along with Him who is the **śeṣin**, and as a couple they both constitute the **upāya** (means) and **upeya** (ultimate goal) of all the living beings.

10. The spiritual quest of man comes to an end when he finds in this two-in-one 'śeṣi' couple, the recipient of all loving service (**kaiṅkarya**) which is divested of all feelings of ego. In other words, **śeṣidaṁpatī** alone is the **summum bonum** of all human life. Lakṣmī and Nārāyaṇa are conceived as two different beings functionally, but essentially and notionally 'they' are but one single indivisible principle. The usage of the word 'They' here is only for the sake of referential convenience and is not a pointer to any dichotomy or duality in the ultimate Reality. The analogy given in the **Pāñcarātrāgamas** and in the **Rāmāyaṇa** for the relation between Lakṣmī and the Lord

***
[[P92]]
80

such as 'rays and the Sun', 'the beams and the Moon', 'effulgence and the gem' and 'fragrance and the flower' are all in support of this concept of the ultimate principle of 'Lakṣmī-Nārāyaṇa-Dvandva'.

Broadly speaking, these are the ideas which we come across in the works of VD, sometimes briefly and sometimes elaborately. But as pointed out earlier, his commentary on Yāmuna's **Catuśślokī** is of great value in arriving at his consummate view on the status of Lakṣmī.[^92_103]

In the course of his commentary on the **Catuśślokī**, Deśika enumerates as many as eleven views regarding the nature, qualities, position and relation of Lakṣmī with the Brahman. Refuting these views, he comes out with five succinct statements on the status and nature of Lakṣmī which may be noted as follows:

The first view may be traced to the Teṅgalai school which accepts Lakṣmī as **aṇu** and as being dependent on the Lord, but enjoying special powers as distinguished from them.

The second concept is that she is different from all the three known well categories namely, Cit, Acit and **Īśvara**.

[^92_103]: A complete analysis of Deśika's commentary on the **Catuśślokī** may be found in Dr M.Narasimhachary's Yāmuna's Contribution to Viśiṣṭādvaita, pp.31-48.

***
[[P93]]
81

The third view is that she belongs to the category of **Īśvara**, but the Lord alone can be the **jagatkāraṇa** and in this aspect she is only inferior to Him.

The fourth view could be the view entertained by Raṅganātha the commentator on the **Śrīsūkta** to which reference has already been made. According to him, both Lord and Lakṣmī equally enjoy the attributes such as Lordship. There is no contradiction here, because, their mutual consent opens up such as possibility.[^93_104]

The fifth view which he expresses towards the end on the authority of Nārāyaṇa Muni, our author of the PM, is what Deśika himself actually subscribes to. According to this, Śrī is as pervasive as the Lord. She had become subordinate to Him. This subordination is voluntary but not obligatory because it takes place either by the free will of Lakṣmī or of her consort, or of both.

As the author of the **Puruṣakāra Mīmāṁsā** refers very often to VD and his works, and as Śrīśaileśa the commentator on the PM quotes profusely from a variety of texts of Deśika bearing upon this subject which will be analysed and studied

[^93_104]: Cf. ŚSB, p.48.

***
[[P94]]
82

in the course of this Thesis, Deśika's views presented in those texts are not separately taken up for discussion in this chapter. The point that is worth taking up now is the **Puruṣakāratva** of Lakṣmī which is incidentally common to both the Vaḍagalai and Teṅgalai schools.

The term 'Puruṣakāra' is found employed in the Pāñcarātrāgamas such as the **Viṣvaksena Saṁhitā**. One unidentified Pāñcarātra text says:

> अहंमत्प्राप्त्युपायो वै साक्षाल्लक्ष्मीपतिस्त्वयम्।
> लक्ष्मीः पुरुषकारेण वक्ष्मा प्राश्योजिनी।।
> एतस्याश्च विशेषोऽयं निगमान्तेषु शब्द्यते।।

The following passage is ascribed to the **Viṣvaksena Saṁhitā** where the term Puruṣakāra is employed.

> आखिरग्रन्थैकधारणाः केचिद् भाग्याचिकाः पुनः।
> मत्पदाम्भोरुहद्वन्द्वं प्रपद्य प्रीतमानसाः।।
> लक्ष्मीं पुरुषकारेण वृतवन्तो वशनम्।
> मत्क्षणं प्राप्य सेनेत्रा प्राप्यं प्रापकमेव माम्।
> लब्ध्वा कृतार्थाः प्राप्स्यन्ते मामेवानन्द्यमानसाः।।

***
[[P95]]
83

Śrī Tirumaḻiśai Appāppaṅgār Svāmī, in his commentary Arumpadavilakkam on the **Śrīvacanabhūṣaṇa** of Piḷḷai Lokācārya explains the term 'Puruṣakāra' in four different ways in the "Prakaraṇavibhāga'. The word 'Puruṣa' refers to the Supreme Being Nārāyaṇa, and also to the **jīva** (individual soul). The etymology of the term is: '**puruṣaṁ karoti iti puruṣakāraḥ**'. With reference to the Supreme Being, the following three interpretations are possible:

1. Puruṣaḥ pūrgatvāt puruṣaḥ (from the root 'pṛ' - pālanapūraṇayoḥ). Then the explanation would be:
"**bhagavantaṁ kṣamādipūrṇaṁ, ujjvalakāruṇyaviśiṣṭaṁ karoti iti puruṣakāraḥ**".
To explain, Lakṣmī, by her intercession, brings out the latent virtues such as mercy and parental love belonging to the Lord, to a fuller display.

2. Puruṣaḥ - 'pālanāt puruṣaḥ' (from the root 'pṛ' itself, in the sense of 'pālana' or protection). The explanation would then be: "**bhagavantaṁ pālakaṁ, arthāt rakṣakaṁ karoti iti puruṣakāraḥ**".
Lakṣmī makes the Lord 'the protector of the **jīvas**'.

***
[[P96]]
93

Śrī Tirumaḻiśai Appāppaṅgār Svāmī, in his commentary Arumpadavilakkam on the **Śrīvacanabhūṣaṇa** of Piḷḷai Lokācārya explains the term 'Puruṣakāra' in four different ways in the 'Prakaraṇavibhāga'. The word 'Puruṣa' refers to the Supreme Being Nārāyaṇa, and also to the **jīva** (individual soul). The etymology of the term is: '**puruṣaṁ karoti iti puruṣakāraḥ**'. With reference to the Supreme Being, the following three interpretations are possible:

1. Puruṣaḥ pūrgatvāt puruṣaḥ (from the root 'pṛ' - pālanapūraṇayoḥ). Then the explanation would be:
"**bhagavantaṁ kṣamādipūrṇaṁ, ujjvalakāruṇyaviśiṣṭaṁ karoti iti puruṣakāraḥ**".
To explain, Lakṣmī, by her intercession, brings out the latent virtues such as mercy and parental love belonging to the Lord, to a fuller display.

2. Puruṣaḥ - 'pālanāt puruṣaḥ' (from the root 'pṛ' itself, in the sense of 'pālana' or protection). The explanation would then be: "**bhagavantaṁ pālakaṁ, arthāt rakṣakaṁ karoti iti puruṣakāraḥ**".
Lakṣmī makes the Lord 'the protector of the **jīvas**'.

***
[[P97]]
84

3. Puruṣaḥ - 'puru-bahu, sunoti-dadāti iti puruṣaḥ'. The interpretation, then is: '**bhagavantaṁ bahuphala-pradaṁ karoti iti puruṣkāraḥ**'.
Lakṣmī makes the Lord confer many a boon on the **jīvas**.

These three definitions point to the Lord as 'Puruṣa' who is made by Lakṣmī to display in a full measure, his qualities of mercy, protection and generosity.

The following definition is based on the interpretation of the word 'Puruṣa' as the **jīva** (individual soul).

4. Puruṣaḥ - jīvaḥ (from the root 'pura' = agragamane). The etymology is: '**puruṣaṁ (jīvan) agragāminaṁ karoti iti puruṣakāraḥ**'
Lakṣmī, by her timely intercession and proper advice, makes the **jīva** turn towards the Lord for his protection and forgiveness, and thus helps him. This meaning is made possible since 'pura' means 'going or marching ahead'. To explain,
"**bhagavad-āśrayaṇavimukhaṁ jīvaṁ bhagavad-agragāminaṁ, bhagavadunmukhaṁ karoti**".

***
[[P98]]
85

Śrī Embār Jeer of Śrīperumbudur, in his Arumbada-vilakkam on the **Śrīvacanabhūṣaṇa**, gives another etymology for the word '**Puruṣakāra**':

"**Puruṣau** = **jīvātma-paramātmānau parasparalābhena sattāvantau karoti iti puruṣakāraḥ lakṣmīḥ**".

Lakṣmī is called the '**Puruṣakāra**' because she makes the Supreme Brahman and the **jīva** attain their respective existences. In other words, the Supreme Being becomes similar to an insentient entity unless He attains the individual self (**jīva**). Likewise, the **jīva** also becomes similar to a non-entity unless he reaches the Supreme Being. To put it in Sanskrit -

'**paramātmalābhaṁ vinā jīvātmā asat-samaḥ;
jīvātmalābhaṁ vinā paramātmapi acit-samaḥ**'.

Śrī Tirumaḻiśai Appāppaṅgār Svāmī points out that the word '**Puruṣakāra**' can afford manifold meanings, as in the case of the sacred mantra, '**Oṁ Namo Nārāyaṇāya**', where the members '**a**', '**ma**', '**nārāyaṇa**', etc., are interpreted in more than one way. He says -

"**akāra** - **makāra** - **Nārāyaṇa** - **Śrīsabdādigaḷaippole puruṣakāraśabdamum anekārthaparam**".

***
[[P99]]
86

Keeping in mind her role as 'Puruṣakāra', the term 'Śrī' is also explained in different ways in the Śrīvaiṣṇava tradition. The following verse in the Ahirbudhnya Saṁhitā (LI bI-62a) sums up all these interpretations:

> शृणाति निखिलाऩ् दोषाऩ् शृणाति च गुणैर्जगत्।
> श्रीयते चाखिलैर्नित्यं श्रयते च परं पदम्।।
> श्रयन्तीं श्रीयमाणां च शृण्वतीं शृण्वतीमपि।।
> (XXI - 8)

Śrī is so called because:

1. She is the one who is resorted to by the erring living beings (śrīyate cetanair iti);
2. She is the one who herself resorts to the Supreme Lord (śrayate bhagavantam iti);
3. She is the one who listens to the appeals of those who seek refuge under her (śṛṇoti āśrita-vijñāpanam iti);
4. She is the one who counsels the **jīvas** who are averse to God (śrāvayati vimukhān iti), or She is the one who makes the Lord listen to the appeals of the erring souls who have resorted to her (śrāvayati bhagavantaṁ svāśrita-vijñāpanam iti);

***
[[P100]]
87

5. She is the one who removes or destroys (lit. 'cooks') the offences of those who resort to Her (śṛṇāti = hinasti/pacati āśritadoṣān iti); and
6. She is the one who makes those who resort to her, increase or prosper through their virtues (śṛṇāti = āśritān guṇair vistārayati vardhayati iti).
* * * * *

***
[[P101]]
88

## NĀRĀYAṆA MUNI VS VEDĀNTA RĀMĀNUJA
DIFFERENCES BETWEEN NĀRĀYAṆA MUNI AND VEDĀNTA RĀMĀNUJA

Having studied the text of PM in detail it is worthwhile to note the main differences between Nārāyaṇa Muni and his chief critic Vedānta Rāmānuja Muni in a codified manner in this chapter. Our understanding of the text of PM is mainly based upon the Maṇidīpikā of ŚŚ, who, as pointed out earlier, must have been the direct disciple of NM. Scholars are of the opinion that the first five pontiffs of the Ahobila Maṭha could have been subscribers to the views of Piḷḷai Lokācārya on the essential nature and role of Lakṣmī.[^101_1] The criticism of VR against NM could have been mainly based upon this conception that what NM was trying to explain in his PM was more in keeping with his Teṅgalai tradition than with the Vaḍagalai tradition represented by Vedānta Deśika.

NM in the very opening verse of PM, may be said to have summarised the central theme of his work.

> स्वतन्त्रः स्वेच्छया सृष्टिस्थितिसंहारमोक्षणे।
> यत्सङ्गं क्रीडतीशः तां भजे लोकमातरम्।। 1।।

[^101_1]: For details see R.C.Lester, 'Renunciation in Śrī Vaiṣṇavism', JOR, Vol.LVI-LXII, p.94.

***
[[P102]]
89

According to NM, creation, maintenance, dissolution and liberation of the Universe are the functions of the Lord who is the only independent principle. All these activities take place due to His own free will. He does all these in the presence of the Divine Mother Lakṣmī, which activity becomes their sport. A number of ideas can be deduced from this simple verse:

(1) Viṣṇu and Lakṣmī form the Divine Couple. The Lord alone is responsible for full-fledged creation, dissolution etc.

(2) The role of Lakṣmī can be appreciated as the Mother of the Universe, since she is the consort of the Lord. She is not directly connected with all those cosmic functions, which the Lord performs. The commentary of ŚŚ brings out the subtleties of this view and explains that Lakṣmī can never have any activity involving or even implying **nigraha**. The subsequent verse:

> स्वयं व्यक्तं रङ्गधाम्नि
> तल्पे वातुल कुल्मके।
> निवसन्तो नमाम्याद्यौ
> दम्पती जनको विधेः।। 2।।

qualifies the meaning of the first verse by declaring that this Divine Couple (identified with Lord Raṅganātha and

***
[[P103]]
90

Raṅganāyakī at Śrīraṅgam) form the parents of Brahmā the four-faced creator God. This verse points out that **jagajjanakatva** (being parents of the universe) need not be taken in a secondary sense as **pitṛtva**. It could even mean being the creators directly as in the case of Brahmā who is accepted on all hands as the son of this Divine Couple.

When these two verses are read together it becomes clear that Lakṣmī, the Divine Mother could have been the direct parent of the Brahmā in the primary sense and Mother for the rest of the universe in a secondary sense. The works of VD speak of Lakṣmī as an attribute of the Lord since she is His '**patnī**'. The secondary status of the '**patnī**' cannot be denied, contends NM. There are several instances in the scriptural passages which posit similarity between the Lord and His consort. There are also passages speaking of utmost similarity (**atyanta-tulyatā**) between them. The chief purpose of PM therefore, is to decide beyond doubt if Lakṣmī the Patnī can lay claims to all the features of Her Lord, in the manner He possesses them 'patnyāḥ pativadīdrktvam asti neti nirūpyate' (PM. p.6).

Vedānta Rāmānuja Muni whose ŚTS was 'designed chiefly to demolish' the PM, takes exception to the stand taken by NM on one important issue namely Her Upāyatva.

***
[[P104]]
91

According to NM, Lord alone is the direct means of salvation but not Lakṣmī. Lakṣmī's being the **upāya** for Mokṣa is also acknowledged in some scriptural and Āgama passages and openly expressed in the **stotras** of Ācāryas as well. But NM prefers to explain this **upāyatva** through Lakṣmī's status as an 'attribute' of the Lord and never as the substantive, that is the Lord. Regarding **nigraha** also, while VR points out **sāmarthya** (capacity) to punish the wicked as being present in the Divine Mother, NM contends that even granting this, Lakṣmī never desires to display it.

"**śaktiḥ śriyo'sti neccheti**" (Kārikā 41a)

For NM the **Viśeṣaṇatva** of Lakṣmī is the key which unlocks the flood-gates of a number of features such as **kāraṇatva**, **upāsyatva**, **upāyatva** and **prāpyatva**. Her creation is marked by pure and unalloyed grace. She receives the **Bhara**, and confers upon the devotees supreme Bliss through sheer love and affection. The Lord is a **daṇḍadhara** but Lakṣmī is entirely devoid of this quality. In so far as conferring Mokṣa is concerned while VR contends that Lakṣmī is as powerful and full-fledged an **upāya** as the Lord is, NM makes her the **upāya** through the

***
[[P105]]
92

golden means of Her status as an Attribute. The passage '**kāraṇatvādi na śriyaḥ**' shows that the kind of **kāraṇatva** mentioned of Brahman in the Śrutis and Brahmasūtra is not found in Lakṣmī. It does not deprive Lakṣmī of Her glory or status. The Lord is all the time qualified by Lakṣmī. Therefore whatever functions the Lord, has Lakṣmī also can share in. One cannot imagine a substantive without an attribute. Whatever feature the substantive possesses can also be ascribed to the **Viśeṣaṇa** which is a part and parcel of the substantive.

Lakṣmī's role as **jagatkāraṇa**, as intended by Vedānta Deśika in his NS and other works, has been fully subscribed to by NM in his PM. Deśika's CŚB speaks of the relationship of Lakṣmī with Her Lord in terms of **svāmitva**, **saulabhya**, **phaladatva** and **phalatva**. The word **phaladatva** means **upāyatva**. That Lakṣmī also becomes an **upāya** through Her status as Lord's consort is acceptable to Deśika himself, contends NM.

Lakṣmī can also confer Mokṣa, but not in the way Her husband does. The Lord confers Mokṣa only after giving up His wrath. But in the case of Lakṣmī since she is incapable of getting angry, Her conferring Mokṣa will be through Her pure grace alone.[^105_2]

[^105_2]: See PM. Kārikā. 41a. p.12: '**śaktiḥ śriyo'sti neccheti**'

***
[[P106]]
93

According to NM, Lakṣmī being the attribute of the Lord becomes the soul of the entire universe which forms Her body. She becomes a **śeṣiṇī**, she forms the **kartrī**, **niyantrī**, the source of all Bliss and the chief object of meditation like Her Lord. She is all-pervasive and also the ruler like the Lord. But she is still subordinate to the Lord by mutual will and understanding. VR's criticism that NM makes Lakṣmī equal to the **jīvas** is quite unfounded. The definition given in the NS to **Īśvaratva**, is '**svajñāna-svetara-dravya-śarīrakatvam**' ('possessing everything other than Himself and the knowledge as His body'). The characteristics of the **jīva**'are said to be eight in number, viz., **ādheyatva**, **vidheyatva**, **śeṣatva** and **aṇutva** each of which is to be taken to qualify **cetana**tvam and **ahantva**ṁ severally. The characteristic of the Lord are four-fold viz., '**mumukṣūpāsyatva**; **mokṣapradatva**; **prāpyatva** and **ananyādhāratva**'.

According to NM Lakṣmī can never be similar to a **jīva**. Lakṣmī is coeval with the Lord in all His aspects excepting in Her having **nigraha**. There is **sāmya** between both of them but not in so far as **nigraha** and its effects are concerned.[^106_3]

[^106_3]: Text of PM, p. 38.

***
[[P107]]
94

According to NM the definition of **Īśvara** found in the NS has nothing to do with Lakṣmī's nature. It is meant to preclude Brahmā, Indra and other gods from the scope of the definition. According to VR's charge NM should agree that Lakṣmī also being the body of the Lord becomes equal to a **jīva**, in which case he cannot claim any special status for Her. If Lakṣmī's **sāmya** with the Lord is accepted, she being co-eval with Him in all His aspects, she too will be included in the definition of **Īśvara**.

In so far as Her **svarūpa** is concerned, Lakṣmī according to NM is **pāratantra** (dependent on the Lord). This **pāratantrya** is subjected to the will of both. In the case of **jīvas** however, it is purely dependent on the will of the Lord. Therefore Lakṣmī can never be a **jīva**, since she lacks in **svātantrya** and **nigraha**. According to the true and full implication of **Bṛhattva**, from the viewpoint of **svarūpa** and **guṇa**, she cannot be the connotation of the term **Brahman**, points out NM. This clearly defines the position of NM regarding the nature and status of Lakṣmī. Total similarity between them in all aspects is what VR stresses which has its own limitations according to NM, as explained by ŚŚ. Lakṣmī's

***
[[P108]]
95

'independence' is marked by Her 'dependence on the Lord's will'. According to NM, Deśika's **Gadya Bhāṣya** and **Tattvatīkā** make this point clear.[^108_4]

NM repeatedly refers to the fact that Lakṣmī becomes the ruler of the Universe only on the ground of having both the **Vibhūtis** under Her control. In this she is on par with the Lord.[^108_5] But regarding **hetutva**, **upāsyatva** etc., Lord alone possesses them but Lakṣmī can also lay claim to them through Her status as an attribute of the Lord. Even forming the object of meditation (**upāsyatva**) is different in the case of Lakṣmī. One prays to the Lord alone for having the experience of complete Bliss. Lakṣmī also may enter the picture only as an attribute of the Brahman because she, as a **Puruṣakāra**, helps to remove the **nigraha** of the Lord and thus can find a place there also. She does not form the direct object of meditation.

The main reason for controversies regarding the nature and status of Lakṣmī can be traced to various

[^108_4]: See PM, Kārikās 11-12.
[^108_5]: Kārikās 23 to 27 ab.

***
[[P109]]
96

scriptural passages and the varying statements of the **ācāryas**. Some texts speak of her **sāmya** with the Lord. Others refer to their **aikya**; others refer to Lakṣmī as the **śakti** of **ahantā** or **tadvattā**. Deśika has tried to interpret all these passages in a very synthetic and pragmatic manner. The golden principle of **dāmpatya** between Śrī and Viṣṇu is the thesis developed by Deśika. With this principle of **dāmpatya**, everything can explained satisfactorily. **Tadvattā** or **śaktitva** ultimately means **Viśeṣaṇatva**, according to NM.

Though a **Viśeṣaṇa** of the Lord, Lakṣmī according to NM has her own essential difference from the Lord (**svarūpa-bheda**) as in the case of the beams and the Moon. Yāmuna's statement '**kāntāste**' using the sixth case (in ते) really brings out the difference between Lakṣmī and the Lord and in fact this is the reflection of the **śruti**-passage 'hrīśca te lakṣmīśca patnyau' (Taittirīya Āraṇyaka 3-13-2).

According to NM, the Supreme Brahman qualified by Śrī alone is the object of prapatti. The definition of[^109_6]

[^109_6]: > श्रीज्ञास्तस्मात् सर्व हेतुरप्ये ध्यसंव मुमुक्षुभिः। रक्षकश्च श्रीया सार्धं प्राप्यश्चेति सतां मतम्।।१।।

***
[[P110]]
97

prapatti '**ananya-sādhye**' etc., the mantra which speaks of it viz., the **Dvaya** and the **Caramaśloka** which ordains it, several Āgama texts, and the **Śrī Bhāṣya** of Rāmānuja and the tradition are in favour of status of Lakṣmī as a **Viśeṣaṇa**. She can never become an **upalakṣaṇa** as alleged by others. Lakṣmī and the Lord both become the recipients of '**ātmahavis**' in the context of what is known as '**avanayajña**'. The Lord is the **Yajamāna** and Lakṣmī being His patnī also receives this Havis. This clearly states that Lakṣmī becomes an attribute alone like other guṇas and vigraha of the Lord.[^110_7]

Lakṣmī's upayoga in the 'sacrifice of protection' lies in generating a steady love and concentration towards Him in his devotees. She does things favourable to the Lord by giving consent to His protective function. She removes the unapproachability, '**ādhṛṣyatva**' of the Lord by Her very presence. Even during the stage of **Nyāsa** she remains an attribute of the Lord; she destroys the sins of devotees, generates a taste for the Lord who is the goal, and ensures His grace for them. All this is the implication of Her **Puruṣa-kāratva** alone.[^110_8]

[^110_7]: Kārikā > गुणविग्रहवल्लक्ष्मीः प्रपन्नस्य विशेषणम्। 81।
[^110_8]: Cf. '**śṛṇāti nikhilān doṣān**' etc. (Ah. Saṁ.LI.61b-62a)

***
[[P111]]
98

According to NM and VR Lakṣmī forms the **Puruṣakāra** also. They both agree that there is as **sāmarthya** in her. But VR tries relate this **sāmarthya** to **kriyā**, and thus, make Lakṣmī the **sahakartrī** in the act of protection. This according to him is the **upāyatva**. But according to NM as explained by ŚŚ, **sāmarthya** must necessarily involve **kriyā**, which in the case of Lakṣmī is not possible. In other words she cannot do things directly involving **nigraha** as the Lord does. Therefore there is between them what is called **aikarasya** which means **sāmarasya**. It is this 'identity of tastes' that makes Lakṣmī indirectly, a component in the scheme of **upāya**. Thus the main difference between NM and VR lies in establishing Lakṣmī's **upāyatva** through **sāmarasya** and not merely through **sāmarthya**. Even her role as **Puruṣakāra** becomes fruitful only through **sāmarasya**.[^111_9]

As a **Viśeṣaṇa** of the Lord she becomes the **kāraṇa** also, of course indirectly. She is different from gods like Brahmā and Indra who in the **Pratardanavidyā** form the **viśeṣaṇas** of the Lord. This is the difference between NM and VR: Though dependent on the Lord, Lakṣmī can grant **Mokṣa** also by granting **sāmya** etc.

[^111_9]: > ऐकरस्यव्यपदेशः सोविदद्ध्यत्याः सर्वकर्मसु
>

***
[[P112]]
99

NM is of the opinion that the excellence of Lakṣmī strictly speaking, is dependent upon the Lord and therefore, it is not natural to her ('**svatassiddhā**'). But this **guṇabhāva** is the result of mutual will, (**ubhayecchā**). Still this does not undermine her greatness.

According to NM Lakṣmī cannot be the means of liberation 'after shedding anger' (**kopanivṛttipūrvaka**) because this is a feature unique with the Lord only. When a substantive which is qualified is totally negated the intention is to negate the attribute only.

VR charges NM for equating Lakṣmī with other **pāratantra-jīvas**, and making her devoid of **subāśrayatva**, by denying her the powers to grant **Mokṣa**. But according to NM she does not have the desire to confer **mokṣa** like the Lord. Lakṣmī is the abode of all auspiciousness according to NM also. Her **upāyatva** lies in her bestowing the experience of complete bliss on the **jīvas** but the **upāyatva** of the Lord lies in His conferring such an experience after shedding His wrath. Duality of **upāyas** is not acceptable to NM either. The relation of Lakṣmī with the Lord is comparable to the one between a gem and its radiance, flower and its fragrance, the Moon and her

***
[[P113]]
100

beams, nectar and its sweetness. This is natural but not adventitious. Śrī is an **apṛthaksiddha-dharma** of the Lord. Her relation with Him is '**yāvadātmabhāvī**' (as long as she exists), which means 'eternal'.

Lakṣmī removes or destroys all the **doṣas** in those who surrender and this helps the blooming of the **upāya** to its fulness. As explained by ŚŚ under the **kārikā** the special destination of the PM lies in the fact that Lakṣmī has been explained as an **upāya** through her status as **viśeṣaṇa** but not as the **upāya** directly, as held by VR. This is acceptable to VD as understood from RTS and NT. Kumāravarada in his commentary on NT has also explained Lakṣmī's status as an attribute on the analogy of certain Vedic expressions like '**mahendra**', and '**agniṣoma**'[^113_10] involving Dvandva Compound. The same point is also emphasised under the **sūtra**, '**vṛddhihrāsa**' etc. (**Brahma-sūtra**: 3-2-20) as explained by Rāmānuja.

Another difference between NM and VR is regarding the implication of the word **dampati**. According to VR, it indicates equal status between both husband and wife

[^113_10]: > विशेषणेन सम्बन्धो चैतन्ये वास्य देशिके।
> इशिता शौनह्यान्ता घटकोपेश रक्षितः।।
> [K 104 ]

***
[[P114]]
101

(**samaprādhānya**). But for NM, who quotes Varadācārya's commentary of NT, relatively Lord is more important. Several sections of the RTS also indicate this. Because she is a **viśeṣaṇa** to the Lord, she has lesser importance than the Lord. Equal importance is not possible. Whatever kind of **prapatti** one may do to the Lord, **svarūpa**, **bhara** or **phala**, she remains only a **viśeṣaṇa** to the Lord.[^114_11] Even in **yantras**(motifs) dedicated to Lakṣmī, the overall importance of Lakṣmī cannot be accepted, the Lord being the innermost controller of Lakṣmī also. He becomes the **uddeśya** of worship here too.

The salient features of PM are found in the commentary of ŚŚ towards the end of the text. Lakṣmī is the direct agent in all the cosmic activities involving **anugraha**. But in activities involving **nigraha** which is the special prerogative of the Lord, she becomes only a prompting agent. She is also the inner controller of all the beings. She is also the **ādhāra** of all, of course expecting the Lord. Her control (**niyamana**) of the living beings is[^114_12]

[^114_11]: > यद्यप्याम्हनिर्वर्त्ये प्राधान्यमभ्युधोरपि।
> विशेषणं शरव्यस्य भर्जन्यस् तथ्यापि था।।
> K110।।
[^114_12]: PM. text P.No. 361.

***
[[P115]]
102

through pure love and motherly affection. She becomes the mistress of the Universe (**śeṣiṇī**) quite naturally but not as a result of any adventitious condition. She is all-pervasive and forms the recipient of **ātmahavis**. She functions as the **Puruṣakāra**, becoming the **viśeṣaṇa** of the Lord. Like the Lord she too has Cit and Acit as Her body. She is the mother of the entire creation and as a result of mutual will between herself and the Lord, she becomes the **śeṣā**, **niyāmyā**, **pāratantrā** and **ādheyā** in relation to the Lord. Another special point which NM stresses is that she is not a mere bestower of wealth (**dhanadā**) as held by some. Towards the end of the text NM stresses that as outlined by Deśika in his **Catuśślokī-bhāṣya** both in the opening and concluding portions, Lakṣmī is always associated with the Lord and thereby removes the fear of those who want to approach Him. If the Lord is the **Svāmī**, she becomes the **Svāminī**. She is **sulabhā**, **phaladā** and the **phala** itself purely by her association with the Lord as an attribute.

We may therefore conclude that the points of difference between NM and VR are only limited. All these differences boil down to **upāyatva** only, which

***
[[P116]]
103

is the main point of contention between VR and NM. The **kāraṇatva** of Lakṣmī is also a moot point. So is her **viśeṣaṇatva**. NM argues that by virtue of Her **viśeṣaṇatva** only Lakṣmī can be justified as the **upāya**, **upeya**, **kāraṇa**, **Puruṣakāra**, **Īśvarī** and so on. This concept of **viśeṣaṇatva** has been there in the very nature of Lakṣmī, scriptures confirm it and tradition allows it. That she is the **patnī** of the Lord makes her automatically subordinate to Him as the co-performer of his duties. This only adds to the excellence of Śrī and the Lord, because both of them,by mutual will, have become the couple. A comparative study of these two works of the ācāryas viz., the PM and ŚTS inspite of their apparent controversies and contradictions, is a rewarding experience in itself as it highlights several subtle points of the tradition which have their own place and value.

* * * * * * *

***
[[P117]]
104

## DETAILED ANALYSIS
DETAILED ANALYSIS OF THE PURUṢAKĀRA MĪMĀṀSĀ WITH THE COMMENTARY MAṆIDĪPIKĀ

The **Puruṣakāra-mīmāṁsā** (PM) of Nārāyaṇa Muni, has a lucid commentary **Maṇidīpikā** by Śrīśaileśa (ŚŚ) which helps in understanding the intricacies of the concept of Śrī as **Puruṣakāra**. ŚŚ explains each and every word of the **śloka** providing scriptural evidences such as those from Vedas, Upaniṣads, the Rāmāyaṇa, Mahābhārata, Viṣṇupurāṇa etc. He also provides supporting passages from the works of earlier ācāryas, like Yāmuna, Rāmānuja Kūreśvara, Parāśara Bhaṭṭa and Vedānta Deśika. The bulk of his quotations is from the **Catuśślokī** with Deśika's commentary.

After paying obeisance to Lord Kuranganātha the presiding deity at Thirukkuruṅguḍi and His consort, Viṣvaksena and Nammāḻvār, Śrīśaileśa mentions Śrī Rāmānuja, Varada Viṣṇvārya and Vedānta Deśika as the ācāryas who established the Viśiṣṭādvaita tradition. Then he refers to his own father Vātsya Rājagopāla at whose feet he learnt about the real nature of Lakṣmī and Her consort. He also refers to one Ammāḷārya as his teacher. Then he refers to Śrīmannārāyaṇa Muni

***
[[P118]]
106

all that the Lord performs, including destruction. But since she is purely of the nature of **Anugraha** (compassion) and also since the scriptures state that Bhagavān alone is the **daṇḍadhara** (chastiser), Lakṣmī can never be directly connected with activities involving **nigraha**; she can only indirectly be related to such activities. But there is nothing objectionable in her being directly connected with activities involving **anugraha**.

ŚŚ then moves on to the next verse, 'Svayam vyakte'.[^118_3] This is also by way of paying obeisance to the Divine Couple abiding in Śrīraṅgam on the serpent couch.

ŚŚ then takes up the verse 'Śrípatiḥ' etc.[^118_4] He does not comment upon the following verse which is a prayer to Viṣvaksena, the consort of Sūtravatī, who creates sustains and destroys the universe by his mere Saṅkalpa, and who puts off all impediments, by the vibrations of his Vetra.

> सङ्कल्पेनैव यो विश्वं सृजत्यवति हन्ति यः।
> वेत्रस्पन्दास्तविधिं तं वन्दे सूत्रवतीश्वम्।। (v. 3.)

[^118_3]: > स्वयंव्यक्ते रङ्गधाम्नि तल्पे वातुलकुल्मके।
> निवसन्तो नमाम्याद्यौ दम्पती जनको विधेः।। (v. 2.)
[^118_4]: No: 3.Maṇidīpikā.

***
[[P119]]
106

all that the Lord performs, including destruction. But since she is purely of the nature of **Anugraha** (compassion) and also since the scriptures state that Bhagavān alone is the **daṇḍadhara** (chastiser), Lakṣmī can never be directly connected with activities involving **nigraha**; she can only indirectly be related to such activities. But there is nothing objectionable in her being directly connected with activities involving **anugraha**.

ŚŚ then moves on to the next verse, 'Svayam vyakte'.[^119_3] This is also by way of paying obeisance to the Divine Couple abiding in Śrīraṅgam on the serpent couch.

ŚŚ then takes up the verse 'Śrípatiḥ' etc.[^119_4] He does not comment upon the following verse which is a prayer to Viṣvaksena, the consort of Sūtravatī, who creates sustains and destroys the universe by his mere Saṅkalpa, and who puts off all impediments, by the vibrations of his Vetra.

> सङ्कल्पेनैव यो विश्वं सृजत्यवति हन्ति यः।
> वेत्रस्पन्दास्तविधिं तं वन्दे सूत्रवतीश्वम्।। (v. 3.)

[^119_3]: > स्वयंव्यक्ते रङ्गधाम्नि तल्पे वातुलकुल्मके।
> निवसन्तो नमाम्याद्यौ दम्पती जनको विधेः।। (v. 2.)
[^119_4]: No: 3.Maṇidīpikā.

***
[[P120]]
107

Commenting on Kārikā, 'Śrīpatiḥ' etc., ŚŚ observes that Lord Viṣṇu alone, to the exclusion of all others independently confers Mokṣa, when resorted to by those who are desirous of it. But doubts have been raised by some people regarding the exact nature and powers of Śrī because, in the works of the earlier ācāryas are found statements that Lakṣmī also, like the Lord is the ruler of all and that there is therefore, **sāmya** (similarity) between them. There are others who state that there is utmost identity (**atyanta-tulyatā**) between the Lord and Lakṣmī on several issues such as causality of the entire universe, being the refuge of all, and conferment of Mokṣa. Some others are however of the view that utmost similarity cannot be the meaning of expressions like **Sarveśvaratva** (being the ruler of all) because there are innumerable āgama-texts and also the declarations of Śrī Vedānta Deśika to the effect that Lakṣmī happens to be the **patnī** and an attribute (**viśeṣaṇa**) of the Lord, and also that she is the Mother and **Puruṣakāra** of all living beings. Therefore **atyanta-sāmya** must be understood in a slightly narrower sense, they argue. Because of these controversial view-points Nārāyaṇa Muni (NM) undertook to compose the **Puruṣakāra Mīmāṁsā** with a view to clear all doubts and establish the true nature

***
[[P121]]
108

of Lakṣmī according to the highest traditions of Viśiṣṭādvaita Vedānta. Thus he states '**patnyāḥ pativadīdrktvamasti neti nirūpyate**'. So the real concern of this work is to examine whether or not Lakṣmī also becomes an independent cause like the Lord, and also to find out if she becomes a means of liberation and the recipient of **śaraṇāgati** like Him.

The **Pūrvapakṣa**-view raised by NM is that Lakṣmī also is the Cause of the universe, the person to be resorted to and the bestower of **Mokṣa** directly since there are scriptural statements that she is equal to the Lord in all respects. These **Pūrvapakṣins** attribute this view to Vedānta Deśika himself, but NM points out that the **Siddhānta**-view entertained by Vedānta Deśika is that the Lord alone is the cause of the Universe and that He has to be resorted to for liberation; that He becomes the protector and the goal to be attained along with Lakṣmī (**śriyā sārdham**). ŚŚ points out that all **pramāṇas** and established tradition are unanimous that Lakṣmī exists for the sake of the Lord for eternity (**nityasiddha-patipāratantrya**). She is the Mother and hence Her nature is of the very essence of **anugraha** or mercy. Therefore there

***
[[P122]]
109

is nothing wrong in Her being construed as the cause of the universe,the object of refuge and the bestower of Mokṣa, like the Lord. She is also the goal of human endeavour like Him. She is incapable of being hard-hearted (**nighrahabhāva**) and so, all the contingencies of 'strictness' such as creation of different kinds of hells,various types of punishments therein, etc., do not arise in her case. Therefore, strictly speaking, she cannot be called the cause of the universe 'in its entirety' (**nikhila**). It is for this very reason (i.e. since she cannot get angry) she cannot also be the recipient of **bhara-samarpaṇa** which is marked by the absence of strictness although she becomes the recipient of **bhara-samarpaṇa** characterised by pure grace. Therefore this kind of **upāyatva**, i.e., conferring the fruit after 'giving up the strictness' (**nigraha-nivṛtti-ghaṭita**) also becomes absurd in the case of Lakṣmī. She becomes the goal (**prāpya**)by becoming the recipient of different kinds of **Kaiṅkarya** rendered by the different souls. There is no question of **nigraha** at all in her and there is total similarity between her and the Lord on this issue of being the recipients of **Kaiṅkarya**. This is the final settled opinion of the **Siddhāntin**, says ŚŚ. The point to be kept in mind is that creating, sustaining, dissolving and emancipating the cosmos

***
[[P123]]
110

in toto naturally involves a tendency to be strict and hard-hearted, readiness to punish the evil-doers (**nigraha**), if necessary. All these certainly become the characteristics of the Supreme Brahman but not Lakṣmī. This is the quintessential point on which the present text is based, points out Śrīśaileśa.

Introducing the next verse which discusses the role of Lakṣmī regarding creation etc of the universe, ŚŚ brings in the view entertained by Vedānta Rāmānuja (VR) in his **Śrītattva Siddhāñjana** (ŚTS).[^123_5] According to ŚTS the Lord's essential nature, which is peculiar to Himself, is marked by the **ṣāḍguṇya**, five aspects (**para**, **vyūha**, etc.) and creation, maintenance, dissolution and emancipation of all the worlds. These must be held to be common in the case of Lakṣmī also; or otherwise, Lakṣmī can never be held to be equal to the Lord, as declared by the **śrutis**. VR draws a line between the characteristics of **Īśvara** and those of the Brahman. **Īśvaratva** is marked by the mere presence of the capacity (**sāmarthya-mātra**) to create the entire universe, sustain it, etc. As contrasted with this the characteristics of the Brahman are the possession of

[^123_5]: ŚTS, pp. 6-22.

***
[[P124]]
111

spontaneous and natural capacity (**akṛtaka-sāmarthya**) and the actual display of that capacity in action. If there is a cosmic function, then it becomes the characteristic of the Brahman. Such a thing is absent in the liberated and ever-liberated souls as understood, which is declared by the Brahmasūtra, 'jagadvyāpāravarjam' etc (IV.4.17). This is what Vedānta Deśika has stated in his commentary on Śrī Rāmānuja's **Śrīvaikuṇṭhagadya** also.[^124_6] The Brahmasūtra '**janmādyasya yataḥ**' (I.1.2) focuses itself on the **Brahmalakṣaṇa**, namely, the entire activity (**Kṛtsna-vyāpāra**)concerning creation etc., of the universe. The word **kṛtsna** must qualify the word Vyāpāra so as to exclude the over-pervasion of the definition to the four-faced Brahmā and others,who are also creators in a sense but not creators of everything, like the Lord. According to ŚTS, the Vyāpāras in toto include also **daṇḍadharatva** (being a chastiser), which is totally absent from Lakṣmī. The entirety of cosmic activity includes creation of those who live in hells (**nārakins**), their maintenance and their individual destruction, which activity can never be traced to Lakṣmī. The chief point of VR is that all cosmic activities such as creation, maintenance, dissolution and

[^124_6]: Śrīvaikuṇṭhagadya Bhāṣya (VGB), p.192.

***
[[P125]]
112

liberation must be held to be common to both the Lord and His consort. But the distinction between the two lies in the latter (Lakṣmī) being free from the creation, maintenance and dissolution of the inmates of various types of hells.

ŚŚ then introduces the next Kārikā of the text 'antaḥ praviśya' etc.,[^125_7] which proves beyond doubt that the Lord becomes the creator of everything through His Saṅkalpa to become 'many', who controls everything from within, forming its soul. The commentator adds that all the Vedāntas such as 'sadeva somya' 'tadaikṣata' and 'so'kāmayata' point to this. Lakṣmī however cannot be such a cause because (1) she cannot afford to be a punisher; (2) she cannot dispense with justice according to the karman of the living beings assuming **nigraha** and **anugraha** as the case may be,and (3) she has nothing to do with the creation of hell etc. She can never be the controller (**niyantṛtva**) looking after or regulating the cosmic activities in their entirety.

ŚŚ then comments upon the next Kārikā, 'Kāraṇatva-prakaraṇa'etc.,[^125_8] examining the status of Lakṣmī's causality

[^125_7]: No. 8
[^125_8]: No. 9

***
[[P126]]
113

more minutely. The **prima facie** view raised is that the presence of Lakṣmī is indicated at the time of creation by such words as '**śraddhā**' and '**svadhā**'. The text 'Āsyesanā' etc., makes it clear that Lakṣmī becomes the controller of all (**niyantṛtva**) which again leads to her being soul of all (as the **antyaryāminī**). Therefore having everything in common with the Lord, Lakṣmī can be accepted as the cause of the entire universe. It is in refutation of this that the Kārikā, '**Kāraṇatvaprakaraṇe**' is introduced by NM. NM opines that Lakṣmī's presence has nowhere been indicated in the context whereas the Lord alone is spoken of as the cause of the universe. Further nowhere is she said to have **cit** and **acit** as Her body, or stated to be controlling everything from within, as the Lord is. The word '**pativat**' has to be read into the verse to make the sense complete, says ŚŚ, because the discussion had earlier been opened with the statement '**patnyāṁ**, **pativadīdrktvam asti neti nirūpyate**' (We are going to discuss whether this kind of similarity between Her Lord and Her consort, actually exists or not).[^126_9]

[^126_9]: no.9

***
[[P127]]
114

Explaining, ŚŚ observes that the words Śraddhā, Svadhā etc., certainly refer to the presence of Lakṣmī but there is no speciality attached to it. In other words Lakṣmī has no direct bearing on personal involvement in the actual creation of the universe like the Lord. The passage "śraddhayā devo devatvamaśnute" (Yaj.Kāṭ. 3-9-12) has been explained by Vedānta Deśika in his **Catuśślokī Bhāṣya** as suggesting the presence of Lakṣmī as a mere attribute to the Lord, merely keeping company with Him and that it is not of any significance (**prādhānya**) in so far as the actual creation etc., are concerned. Further, **ācāryas** like Kūreśa and Parāśara state that the Lord creates the universe as a sportive gesture to please His consort[^127_10] and that she approves of His activities by Her mere glances.[^127_11] [^127_12]

The central idea is this: The Supreme Being has been stated to be the all-soul and all-controller in texts like the **Antaryāmī Brāhmaṇa**. Depending upon the good and bad deeds performed by the **jīva**-s, he controls them

[^127_10]: **Raṅgarājastava** 22,44: 'krīḍasi śrīsamakṣam.'
[^127_11]: **Śrīstava**, v-1: 'yasyā vīkṣya mukham.'
[^127_12]: SGRK. V.1: 'angīkaribhiralokaiḥ'.

***
[[P128]]
from within, through **nigraha** and **anugraha**. Śrī who is His attribute (**Viśeṣaṇa**) also abides within the **jīvas** as their inner controller and in accordance with their **sukṛta** (good deeds) directs them and engages herself in this kind of niyamaṇa which is motivated by pure grace. But never does she control them through **nigraha**. There again, it must be understood that she has the power to show **nigraha**, but she never has a desire to display it.[^128_13] This has to be accepted on the authority of scriptures which speak of Lakṣmī as an embodiment of **anugraha** characterised by motherhood and mediacy. Śrī Deśika while interpreting the word **Svadhā** does not seem to favour the presence of Lakṣmī in the context of causality. Still, while explaining the text '**Anīdavātam**', he first makes out that the Brahman does not depend upon anybody for His existence. Subsequently however, he interprets that Lakṣmī's presence is also to be accepted (**sahayoga**). He concludes, on the basis of a quotation from the **Rāmāyaṇa** that the Lord may be said to depend upon His consort (**Svadhā**) in the sense that He has so much of love for Her. There is no room however to suspect that Lakṣmī thereby becomes the cause of the universe like Her Lord.

[^128_13]: Cf. "**śaktiḥ śriyo'sti neccheti**". [No. 41a]

***
[[P129]]
116

The succeeding Kārikā '**yatsaṅkalpāt**'[^129_14] according to ŚŚ, brings out the role of Lakṣmī as a mere **Viśeṣaṇa** of the Lord who alone is the creator of this universe by His mere **saṅkalpa** and who alone forms the single object of meditation. In all the aspects of the Lord - **Kāraṇatva**, **Upāsyatva**, **Upāyatva** and **prāpyatva**, Śrī becomes His attribute. Her specific function or utility in being the **Viśeṣaṇa** lies in Her bringing out creation etc., involving pure Grace, in receiving the **bhara** (responsibility) of those who surrender to Her, for the full benefit of experiencing **Mokṣa**) and also in conferring upon them that kind of experience through sheer love and affection. It is necessary here to draw a line between the functions of Lord and those of Lakṣmī because, the Lord alone is known as **daṇḍadhara**. Śrī Deśika in the verse '**yatsaṅkalpāt**' etc., of his **Śrīstuti** (no. 4) expresses the same idea.

In all such cases, Lakṣmī must be understood to be included in the personality of the Lord although Her presence is not expressly stated.[^129_15]

Śrīśaileśa refers to an opinion expressed by scholars, that the presence of Lakṣmī is absolutely

[^129_14]: No. 10
[^129_15]: Cf. ŚGRK. v.28.

***
[[P130]]
117

absent in the context of causality, because the Kārikā quoted earlier'**kāraṇatvaprakaraṇe**' etc., itself declares to that effect. ŚŚ answers that the intention of the passage is different. It merely states that Lakṣmī does not appear in that context as an important functionary involving herself personally in the creative activity along with the Lord. The **sahānvaya** of Lakṣmī has to be clearly understood, he warns.

ŚŚ in this context also refutes another view that the **Sahānvaya** of Lakṣmī in the context of causality merely refers to Her **sāmarthya** (capacity). The word **sāmarthya** suggesting (eligibility) cannot convey the complete idea that Lakṣmī can do all that the Lord actually does.

Deśika in his **Tattvatīkā** states that conferring Mokṣa is an exclusive characteristic of the Brahman. If that be so, how can this power be stated to exist in both Lord and His consort? This question is answered on the ground that although both are accepted as the cause of the Universe, performing all the activities regarding creation etc., in toto alone characterises Brahman. On the same analogy, conferring Mokṣa also can be attributed to both although it is the exclusive

***
[[P131]]
118

prerogative of Brahman alone. As a matter of fact NM in the PM itself specifies the exact role of Lakṣmī as the **Viśeṣaṇa** of the Lord.[^131_16]

Although Lakṣmī is the **Viśeṣaṇa**, she can still be construed as being 'related' to the cosmic activities.
Śrīśaileśa, introducing the succeeding two Kārikās[^131_17] observes that the definition of the term 'Brahman' should involve all the cosmic functions, in all their plenitude. Śrī Deśika in his **Tattvatīkā**[^131_18] mentions six characteristics of Brahman, namely, that He is the cause of everything that is created; that He is the object of meditation for those who seek liberation; that He is the one who confers Mokṣa; that He is the chief import of all Vedāntas; that He is the consort of Śrī and that He is the ultimate goal. The statement that '**kāraṇatvādi na śriyaḥ**' merely intends to state that the **Kāraṇatva** mentioned of Brahman as stated above, and as corroborated in the Śrutis and Brahmasūtra is not to be found in the case of Lakṣmī. It does not

[^131_16]: See Kārikā No. 84, 133, 104
[^131_17]: Nos. 23,24
[^131_18]: Cf. TT, p.12. > अत्र सर्वकार्यस्रष्टृत्वादिनी मुमुक्षूपास्यत्व-मोक्षप्रदत्व-ग्रध्यन्तप्रधानवेद्यत्व-श्रीनिवासपरमप्राप्यत्वादिनी च गुणषन्ते।

***
[[P132]]
119

preclude the presence of Lakṣmī as the **Viśeṣaṇa** wherever the Lord is mentioned as the **kāraṇa**, **upāsya**, **upāya** and **prāpya**.

ŚŚ controverts the view of VR that Lakṣmī is not referred to in the **Śrutis** and **Sūtra**, although, he does not accept the characteristics of Brahman in Lakṣmī as involving the creation etc.of the entire universe. Posing various alternatives and quoting the **Tattvatīkā**,the NS, **Stotra Bhāṣya** etc., of Vedānta Deśika and various **Kārikās** of the PM, ŚŚ contends that such an opinion cannot be entertained. The Lord is all the time qualified by Lakṣmī and there cannot be a speck of doubt about it.

ŚŚ also examines in this context the allegations made by VR against NM, that he contradicts the opinion of VD who declared that Lakṣmī also is **jagatkāraṇa** in his NS and other works.

The intention of the passage is entirely different according to ŚŚ. What is meant is, that Lakṣmī is not responsible for all the cosmic activities and that she is incapable of certain functions which the Lord alone is capable of. She has the capacity of carrying on all the cosmic activities but she is not involved in those

***
[[P133]]
120

activities in full. There is no contradiction involved in the statements of NM. As a matter of fact the **Catuśślokī Bhāṣya** of Deśika does not speak of all these cosmic activities with reference to Lakṣmī. It merely speaks of the relationship Lakṣmī has with Her consort in terms of **svāmitva**, **saulabhya**, **phaladatva** and **phalatva**. That she is also the mistress of the universe that she is of easy access, that she confers **mokṣa** and that she also constitutes the **phala** in association with Her Lord, is what is meant by these terms.

ŚŚ also clears the misconception that there is mutual contradiction in the statements made by Deśika in his TT and NS. The TT states that the **Brahmalakṣaṇa** cannot be applied to Lakṣmī and the NS points out that the Divine Couple constitutes the cause of the universe. It is true that there seems to be a contradiction here. But it is only apparent. In the context of TT Deśika merely kept in mind the **causality** of the universe in all its aspects without bringing out the characteristics of Lakṣmī such as motherhood and grace. But in the NS, those facts have been taken into consideration. So there is no contradiction here.

***
[[P134]]
121

ŚŚ then moves on to the next Kārikā[^134_19] emphasising the point that Lakṣmī is characterised by **mātṛtva** and **anugraha** alone and as such, we cannot attribute all cosmic activities to Her. This is what this Kārikā of PM states.

'If Lakṣmī were to be considered the cause of the creation, destruction, punishment etc.of certain lower orders of beings, such as trees and plants, how can one understand her role as the Mediator (**Puruṣakāra**) and Mother?' asks NM.

In the next Kārikā[^134_20] NM states that Lakṣmī is not stated in the **śrutis**, **Brahmasūtra**, **Śrī Bhāṣya**, the three **Gadyas**, **Vedāntasāra**, in the various **stotras** of earlier **ācāryas** and their commentaries as the cause of the Universe **on par** with Her Lord. Even if there are statements in a few **śrutis** that Lakṣmī is the **kāraṇa**, these must be reviewed in the context of Her essential character namely benign grace, and are to be interpreted in a restricted sense.

[^134_19]: No.14
[^134_20]: No.11

***
[[P135]]
122

ŚŚ then takes up the next verse 'Rahasyatraya-sāradeli' etc.,[^135_21] and explains that a few commentaries in the RTS of Vedānta Deśika, make out a case for Lakṣmī's being the **niyantrī** (controller) of the living beings. But, these statements must be clearly analysed, keeping in mind Lakṣmī's essential nature viz., that she has no strictness (**nigraha**) in dealing with the living beings. Her cosmic functions including the conferring of **Mokṣa** must also be carefully understood. E.g., Lakṣmī also confers **Mokṣa** but not in the way her husband does it. The Lord confers **Mokṣa** on a person only after giving up His **nigraha**. That means, He first shows His anger or strictness enforces strict discipline, and only thereafter he sheds anger and confers Mokṣa. But since Lakṣmī is incapable of showing any **nigraha**, statements that she confers **Mokṣa** must be understood in a different way. That is, she shows **anugraha** only and through that, confers Mokṣa. There are therefore such intricacies involved in explaining the role of Lakṣmī in regard to cosmic activities. That is why NM says in the Kārikā 'sancintyaḥ arthab kvacit kvacit' ('The matter has to be,

[^135_21]: No. 12.

***
[[P136]]
123

depending upon the context, reviewed in the proper light.) It has already been pointed out that because Lakṣmī is always associated with Her Lord (**sahayoga**), Lakṣmī stands as an attribute to the Lord who forms the substantive. She cannot grant Mokṣa or become the **kāraṇa** of all cosmic activities like the Lord and whatever is understood about Lakṣmī must be essentially streamlined by Her position as the consort of the Lord.

Liberated souls are said to have extreme similarity (**paramasāmya**) to the Lord. But this has to be understood in a restricted sense only as explained in the Sūtra, '**jagadvyāpāravarjam**' etc. (IV. 4.17). In the case of Lakṣmī also the same principle has to be adopted. She too is said to be 'extremely similar' to the Lord. But still she is of a different nature (Cf. Sāttvata Saṁhitā 'bhinnalakṣaṇam') That she is the consort (**patnī**) of the Lord and that she is dependent (**paratantra**) on Him, are quite well-known. That she is the Mother, full of unmotivated love for the beings and that she acts as a mediator between them and the Lord are also equally well-known. Therefore statements that she is 'totally similar' to the Lord must be understood within the framework of these accepted features. Texts like the **Tattvatīkā** make this point clear. The functions of Lakṣmī

***
[[P137]]
124

in association with her Lord have been clearly brought out by VD in the opening verse of his commentary on the **Catuśślokī**.[^137_22]

Summarising the discussion ŚŚ states that although certain qualities are common among the Divine couple, certain qualities are strikingly different -- **nigraha** and its effects are peculiar to the Lord alone and not to Lakṣmī. Therefore His causal character is underlined by His **nigraha**. This kind of causal character cannot be found in Lakṣmī. Therefore, pointing out a defect in PM's statement '**Kāraṇatvādina śriyaḥ**' does not carry weight. Absence of certain qualities in Lakṣmī does not make Her the Brahman technically, but this does not deny Her the status of being equal to Him in other aspects. This is what is going to be stated later on in the Kārikā, '**śruti-sūtrādisamsiddhaiḥ**' etc.[^137_23]

ŚŚ then introduces the next Kārikā of PM '**prapanna pārijāta ca**' etc.[^137_24] According to this, Vātsya Varada in

[^137_22]: CŚB. '**svaseṣaśeṣārtho niravadhika-nirbādha-mahimā**' etc.
[^137_23]: No. 48.
[^137_24]: No. 13

***
[[P138]]
125

his PP did not mention Lakṣmī as the **Kāraṇa** although she forms the **Viśeṣaṇa** of the Lord. But what he stressed is her role as **Puruṣakāra**, which becomes invariable and essential at the time of **Nyāsa**. In other words, Lakṣmī's status as **Puruṣakāra** becomes significant only when we do **Śaraṇāgati** to the Lord. ŚŚ quotes the relevant passages of the PP to show that **jīvas** who are ever prone to commit offences cannot themselves approach the Lord. It is then that Lakṣmī steps in as the **Puruṣakāra**. Because of her love for the Lord, she easily approaches Him, and increases His affection for the beings at the right moment. His qualities like **jñāna** and **śakti** will be heightened by Her because they will be helpful in protecting the **jīvas**. By Her own personal charm, she will also bring out the charm of the Lord which becomes an object of enjoyment for the devotees. The word '**jagadīśitrī**' of this quotation may mean that Lakṣmī becomes the ruler (**niyantrī**), implying Her causal character also. But here again, as pointed earlier, we have to restrict the meaning of Her causality since she is incapable of showing any **nigraha**.

The next Kārikā, '**Vṛkṣādi**' etc.,[^138_25] has already been referred to by ŚŚ. This verse points out the contradiction

[^138_25]: No. 14

***
[[P139]]
126

in Lakṣmī's being the cause of creation (including those of trees) and destruction involving punishment of offenders in different types of hells on one hand and Her being the **Puruṣakāra** and Mother on the other.

The creation of trees etc. (the lower orders of plant kingdom such as shrubs and creepers) is a kind of punishment inflicted on certain beings. Destruction of certain individuals and the creation of various types of hells, also imply **nigraha** on the part of the creator, whoever it be. It is true that the **nigraha** of the creator, is based upon the sins of the concerned beings. Now the question is, can Lakṣmī ever be imagined even, to be the cause of such creations. The very word '**Vṛkṣādi**' of the Kārikā points out the absurdity of Lakṣmī's being their creator. All this is at what is called the '**Vyaṣṭi**' (individual) level. It may therefore be stated that creation and destruction of beings at the '**Samaṣṭi**' (collective) level does not smack of **nigraha** at all, and hence Lakṣmī's creatorship at that level may be acceptable.

In fact the Kārikā of PM '**śaktiḥ śriyo'stu**' which is going to be explained later on, suggests that Lakṣmī is capable of such an act, which normally results from **nigraha**. But what is emphatically denied is that she has cosmic

***
[[P140]]
127

functions on par with Her husband. This has been emphasised by the **Pramāṇas** and the traditional teachings. This is also in keeping with the essential character of Lakṣmī.

ŚŚ in this context quotes the ŚTS and refutes it on the following issue. VR observes that the **nigraha** of Lakṣmī cannot be construed through what is called **Pratikūla-sṛṣṭi** (creation of trees etc., which is not favoured). According to him creation cannot be treated as being **pratikūla** at all. Creation means 'giving birth', which means associating a soul with a specific body. This also suggests the expansion or spread of knowledge in a corresponding degree. This association with a body and the rise of knowledge cannot be described as unfavourable to the **jīva** concerned, argues VR. But for a person who is intensely desirous of getting liberated, his body may become **pratikūla** at that stage only; but at the time of its production it was not **pratikūla**. On the other hand for one who remained almost like an insentient entity (**acit**) before creation, getting a body itself has to be construed as a **puruṣārtha**.

ŚŚ refutes this view thus - one cannot conclude that association with a body in general which gives rise to

***
[[P141]]
128

knowledge at a particular level itself becomes **pratikūla** to a given being. E.g., the bodies of divine beings and men giving rise to different degrees of knowledge cannot be considered as being unfavourable (**pratikūla**) to the concerned beings. In the case of trees and plants, the bodies they give give very little room for the rise of knowledge in those beings. In such cases, those bodies may be considered as being **pratikūla**. VR's statement concerning a person with an intense desire for liberation is out of context, says ŚŚ. Such a state is possible only in the case of men who are subject to śāstraic injunctions. 'How can one's body become **pratikūla** even in the state of **mumukṣā**?' asks ŚŚ. NM opines that if Lakṣmī were to be accepted as creating these lower orders such as plants and trees, then she may have to be understood as having **nigraha**.

Another objection raised by VR is also stated and answered by ŚŚ in this context. VR argues that since the creation of trees etc. forms a source of misery for the beings concerned it should not even be willed by the Divine Mother. That is against her status as the Mother. Even a remote association with such a saṅkalpa undermines

***
[[P142]]
129

Her benign nature. Her giving the necessary permission to the Lord and even prompting Him to carry on such creations do not fit in Lakṣmī's personality, according to VR.

ŚŚ answers that Lakṣmī cannot be charged with **nigraha** on the ground that she is responsible for the result of creations which ultimately results in the misery of the concerned beings. Any attempt to connect Lakṣmī with cosmic activities - directly or indirectly then becomes unjustified and useless. What is intended by PM is that Lakṣmī, if accepted as creating trees etc. and as bringing in dissolution at the **vyaṣṭi**-level, and also as creating hells with all the tortures, then she has to be admitted as having **nigraha**. What is wrong in it? If she is really doing all that, she must be accepted as having the will (**Saṅkalpa**) to subject certain beings to suffering and agony. If Lakṣmī, who is declared by the Śāstras as not having any **nigraha** at all, is accepted as permitting or prompting the Lord to show **nigraha**, then it becomes a contradiction. Therefore, the only answer that can be given is that Lakṣmī does not herself have any desire to punish anybody, but indirectly such a thing may be attributed to Her. Or it may also be explained that creation of trees, hell, etc. done by the Lord is passively permitted by Lakṣmī, i.e. remaining

***
[[P143]]
130

'indifferent' (**upekṣā**) on such occasions. 'Indifference' means remaining neutral to a thing without showing interest or disinterest. Therefore if Lakṣmī remains as a passive spectator, it cannot be construed as an act of **nigraha**.

Another argument of VR's also discounted by ŚŚ. According to VR, Lakṣmī's non-involvement as creator in the cosmic activities should be understood only with reference to **vyaṣṭi-sṛṣṭi** i.e., individual creation. But on the collective side, since all the **jīvas** before creation remain 'dormant' as in deep sleep, their creation or even dissolution does not indicate her **pratikūlatva** (in as much as they are all **insensitive** to any suffering). This however should not make us forget Her causal character because all the 'capacity' therefor is latent in Her, argues VR.

ŚŚ criticises this view on the following lines: Nowhere has NM denied Lakṣmī's agency - either for the **vyaṣṭi-sṛṣṭi** or **samaṣṭi-sṛṣṭi** or **samaṣṭi-saṁhāra**. Nor has he stated anywhere that Lakṣmī does not have the capacity to do so. What all he stresses is that she does not have 'that kind of causal character' which is present in the Lord. In the light of this all objections raised earlier are set aside, points out ŚŚ.

***
[[P144]]
131

ŚŚ also answers a question as to how the terms '**sarvaloka-maheśvarī**' (supreme ruler of all the worlds) and **niyantrī** (controller) which point to her **niyantṛtva**, fail to show her as the cause of the entire universe. He states that Deśika had already indicated the method of interpreting such expressions in his **Gadyādhikāra**. Even Rāvaṇa the vilest sinner had been treated by the Divine Mother like a lunatic son (उन्मादपुत्र इव श्वत्, p.134) and was kindly advised to make friends with Rāma, who is merciful to all who surrender to Him. She taught him the greatest secret that surrendering to Rāma was open to all. But anyway he did not heed to her advice and ruined himself. Deśika suggests that by becoming the innermost controller of all the beings out of her unconditioned affection and love, the Divine Mother exercises her control (**niyamana**) by tendering timely advice. That is why she is referred to as **niyantrī** and **Maheśvarī**.

The succeeding Kārikā '**ajnāta-nigrahāyasca**' etc.,[^144_26] is introduced by Śrīśaileśa with the **prima facie** view that Lakṣmī should be accepted as having **nigraha** like the Lord because terms like **niyantrī** and **Maheśvarī** are in support. Further, the Lord also is known for His compassion, unmotivated friendship etc. for the beings,

[^144_26]: No. 16

***
[[P145]]
132

although He is accepted on all hands to be a strict disciplinarian. Why not Lakṣmī be accepted in the same way, (i.e. as having both the aspects) is the contention of the Pūrvapakṣin.
