In answer ŚŚ states that Lakṣmī is known to be full of compassion with no trace of **nigraha**. 'Such being the case if Lakṣmī is represented to have **nigraha** also like the Lord, what distinction is drawn from the lord?' retorts Śrīśaileśa. In so far as the auspicious qualities are concerned, they are common between Lord and His consort. But the scriptures assert that Lord is the Father of the creation,the ruler of all, chastiser of the wicked etc. Therefore, showing **nigraha** becomes a natural trait of the Lord. When we speak of His filial qualities such as compassion, parental love and universal friendship, we must take care that the **nigraha**-element in Him is not overlooked. But in the case of the Divine Mother the very same scriptures assert Her qualities of unmotivated grace and spontaneous mediatorship. So in the case of Lakṣmī, the quality which make Her distinct from the Lord is **Puruṣakāratva**. The **Sāttvata Saṁhitā** passage '**tadrūpamiśraṁ bhinna-lakṣaṇam**' and the statements of ācāryas like Deśika must all be explained keeping this

***
[[P146]]
133

particular quality of Lakṣmī in mind. Therefore if Lakṣmī also were to be accepted as punishing the wicked through **nigraha**, there will not be any difference between Her and the Lord. So the upshot of this discussion is that in as much as **nigraha** and the consequent **niyamana** are absent in Lakṣmī, she cannot form the cause of the entire universe like Her husband. Her being the cause of the universe through **anugraha**, is of course reasonable since there is no contradiction of scriptural texts.

The next Kārikā'**Yasmāddevyāḥ**' etc.[^146_27] confirms this position of Lakṣmī (that she has no **nigraha** in her) with reference to Deśika's commentary on the **Śaraṇāgati-gadya** (ŚG). The Kārikā states that in as much as Lakṣmī has no '**taste**' for **nigraha** at all, she is referred to by Rāmānuja in his **Śaraṇāgati-gadya** as **niravadyā** (the faultless one). This has been corroborated by Deśika himself.

ŚŚ in his commentary on this verse quotes profusely from Deśika's Bhāṣya on Rāmānuja's ŚG and confirms that Lakṣmī is totally incapable of getting angry. Deśika observes that normally speaking,women, in spite of their loyalty and love to their husbands, still occasionally exhibit bad temper, a sort of aversion to their opinion, short-

[^146_27]: No.17

***
[[P147]]
134

sightedness, hasty action, hard-heartedness and a tendency to show **nigraha**. That being the case, how can anybody with no other hope of protection approach Lakṣmī wholeheartedly? That is why Śrī Rāmānuja calls Lakṣmī **niravadyā** (the blemishless or spotless one). As for the general statement of women being hard-hearted, fickle-minded etc. that may be applicable only to humans who are conditioned by their own Karma. This cannot therefore be applied to Lakṣmī. In fact the **Lakṣmī Tantra**,**Rāmāyaṇa** and other texts declare that Lakṣmī is free from all such defects. Sītā's warning to Rāvaṇa (Sundarakāṇḍa, 27-20) that she does not reduce Him to ashes by Her power since she does not have the sanction of her Lord makes it clear that even against worst sinners she is not inclined to show Her anger.

In the succeeding four Kārikās ŚŚ raises the **Pūrvapakṣa** that if Lakṣmī is never known to have **nigraha**, how can epithets like '**daitya dānava mardinī**' (one who destroys daityas and dānavas) be applied to Her? The answer is that such epithets are derived from the work Lakṣmī does through Durgā and other ferocious Goddesses. As a matter of fact that ferocity is not due to the **saṅkalpa** of Lakṣmī at all. On the contrary wherever those Goddesses (other[^147_28]

[^147_28]: Nos. 18,19,20,21.

***
[[P148]]
135

than Lakṣmī) are stated to show compassion, it has to be traced to Lakṣmī's **Saṅkalpa**. Another question is that if Lakṣmī is said to depend upon the **karman** of certain beings when punishing them through her aspects like Durgā and Kālī, what distinction could be drawn between herself and the Lord? Because He too is known to take into account the **karman** of the beings whom He punishes. The line of difference between the Lord and Lakṣmī is that the Lord being the father of the living beings naturally tries to chastise them whenever necessary. Lakṣmī, on the contrary acts as the Mediator between them, being motivated by Her Motherly status. The word **kānta-prasāda**[^148_29] clearly shows the remarkable and overwhelming grace of Lakṣmī, which rules out even a trace of **nigraha** in Her. This is also clear from the introductory portion of Deśika's commentary on the **Catuśślokī**. The point that has been established there is that no causality of Lakṣmī can be attributed with reference to each and every cosmic activity, involving **nigraha**. There is no dispute in so far as Her causal character streamlined by **anugraha** is concerned.

[^148_29]: Vide. CŚ. V.3.
'aravinda locana-manaḥ-kāntāprasādādṛte'.

***
[[P149]]
136

The following five and a half Kārikās[^149_30] (of which the first one is actually a quotation from Deśika's TT) explain as to why Lakṣmī cannot be accepted as the agent of all cosmic activities involving **nigraha**. In fact such a proposition will be the contingency when one takes into consideration the statement of Deśika in Nyāya Siddhāñjana that there is **sāmya** between the Lord and His consort.

NM states that as Deśika pointed out in his TT, the opening verse of Rāmānuja's **Śrībhāṣya** mentioned six characteristics of Brahman.[^149_31] [^149_32] These qualities, like **Brahmatva** and **Śrīpatitva** are found only in the Lord but not in Lakṣmī. If Lakṣmī is the **Viśeṣaṇa** of the Lord she would participate in His **nigraha** also. To deny such a contingency NM says that for the pleasure of His consort the Lord will be carrying on the cosmic functions in a sportive way. Deśika in his commentary on the CŚ[^149_33] has already stated that because the whole thing is conceived as a divine sport, Lakṣmī may also be said to have a role in it, through indirect relationship.

[^149_30]: Nos. 22,23,24,25,26,27 ab
[^149_31]: " अखिलभुवन ... "
[^149_32]: These points have already been mentioned before; see p.15 above.
[^149_33]: CŚB. p.19.

***
[[P150]]
137

Explaining these verses ŚŚ points out that the word **samastakārya-hetutvaṁ**, agency regarding individual destruction, creation of hell etc. are unique to the Lord and are absent in Lakṣmī. The next expression **mumukṣubhiḥ upāsyatā** also applies to the Lord alone, because being the object of meditation for attaining the Bliss of the full experience of Brahman, caused by the annihilation of all association with material Nature (**prakṛti**), the latent impressions of beginningless karma caused by **avidyā**, which are in turn generated by a series of **nigrahas** consequent to the violation of the Lord's commands from time immemorial. Only the Brahman can be such an object of meditation. Likewise the power to confer Mokṣa after shedding all **nigraha** lies only with the Brahman. Being the chief object or import (**pradhāna-pratipādyatā**) of the Upaniṣads is also applicable to Brahman alone. Though Lakṣmī is His attribute, still the substantive namely the Lord, is relatively more important. There can be no dispute regarding Lakṣmī's having characteristics where the element of **nigraha** is absent, but she can never acquire those attributes which characterise the essential nature of Brahman. Summarising the discussion in four mnemonic verses ŚŚ states that being an attribute of Lord Viṣṇu

***
[[P151]]
138

and having the entire universe as Her body by virtue of Her being the **śeṣiṇī** along with Her consort, Lakṣmī becomes the agent, the source of Bliss, the object of meditation for attaining that bliss, and the chief goal of attainment. Even regarding **nigraha** she has the capacity (**sāmarthya**); she can be the **niyantrī** (controller of all the activities of the virtuous people). She is also all-pervasive and the universal ruler like Him. Her being subordinate to Him however is by mutual will and understanding. These are the aspects of Lakṣmī mentioned by NM in the above Kārikās.

As for the argument that Deśika's statement of **Sāmya** (equality) between the Lord and His consort made in his **Nyāyasiddhāñjana** should be taken to its logical conclusions regarding Lakṣmī's causality, ŚŚ points out that **Sāmya** must be understood in its own limited sense. Deśika himself in his TT clarifies that this **Sāmya** cannot be total and absolute. Lakṣmī is similar to the Lord in all features and characteristics excepting those essential features which make the Lord the 'Brahman'.

The discussion then turns to a more important question discussed in the **Nyāyasiddhāñjana**, namely whether Lakṣmī belongs to the category of the **jīvas** or

***
[[P152]]
139

not. The view of the **Pūrvapakṣin** is that the Nyāyasiddhāñjana mentions eight characteristics of the **jīva** and four of the Lord. On an impartial observation Lakṣmī is found to possess the characteristics of **jīva** but not of **Īśvara**. The seven Kārikās that follow summarise this discussion.[^152_34]

The definition of **Īśvaratva** according to NS is: '**svajñāna-svetara-samastadravyaśarīrakatvam**' ('possessing everything other than Himself and His knowledge, as the body').[^152_35] This cannot be applied to Lakṣmī at all. The definition that can be applied to Her is '**śeṣatve sati boddhṛtvam**', ('being the possessor of knowledge while being subordinate to the Lord'). The **Pūrvapakṣin** asks for an impartial examination of the characteristics of **jīva** and **Īśvara** mentioned by Deśika in his **Paramatabhaṅga** also to find out whose qualities Lakṣmī shares.The characteristics of **jīva** mentioned there in are eight-fold **ādheyatva** (being supported), **vidheyatva** (being controlled), **śeṣatva** (being subordinate) and **aṇutva** (being atomic in

[^152_34]: Nos. 29,30,31,32,33 ab
[^152_35]: NS., p.271. See the footnote there for the dala-prayojana of the term 'sva' of this definition.

***
[[P153]]
140

size), each one of which is to be taken severally qualifying **cetanatvam** (being conscious) and **ahaṁtvam** (having the cognition of 'I').

The characteristics of the Lord are four-fold namely, **mumukṣu-upāsyatā** (being the object of meditation by those who are desirous of liberation), **mokṣa-pradatva** (bestowership of emancipation), **prāpyatva** (being the final goal) and **ananyādhāratā** (not having anybody else as His support).

It will be quite clear from this that Lakṣmī who forms the body of the Lord depends upon Him. The **Lakṣmī-sahasranāma-stotra** mentions '**amṛtadhārā**' as one of the names of Lakṣmī. The explanation for this word is that Lakṣmī is dependent on the Lord who is called **amṛta**. The same stotra also mentions '**nirāśrayā**' as yet another name of Lakṣmī. Vedānta Deśika states that this word has to be interpreted like Her another name '**nissaṅkalpā**', without contradicting statements like '**śrayate ca paraṁ padam**' mentioned in the Āgamas (She resorts to the Supreme Brahman (**paramaṁ padam**) or the highest abode). So the word **nirāśrayā** cannot mean, 'one who stands alone without anybody's support'. It may mean 'one who has no support

***
[[P154]]
141

other than the Lord'. Likewise the word '**nissaṅkalpā**' (lit, one who has no will) also has to be explained as 'one who has no will independent of the Lord's'.

The NŚ clearly mentions Lakṣmī as the body of the Lord[^154_36] in the following way: Lakṣmī can be construed as a different state of existence of the Lord, like the **Vyūhas** since everything in creation has the Lord as its soul. The manifestation of Lakṣmī should also be taken as a different of state of existence of the Lord Himself motivated by either by the desire of Lakṣmī or by that of the Lord. Śrī Kṛṣṇa Tātārya, author of the commentary **Ratnapeṭikā** is also quoted by ŚŚ in support.[^154_37]

The conclusion arrived at is that Lakṣmī and Nārāyaṇa alone constitute the Divine Couple and they are all-pervasive by nature. Being unlimited in **Svarūpa**, He is to be seen in all the **jīvas**, but this cannot be applied to Lakṣmī.

In the earlier portion of NŚ it was stated that Lakṣmī does not possess the characteristics of Brahman.

[^154_36]: NS, p.271: " तद्देहभूतं लक्षणं तु " ... etc.
[^154_37]: Ibid., p.363.

***
[[P155]]
142

That Lakṣmī does not have any **nigraha** in her is also a point in this direction. This however, does not mean that Lakṣmī is a **jīva**. The latter portion of NŚ establishes this point by positing **sāmya** between the Lord and Lakṣmī. Therefore one has to be careful in arriving at the intention of NŚ regarding the exact status of Lakṣmī. What Deśika exactly intends is that Lakṣmī is coeval with the Lord in all aspects excepting in her having **nigraha** and in Her not forming the cause of all aspects of creation. In every other feature she is supreme like the Lord Himself.

The succeeding Kārikā[^155_38] of NM points out that according to some critics Śrī also becomes the import of the word 'Brahman'[^155_39] because according to them Brahman is characterised as Truth, Knowledge and Infinity (cf. '**satyaṁ jñānam, anantaṁ Brahma**'). NM observes that this view cannot be correct.
NM in the latter portion of the Kārikā clarifies this point regarding Lakṣmī's position.[^155_40] This is the final ascertained opinion: The characteristic of 'Brahman' namely causality regarding the universe applies only to the Lord

[^155_38]: No. 36.
[^155_39]: See ŚTS, p.35
[^155_40]: No. 47,48

***
[[P156]]
143

and not to both. Those features which are said to be common to the couple are not the characteristics of Brahman. The **sāmya** between Lakṣmī and the Lord has been explained in the NŚ without infringing upon the characteristics of Brahman which are clearly enunciated in the **Śrutis**, **Upaniṣads**, **Brahmasūtra** and other texts.

What follows is a criticism made by ŚŚ of certain statements made by VR in his ŚTS. The problem is one of syntactical interpretation and not of any philosophical significance.[^156_41] VR interprets VD's CŚB statements regarding **Paramasāmya** between the ever-liberated souls and the Lord which does not mean total identity, a point accepted on all hands (cf.'jagadvyāpāravarjam,' IV.4.17). Likewise the statement of **sāmya** made between Lakṣmī and the Lord also has to be accepted with due reservations. The expressions '**yathā**' and '**tathā**' which are relative indeclinables, must bring out similarity in all aspects, argues VR.[^156_42]

Pointing out the correct interpretation of this passage, ŚŚ states that although the liberated souls

[^156_41]: See ŚTS, p.35.
[^156_42]: Found in CŚB.,p.12.

***
[[P157]]
144

are said to be extremely similar to the Lord in terms of **jñāna** and **ānanda**, still, they differ from Him by virtue of their dependence and subordination. That they cannot be the chastisers of the wicked (**daṇḍadhara**) is the point of dissimilarity (**Vaiṣamya**). Likewise, though Lakṣmī is also said to be similar to the Lord in being the parent, **śeṣiṇī**, the goal, all-pervasive and so on, still she differs from Him by virtue of Her womanhood, loyalty to Him etc. In Her case also the point of dissimilarity (**vaiṣamya**) is that she cannot be a punisher of the wicked (**daṇḍadhara**). ŚŚ likewise finds fault with another statement of ŚTS (p.35) regarding the interpretation of a passage of Deśika.[^157_43] The actual point is that there cannot be any comparison between the liberated souls and Lakṣmī. The liberated souls have no place in the context of causality whereas Lakṣmī has such a privilege. But still Lakṣmī is present as a **viśeṣaṇa** (attribute) which is accepted in all the scriptures. Parāśara's verse '**svarūpaṁ svātantryam**' etc. also corroborates this view.[^157_44]

Another statement of ŚTS (p.35) that 'Lakṣmī cannot share the qualities of the Brahman and that she possesses the

[^157_43]: CŚB., p.12.
[^157_44]: ŚGRK, śl.28.

***
[[P158]]
145

qualities of **Īśvara** because the form of the couple with Him' is also criticised by ŚŚ. ŚŚ obviously make a distinction between **mukhyeśvaratva** (brahmatva) and **Īśvaratva** bringing Lakṣmī under the second category. Such a classification is not warranted by any **pramāṇa**, says ŚŚ. In fact NM whom ŚŚ calls '**asmadācārya**' (our preceptor) never interprets Deśika in the wrong light. As a matter of fact NM does not attribute all cosmic activities to Lakṣmī although he speaks of other characteristics which are common between them, in the beginning, middle and end of the present text PM. NM has consistently stated that Lakṣmī does not have all the cosmic activities in the light of Deśika's statement '**atyantasāmyamapi asyāḥ**' etc. The objection raised in ŚTS (p.36) that the definition of **Īśvara** given in the NŚ (**svijñāna-svetara-dravyaśarīrakatvam**) becomes the definition of **Pati** (Brahman) but not of **Īśvara**, is also subjected to criticism by ŚŚ. As a matter of fact VR who accepts Deśika's view,points out that Lakṣmī is **Vibhu**. He is against the view that Lakṣmī is **aṇu**. Then, what is the implication of this definition of **Īśvara**? According to the definition everything other than the Lord and His knowledge forms His body. So Lakṣmī also automatically becomes His **śarīra**. In other words Lakṣmī is not **Vyāpaka** like the Lord. Therefore the definition

***
[[P159]]
146

given to both 'Pati' and 'Patnī' viz., '**vyāpakatve sati cetanatvam**' becomes contradicted, because only Pati is **Vyāpaka** and not the **Patnī**. Then it has to be replied by VR, that although Vibhutva of Lakṣmī is Deśika's **Siddhānta**-view, the definition of **Īśvara** given by him in the NŚ has been made from the view-point of these who believe that Lakṣmī is **aṇu**. Then, by the same token, argues ŚŚ, that even according to NM, the definition of **Īśvara** given by VD has been given from the viewpoint of those who do not believe in the **Īśvaratva** of Lakṣmī.

The intention of ŚŚ is to show that NM's understanding of VD's position is correct and that pointing out defects in his standpoint by VR is not reasonable.

ŚŚ continuing his criticism of ŚTS (p.36) regarding the 'definition of definition' and its application to the definition of **Īśvara** as understood by NM, observes as follows: The definition of **Īśvara** '**Vyāpakatve sati cetanatvam**', is applicable to both the Lord and His consort. The real problem arises only when we say that Lakṣmī has the contradictory qualities of both **Īśvara** and **anīśvara** in Her. But there is no contradiction at all according to ŚŚ because of the definition of **Īśvara** given in the NŚ which is meant to preclude Brahmā, Rudra

***
[[P160]]
147

and other divine beings from the scope of Lordship because they too come into the picture staking their claims for Lordship. The intention of the passage is not to discuss the status of Lakṣmī either as belonging to the category of **Īśvara** or that of **anīśvara**. As a matter of fact a more detailed discussion on Lakṣmī as **Īśvara** has to be made, and it was taken up by Deśika at a later stage of the NŚ through such passages as '**śriyā saha tu dāmpatyam**' etc.

ŚŚ contends further that there is no room for **anīśvaratva** in Lakṣmī as is clear from NM's declaration '**siddhaṁ tadubhayecchātaḥ sarvaiśvaryasṛuteḥ dvayoḥ**'. According to NM both the Lord and His consort are declared by the **Śrutis** to be the Lords of the entire universe. But how can both be accepted as rulers at the same time? The answer is that 'their by mutual will' is responsible for such a status. ŚŚ in this context answers a number of criticisms levelled by ŚTS against NM's arguments mainly regarding the loopholes in the definition of **Īśvara**. ŚŚ states that a definition can be two-fold: general and special. The definition '**Vyāpakatve sati cetanutvam**' etc., is a common definition

***
[[P161]]
148

of **Īśvara** whereas '**svajñāna-svetara-dravya-śarīratvam**' is special, concludes ŚŚ.

ŚŚ points out a number of instances from the PM to show that according to NM, as according to Deśika, Lakṣmī is **Īśvarī**. Therefore, trying to refute his view by pointing out the presence or absence of definitions of **jīva** and **Īśvara** in Lakṣmī by VR is beside the point and unwarranted. At the beginning of the NŚ, **sāmya** has been posited between Lord and His consort for which criticism has been raised regarding Lakṣmī's sharing the characteristics of the Brahman. Also, the definition of **Īśvara** given in the NŚ and the presence and absence of the definition of **jīva** and **Īśvara** in Lakṣmī given in Deśika's **Paramata Bhaṅga** are also explained. NM in the succeeding Kārikā '**ata eva anantapadaṁ vyāvṛttiḥ**'[^161_45] points out the absence of Brahman's **Svarūpa Lakṣaṇa** from Lakṣmī as given in the TT. ŚŚ points out that according to Rāmānuja's commentary on '**janmādyasya yataḥ**', (Br.Sū. I.1.2) the word **ananta** indicates the 'absence of limit' in the **Svarūpa** of the Lord from the viewpoint of time, space and other objects. Since the **Svarūpa** of the Lord

[^161_45]: अत एवानन्तपदं व्याख्याद्येत्यादि। etc. (No. 37)

***
[[P162]]
149

is always qualified, it also becomes infinite (**ananta**). According to ŚŚ this statement implies that the **Svarūpa** and **guṇas** of all the eternal beings are removed from the scope of Brahman because they are all limited. But in the case of Lakṣmī, although Her **Svarūpa** is unexcelled, she becomes limited by virtue of Her **Pāratantrya** (dependency on the Lord). This indicates further that even regarding causality, Lakṣmī is excelled by the Lord and thus She stands on a different footing. The **Pāratantrya** of the **jīvas** is dependent on the will of the Lord. But the **Pāratantrya** of Lakṣmī is dependent on the will of both Herself and the Lord. This does not indicate that Lakṣmī is a **jīva**. Nor does it undermine Her Lordship. What is undisputed is that because Lakṣmī happens to be the consort of the Lord, the mediator between man and God, and the Mother of the universe, she has no cosmic activity which involves **nigraha**. Since Lakṣmī thus becomes limited in Her **guṇa** and **Svarūpa**, lacking as she is in **svātantrya** and **nigraha**, she does not have **Brahmatva** in Her. The word 'Brahman' applies only to the Lord because the full implication of **Bṛhatva** ('bigness') from the viewpoint of **Svarūpa** and **guṇa** is found only in Him.

***
[[P163]]
150

The succeeding Kārikā[^163_146] points out another reason why Lakṣmī cannot be included in the meaning of the word 'Brahman'. The Supreme Brahman is alone **ananta**, from the viewpoint of **guṇas** and **anavadhika-atiśaya** (limitless excellence) and from the viewpoint of **Svarūpa**. This Brahman alone described as the goal (**prāpya**) in the scriptures, says NM in this Kārikā.[^163_47]

ŚŚ quotes several passages from the Śrī Bhāṣya and the Śrutaprakāśikā to justify this point. The implication is that Lakṣmī does not come into the picture in so far as the definition of the term 'Brahman' is concerned. ŚŚ then takes up statements found in the ŚTŚ which imply a controversy on the meaning of the term 'Brahman' (whether Lakṣmī is included in Brahmatva or not), a contradiction which according to ŚŚ does not really exist. NM is purported to have, in his PM, declared and accepted Lakṣmī also as meaning of the word Brahman. This according to ŚŚ, is a baseless allegation. All the ācāryas like Bhāṣyakāra and Vedānta Deśika are unanimous in accepting Lord Puruṣottama alone as the meaning of the word 'Brahman', and Lakṣmī does not come into the picture anywhere. 

[^163_146]: No. 38
[^163_47]: "तदनन्तं ब्रह्म वेद्यं तत् प्राप्यश्चेति श्रवणात्।।" [Ibid.]

***
[[P164]]
151

A number of passages from the TT and the Gadya Bhāṣya of Vedānta Deśika are quoted in support. The **Pāratantrya** of Lakṣmī is not adventitious but natural for Her. In the same way the **svātantrya** of the Lord is natural but not adventitious. Like the sun becoming unexcelled by virtue of the brilliance of his radiance, the Lord also becomes unexcelled by virtue of His association with Lakṣmī of excellent virtues.

That is to say that if Lakṣmī is unexcelled even by Her Lord, it still adds to the glory of the Lord as unexcelled and unequalled (**niḥsamābhyadhika**). On the analogy of Prabhā we can also conclude that the dependency and subordinate character of Lakṣmī are natural to Lakṣmī since she is the Patnī of the Lord; and because it is dependent upon Her eternal will, her dependency on the Lord also becomes eternal. The question of **sāmya** between the Lord and Lakṣmī has already been discussed. Nobody who really understands Deśika would argue that the dependency of Lakṣmī is adventitious (**aupādhika**) and that Her independence is natural. Deśika's **Bhāṣya** on Yāmuna's **Stotraratna** makes this point clear. In other words, the **Pāratantrya** etc., of Lakṣmī are the result of mutual will which is eternal and as such, they are natural (**svābhāvika**). The word '**svābhāvika**' means '**Yāvadātmabhāvitva**',

***
[[P165]]
152

lasting as long as the soul lasts, which means, 'eternal'
The RTS also establishes that the **Pāratantrya** of Lakṣmī is eternal.[^165_48]

ŚŚ also criticises the view of ŚTS that the Lord and Lakṣmī have total similarity regarding their **Svarūpa**, **sthiti** and **pravṛtti** and that both have the same kind of **Lordship**. As already explained on several occasions, Lakṣmī's independence is marked by dependence on the Lord's will. The Lord alone can be described as the really independent Supreme Being by whose **Saṅkalpa** alone Lakṣmī has attained her status. An analysis of Deśika's **Gadyabhāṣya**, **TT** and NM's PM establishes this point beyond doubt. ŚŚ also quotes a number of passages from the stotras of Yāmuna, **Śrīvatsāṅka** and Parāśara Bhaṭṭa in support of this view.

The next Kārikā continues the question of **Sāmānādhi-kāraṇya** (co-ordinate predication) between Lakṣmī and other objects, driving home the point that though all-pervasive and eternal, she is only 'limited' (**paricchinnā**) from the viewpoint of **guṇas**.[^165_49]

[^165_48]: See Appendix for the text of PM with Maṇidīpikā, p.84 ff.
[^165_49]: No. 39

***
[[P166]]
153

Lakṣmī like the Lord becomes **sarvaśeṣiṇī**. Therefore Coordinate Predication e.g., '**artho viṣṇuh iyaṁ vāṇī**' (the Lord is the meaning and Śrī is the speech) becomes possible.

ŚŚ explains that the word '**sarvaśeṣitayā**' of the Kārikā must be interpreted as **sarvadhārakatayā** ('supporting everything') but not as '**sarva niyantṛtayā**' (controlling everything) because Lakṣmī cannot be said to control either through **nigraha** or **anugraha**. Because Lakṣmī supports both **cit** and **acit** and has them as Her modes, she can be referred to with Coordinate Predication involving all entities other than the Lord. Though she is thus **nitya** (eternal) and **vibhu** (all-pervasive) she cannot become the connotation of the word **ananta** (infinity). ŚŚ explains that although by her **Svarūpa** and **Vibhūti** Lakṣmī has no limitation, still what is called as **guṇaparyāparyanta** ('limitation from the view point of attributes) is possible in the case of Lakṣmī. That is what is meant by the expression '**paricchinnaiva vastutaḥ**' in the Kārikā.

The next Kārikā[^166_50] continues the argument and states that compared to the Lord, Lakṣmī is inferior from

[^166_50]: No. 40.

***
[[P167]]
154

the viewpoint of qualities (**guṇa**) and activities (**vyāpāra**).

NM states that although Lakṣmī is all-pervasive, she does not become the creator. Explaining this, ŚŚ says that becoming all-pervasive is not the criterion of creatorship. If it were so, Time which is all pervasive, should also be accepted as the creator, which of course, is absurd. Creatorship means, 'being the agent of creation' which again means, 'being the locus of volition which is favourable for creation'. Time being insentient, cannot be the creator. Posing different alternatives ŚŚ points out that being an 'all-pervasive conscious being' (**vibhu-cetana**) cannot be the qualification required of a creator. That Lakṣmī is inferior to the Lord from the viewpoint of **Vyāpāra** (activity) may also be understood from a different point of view. **Vyāpāra** here means **nigraha-vyāpāra** ('activity involving **nigraha**'), which is absent in Lakṣmī. ŚŚ contends that being atomic in size also does not preclude a conscious being from becoming a creator, e.g., Brahmā and others who are[^167_51]

[^167_51]: Brahmā, Indra and others are all **jīvas** and hence atomic in size.

***
[[P168]]
155

mentioned in our scriptures as creators in different Kalpas.

The succeeding Kārikā '**śaktiḥ śriyo'stu**'[^168_52] again makes it clear that Coordinate Predication between Lakṣmī and the world is possible because (1) she has the entire universe as Her mode (**prakāra**), (2) she becomes the controller (**niyantrī**) of all and also because (3) she has the capacity to show **nigraha** although she never entertains such a will.

Explaining the verse,[^168_53] ŚŚ points out that **niyantṛtva** can be three-fold -- through grace, through strictness, and through both. Therefore even if one aspect is present one can become the Controller and this is possible in the case of Lakṣmī, i.e. she can control people through Her grace and benevolence. As a matter of fact this quality has been highlighted in the words of Sītā to Rāvaṇa.[^168_54] That she is completely free from cruelty is also clear from another expression of the Rāmāyaṇa.[^168_55]

[^168_52]: No. 41
[^168_53]: " प्रसादः कोप शान्तिः सा देव्या नास्तीति भाषितम्।"(p.35)
[^168_54]: See Su.Kā.27.20. > न त्वां कुर्मि दशग्रीव भस्म भर्त्सार्हतेजसा।।
[^168_55]: Ibid. 38.41. > आनृशंस्यं परो धर्मः त्वत्त एव मया श्रुतः।।

***
[[P169]]
156

So it is clear that Lakṣmī has a desire to show **anugraha** and also the 'capacity' to show **nigraha**. From both these viewpoints we can call her **niyantrī** on the basis of which coordinate-predication can be made in a primary sense without twisting the text. This view is supported by tradition and many **Pramāṇas** such as '**ubhayādhiṣṭhānaṁ ca ekaṁ śeṣitvam**',[^156_56] '**mukārastu tayor dāsaḥ**' etc.[^156_57]

The following Kārikā[^156_58] brings out the same point in clearer terms. According to ŚŚ, Lakṣmī also becomes ruler (**Īśvarī**) of the universe on the only ground of having both the **Vibhūtis** (**nitya** and **līlā**) under Her control. On this issue she is on par with the Lord. But in so far as **hetutva**, **upāsyatā**, etc. are concerned they apply only to the Brahman but not to Lakṣmī who is only an attribute of the Brahman. The point to be noted is that according to ŚŚ, Lakṣmī cannot become the object of meditation exactly in the manner in which Lord becomes the object of meditation. One prays to the Lord thus -

[^156_56]: Sāgārtha Saṁkṣepa
[^156_57]: Kāṭha Śruti.
[^156_58]: No. 42

***
[[P170]]
157

'O Lord, Give me a full experience of your self'. ŚŚ contends that although Lakṣmī too becomes an object of meditation, here, because she is an attribute of the Brahman, still she merely helps to remove the **nigraha** of the Lord and as such, does not become the direct object of meditation.

The next Kārikā[^170_59] clarifies that the qualities which are stated to be common between the Lord and His consort cannot be taken as the characteristics of the Brahman.

ŚŚ explains that the characteristics of Brahman such as being the cause of the creation etc. of the universe exist only in that person, who has **Brahmatva**. So they cannot be found in Lakṣmī. As for the other qualities like being the ruler of the two **vibhūtis** they can be applied to Lakṣmī also. For this reason, these qualities cannot constitute the characteristics of Brahman. VD has mentioned such common qualities in his texts like the NS. Then what about the passage, '**anīdavataṁ svadhayā tadekaṁ**' (Ṛg Veda X.129.2), which suggests the existence of Prāṇa

[^170_59]: No. 44

***
[[P171]]
158

(vital breath) whose effect is referred to by the word **ānit** at the time of cosmic dissolution? It also speaks of **Svadhā** to which the Supreme Brahman owes his own existence.

The commentator explains that no vital breath (**mukhya-prāṇa**) is referred to here. Prior to creation Brahman alone is said to have existed. The contention of the **Pūrvapakṣin** is that **Śreṣṭhaḥ prāṇaḥ** which is said to have existed prior to creation must be accepted as a product (**kārya**), not like the element (Ether). it must be explained on the analogy of souls (**ātman**).

ŚŚ explains that even for the **Pūrvapakṣin**, Lakṣmī cannot form the cause of the entire universe, since Brahman alone existed prior to creation to the exclusion of every other being. The question of Lakṣmī's causality does not arise at all.

The succeeding four Kārikās[^171_60] confirm the same view,referring to Deśika's commentary on the **Catuśślokī**. The point to be kept in mind is that Lakṣmī cannot be cause of the universe on par with Her Lord.

In his commentary on the CŚ, Deśika takes up the word **Svadhā** and explains it in four different ways.

[^171_60]: Nos. 43,44,45. 46.

***
[[P172]]
159

On any ground, the chief causal character of the Lord is firmly established.

(1) The word **svadhā** in some texts, is used as a synonym for Lakṣmī. Still it cannot be argued that the existence of Brahman is dependent on **Svadhā**, namely Lakṣmī. Brahman depends upon his own self for His existence and this has been accepted and declared so by many **Śrutis**. Hence the word **Svadhā** can be explained as '**svasmin dhīyate**' which means the existence of the Lord which depends upon His own person (**Svasmin**).

(2) Alternately, the word **svadhā** can also be explained as '**svakīyaṁ viśvadhāraṇaṁ**' which means 'the Lord's own capacity to support the entire universe'.[^172_61] This kind of interpretation has been given by Śrī Rāmānuja also in His commentary on the aphorism "**sreṣṭaśca**" (**Brahmasūtra** II.4.7).

(3) Even if the word **svadhā** is taken as referring to Lakṣmī, the passage in question merely points to Her '**sahayoga**' (co-presence or association) with no implication of involvement in the cosmic activity. This point is corroborated by the Mahābhārata passage '**ahaṁ svahā svadhācaiva**'.

[^172_61]: Said to be from the Śrī-Vāsava Saṁhitā.

***
[[P173]]
160

(4) The passage '**Anīdavātam**' etc., has its import in the remarkable love the Lord has towards His consort Lakṣmī by reason of which He is said to be totally dependent on Her (**premapāratantryam**).

In the next Kārikā, '**nirasta kāraṇatvaṁtu śriyo noktam na śaṅkitam**',[^173_62] NM asks the scholars to examine the passage '**ānīt**' etc., impartially and decide whether Lakṣmī could be the cause of the universe. Since there is no logic in favour of Lakṣmī's causality, the word **svadhā** doesnot deserve to be interpreted as Śrī, concludes NM.

Even if she exists at the time of cosmic dissolution she need not be taken as **jagatkāraṇa** because it could lead to the contingency of accepting other factors also as **jagatkāraṇa** purely on the ground of their prior existence.

In the next Kārikā[^173_63] '**śruti-sūtraiśca samsiddhaiḥ**' etc., NM discusses the question of Lakṣmī becoming the Brahman just because **sāmya** (similarity) has been posited between the Lord and His consort. This would lead to the

[^173_62]: No. 45
[^173_63]: No. 48

***
[[P174]]
161

unwarranted position that because Śruti says, '**nirañjanaḥ paramaṁ sāmyamupaiti**' (Muṇḍaka.Up., 3-1-3) even the liberated soul becomes the Brahman and **jagatkāraṇa**.

The succeeding Kārikā[^174_64] points out that Deśika had already shown in his NŚ the way of understanding **sāmya** between Lakṣmī and Her consorts without infringing upon the characteristics of Brahman, mentioned in the **Śrutis**, **sūtra**,etc.

The next two Kārikās[^174_65] mention the characteristics which are common between Lakṣmī and Her Lord, which make their **dāmpatya** eternal.

Qualities like **ādheyatva** (dependence), **īśitavyatva** (being the ruled) and **śeṣatva** (being subordinate), which are found in Lakṣmī make Her the body of the Lord and hence a **kārya**. Then the question will be raised as to how the divine body of the Lord which is known to be eternal cannot be a **kārya**. ŚŚ answers that the **Śrutaprakāśikā** answers this question as to how, though being

[^174_64]: No. 49
[^174_65]: Nos. 50, 51

***
[[P175]]
162

a **kārya** the Lord's body is still **nitya** as is the case of the ever-liberated souls (**nityamukta**) and the **Nitya Vibhūti** accepted in the **sampradāya**.

Although Lakṣmī thus becomes a **kārya** being the **śarīra** of the Lord, she is still said to be similar with the Lord. As a matter of fact **kāryatva** and **sāmya** are mutually inconsistent. Still Deśika has explained the cases of **sāmya**, **aikya**, **śaktitva**, **tadvattā** etc., referred to in scriptures with the golden principle of **dāmpatya** between Śrī and Viṣṇu. Because Śrī has been specifically mentioned here as forming a couple with the Lord, ŚŚ contends that she is superior to other consorts like Bhūmi and Nīlā. Because the **dāmpatya** between Śrī and Viṣṇu is eternal, there is no difficulty in explaining **sāmya** and **aikya** between them.

The next Kārikā[^175_66] mentions such instances where **sāmya** has been referred to in scriptures. The passage '**tasya śaktidvayaṁ tādṛk**' ('He has two such powers') is taken from the Sāttvata Saṁhitā. '**yasyāste**' is a reference[^175_67]

[^175_66]: No. 50 ca
[^175_67]: "tasyā śaktidvayaṁ tadrūpamiśraṁ bhinna-lakṣaṇam." (No. 51ab)

***
[[P176]]
163

to v.2 of Yāmuna's Catuśślokī which also speaks of similarity. **Satya**,**jñāna**, **ananta** etc., are qualities which are common between the Lord and Śrī as in the case of the ever-liberated souls. Whatever be the case, there is no contradiction in the Lord and Lakṣmī forming a couple. Although in some places Lakṣmī and **nityamuktas** seem to be on the same footing (by virtue of **jñāna**, **ānanda**, etc) she is still distinct from them being the Mother of the universe, its mistress, object of refuge and ultimate goal. This forms the content of the next Kārikā.[^176_68]

NM observes that the **sāmya** between the Lord and His consort consists in their being the Parents of the creatures and the like and that this distinguishes the ever-liberated souls who are also said to be having **sāmya** with the Lord. NM makes a suggested reference to Raṅga Rāmānuja's commentary on NŚ where **pitṛtva** is explained as **janakatva** (being the producers).[^176_69]

ŚŚ explains that the word **janaka** used by Raṅga Rāmānuja no doubt refers to the parent but still, it

[^176_68]: No. 52
[^176_69]: See NP p.361.

***
[[P177]]
164

does not suit the context. Lakṣmī cannot be said to have existed along with Brahman prior to creation, in the status of a parent. She merely exists as an attribute and hence **Kāraṇatva** cannot be attributed to Her.[^177_70] This point has already been referred to.

The next Kārikā[^177_71] points out that even as the word **janaka** is interpreted in a secondary sense to mean a parent, the word **jagat** in the compound **jagajjanakatva** etc., should also denote the conscious beings, but not the entire universe including the insentient beings also. Explaining, ŚŚ points out that in Rāmānuja's ŚG also, the expression '**akhilajaganmātaram**' means 'the mother of all the living beings'. Only then **pitṛtva** will be common to both the Lord and His consort.[^177_72]

In the same Kārikā, NM further observes that in the Dvandva Compound, '**jagajjanakatva - śeṣitva śaraṇyatva - prāpyatvādi-sāmyācca**', the word '**jagat**' happens to be the first member. By the rule '**dvandvāt pūrvaṁ śrūyamāṇaṁ padaṁ pratyekam abhisambadhyate**' ('A word heard at the beginning

[^177_70]: See p.97 of the Text given in the Appendix (K. 46)
[^177_71]: No. 52
[^177_72]: See Raṅgarāmānuja's commentary on NŚ, p.361.(K. 53)

***
[[P178]]
165

of the Dvandva Compound must be construed severally with all the members of the Compound'), it has to be understood only as the sentient, but not the insentient entities as well. Only then the words, '**janakatva**', '**śeṣitva**', '**śaraṇyatva**' and '**prāpyatva**' become significant.

The next Kārikā[^178_73] explains the point by an analogy. NM says that in the word '**Nārāyaṇa**' of the **Aṣṭākṣarī-mantra**, the word '**nāra**' means (a) multitudes of living beings and (b) all things associated with them. The word '**ayana**' also means, (a) the **upāya** and (b) **upeya**, since **upāyatva** and **upeyatva** being the 'means' and 'goal of attainment' become applicable only for living beings but not inanimate entities. So the word '**nārāḥ**' must be taken to mean only the 'living beings'. On the same analogy, in the expression '**jagjjanakatva-śeṣitva**' etc., the word '**jagat**' must be interpreted as 'living beings' but not as 'inanimate matter' because the later sense cannot be syntactically connected with '**janakatva**', '**śaraṇyatva**' etc.

In the following Kārikā[^178_74] ŚŚ explains that direct **janakatva** with regard to the universe in its entirety

[^178_73]: No. 54
[^178_74]: No. 55

***
[[P179]]
166

is found in the Lord only, whereas in the case of Lakṣmī it can be traced indirectly by virtue of Her sharing the sportive joy of creation along with Her Lord. In any case '**Janakatva**' is common between the two only in this sense.

The **sāmya** cannot be from the view-point of qualities like **jñāna** and **ānanda**. Expressions like **Viṣṇupatnī** and **Śrīpati** ascribe **svāmitva** to both the husband and wife with reference to the Universe. Therefore there is **sāmya** but no **guṇapradhāna**-relation (secondary-primary relationship between them).

The following two Kārikās[^179_75] discuss the same issue of **sāmya**. According to some, there is **sāmya** between the Lord and His wife in being the masters with reference to **nitya** and **līlāvibhūtis**. But all other **sāmya** is based on their mutual **śeṣatva** implied by the words **pati** and **patnī** (in **śrīpati** and **viṣṇupatnī**). In other words **sāmya** is understood as **śeṣitva** which is two-fold: (a) with reference to the two **vibhūtis** and (b) with reference one another in being husband and wife. As regards their being the masters of the two **Vibhūtis**,there is scriptural evidence and hence there is no room for doubt. But their mutual **śeṣitva**

[^179_75]: Nos. 56, 57

***
[[P180]]
167

implied by the words '**pati**', '**patnī**' has to be carefully analysed, says NM. That means, there is no scriptural authority to show that Lord becomes subordinate to the other, although the reverse is possible. To explain the passage '**hrīśca te lakṣmīśca patnyau**' (Tai.Āraṇya. III. 13.2) that Lakṣmī is **śeṣa** to the Lord. But there is no express statement to the effect that Viṣṇu is subordinate to Lakṣmī.

It may be argued that expressions like '**śriyāpatiḥ**' and '**Viṣṇupatnī**' show mutual sāmya between both Lord and His consort, but they do not indicate that one is subordinate to the other.

The word '**pati**' and '**patnī**' normally indicate '**svāmitva**'. Therefore, the view that one is subordinate and the other superior, cannot be maintained. This view has been refuted by ŚŚ quoting the Sūtra, '**liṅgaviśeṣa-nirdeśāt**' (Pūrva.Mīm. VI.I.6) and Śabara's commentary thereon. ŚŚ points out that '**patnī**' is technically a woman who has a right to participate in the sacrificial performance of her husband and by the same token, she shares in all the merits that her husband can claim. She has full rights over the **dravya** acquired by her husband. By this interpretation, '**pati**' and '**patnī**' became the

***
[[P181]]
168

rightful owners of any entity or property. Therefore there can be no contradiction in one becoming subordinate to the other. This is the way in which all statements of **sāmya** have been justified by VD in his NŚ and other texts.

In the following Kārikā,[^181_76] NM following Deśika, shows the method of accounting for statements which speak of 'oneness' (**aikya**) between the Lord and His consort. He says that the '**aikya**' mentioned in the **śrutis** between the liberated souls and the Brahman is on the ground of their having one and the same **Prakāra** or mode. On the same analogy, we can understand **prakāraikya** ('oneness of the mode') subsisting between the Lord and Lakṣmī. This '**aikya**' (oneness) may be: (1) due to the oneness of the mode brought in by the extreme similarity which is possible between husband and wife; or (2) due to the oneness of **Prakāra** understood as the **śeṣatva** that this couple has with reference to the entire creation including the **nitya** and **līlāvibhūtis** or (3) it can also be understood as '**oneness of prakāra**' in forming the deities intended to be the recepients of the '**havis**' in the form of all the souls

[^181_76]: No. 58, to ab.

***
[[P182]]
169

(**ātmahaviḥ**).

ŚŚ quotes relevant passages from the NŚ[^182_77] to support this view. He explains that there are several **śruti-passages** such as '**Brahmaveda Brahmaiva bhavati**' (Tai.Up. I.2.1) and '**nirañjanaḥ paramaṁ sāmyamupaiti**' (Muṇḍ.Up., 3.1.3) which indicate that one who sheds the mortal coil becomes free from **nāma** and **rūpa**, brought in by the association with **prakṛti**. In such a state one can merely be referred to as 'having knowledge as his form' (**jñānam eva ākāraḥ**) and thus form the **Prakāra** of the Brahman. The word **prakāraikya** consists in referring to one entity as being identical with another entity (which is of course, a secondary usage) as when we say, '**so'yaṁ gauḥ**' ('he is a bull'). ŚŚ argues that statements which refer to the oneness of Lakṣmī and Nārāyaṇa can also be understood through **prakāraikya**. This **prakāraikya** can again be understood from three different angles as pointed out earlier.

The discussion on 'oneness of mode' (**prakāraikya**) between the Lord and His consort is continued in the next Kārikā also.[^182_78] NM says that the word '**prakāraikya**'

[^182_77]: See p.362.
[^182_78]: No. 59

***
[[P183]]
170

should be first of all construed with the preceding expression quite naturally. Without this, connecting it with the succeeding passage does not make any sense. ŚŚ points out that in the original passage of NŚ,[^183_79] similarity between Nārāyaṇa and Lakṣmī who form the couple should be explained through **prakāraikya** alone and this **prakāraikya** must be in terms of qualities like **jñāna** and **ānanda**. Although there is difference between the **jñāna** and **ānanda** of Lakṣmī and those of the Lord, we have to take into consideration the **sausādṛśya** (extreme similarity) between the **jñāna**s of Lakṣmī and Viṣṇu and also between their **ānandas**. It is this extreme similarity that facilitates treatment of their **jñānas** as being one and identical, and **ānandas** also as becoming one and identical. This leads to the intended **prakāraikya** on the basis of which the '**aikya**' of the couple can be satisfactorily accounted for.

ŚŚ winds up the discussion on **prakāraikya** and remarks that the method of interpretation shown so far applies to 'statements of oneness' (**aikyavāda**) found in authoritative texts. It does not apply to statements of oneness which have no scriptural authority at all, and

[^183_79]: NŚ, p.362:

***
[[P184]]
171

which one comes across very often.

The following four Kārikās[^184_80] continue the discussion on the '**aikya**' between Lakṣmī and Nārāyaṇa.

VD's verses forming part of his commentary on the first verse of the Catuśślokī are quoted as authority regarding the interpretations of text mentioning the identity of Lord and His consort. ŚŚ points out that the CŚB takes up the issue of 'oneness of Lakṣmī and Nārāyaṇa' and solves it through what he calls **sāmarasya** (having identical tastes and mental inclination). But in the NŚ this **aikya** has been explained as three types of **prakāraikya**.

There are some critics who argue that it is cumbersome to accept the Divine couple Lakṣmī Nārāyaṇa as two persons and as such it will be parsimonious to accept one single one. NM argues that if parsimony is the only criterion, then the plurality of **jīvas** can be dismissed and only one **jīva** should be accepted, which theory however is rejected by Śrī Rāmānuja.

[^184_80]: Nos. 62, 63, 64, 65

***
[[P185]]
172

There are also some who argue that all the living beings are both different and non-different from one another. On this view, Lakṣmī and Nārāyaṇa can also be accepted as one. But this view is rejected by the traditionalists. Statements involving **abheda** (non-difference) between Lord and Lakṣmī can be explained like the statement '**Rāmasugrīvayoraikyam**' without undermining the essential difference between each other.

ŚŚ states that Deśika has already proved the difference between the Lord and His consort. Texts like '**naranārīmayo hariḥ**' and '**nārāyaṇātmikāṁ devīm**' found in the Brahmāṇḍa and Kāśyapīyapurāṇas appear to explain the oneness of the Lord and His consort. But the intention of these passages is quite different. They have to be explained in such a way that the **svarūpabheda** between the Lord and His consort is not ignored. When we say '**jyotsneva himadīdhiteḥ**' ('like the beams of the Moon') we mean only the oneness of the Moon who is the locus of the beams. The NŚ of VD as explained by Raṅga Rāmānuja (RR)[^185_81] records a number of views on Lakṣmī such as:

[^185_81]: See p.360.
Cf. CŚB, pp. 3-5.

***
[[P186]]
173

(a) The Lord qualified by sattā etc., is alone is termed as Śrī; (b) Bhagavān, who has permanently taken a different feminine form is called Śrī; (c) The Lord Himself for His own enjoyment takes up a female form which is called Śrī, etc. All these views are rejected by the śruti-passage '**hrīśca te lakṣmīśca patnyau**'. (Tai.Ār.III. 13.2) which clearly establishes the difference between the Lord and His consort in the most natural way ('as husband and wife'). Moreover Yāmuna's reference as '**Kāntāste**' (using different Case-endings) supports this view.

In the next Kārikā,[^186_82] NM states that the views expressed by the commentator seem to favour the oneness of the Lord and His wife. Some can be explained or justified while others are totally unauthoritative.

Then what about those passages wherein Lakṣmī is stated to be the **Śakti** of the Lord? The following Kārikā[^186_83] explains this point. ŚŚ points out that NŚ shows the way of interpreting passages where Śrī is

[^186_82]: No. 66
[^186_83]: No. 67.

***
[[P187]]
174

identified with the **Śakti** of the Lord. According to it **Śakti** forms only the **Viśeṣaṇa** of the Lord, being His consort. At the time of creation, this **Śakti** is identified with Lakṣmī and she can be taken as **sahakārī kāraṇa** because she also has cosmic creation etc., as a sportive activity. The words '**samāna-niyatayā**', do not mean that Lakṣmī has all cosmic activities as her sport, since she has no **nigraha**. This expression therefore means '**sāmarasyena**', as having identical taste. Deśika's commentary on Rāmānuja's **Gadya** is also quoted in support. ŚŚ also observes that inducing the servants to action is done by the kings through their command. Ministers and others induce the kings to action through appeals. Among equals, kings bring in inducement through gifts but in the case of the Lord, Lakṣmī induces Him to action only through **sāmarasya** as expressed by the following Kārikā.[^187_84]

In the succeeding Kārikā,[^187_85] NM refers to the interpretation of '**Śakti**' shown by Deśika in his commentary on

[^187_84]: > नार्थाया न च दानॆन प्रॆरकत्वं न याचया।। [No.68 ab]
[^187_85]: No. 69

***
[[P188]]
175

the **Catuśślokī**. According to these quotations which are taken from the Pāñcarātrāgamas, Brahmasūtra and **Brāhmapurāṇa**, **Prakṛti** is called **Śakti** of the Lord. This **Prakṛti** could be the primordial Nature according to the **prima facie** view. But according to ŚŚ, **śakti** being an aspect of Śrī, can also be identified with her.

Another way of understanding the identity of Śrī and **Prakṛti** according to the next Kārikā[^188_86] of NM is by recognising **Prakṛti** as an aspect of Lakṣmī. Commenting on this verse ŚŚ remarks that Raṅga Rāmānuja in his commentary on NŚ puts forth what is called '**śaktitva-vāda**' according to which Śrī is same as **Prakṛti**, which is the **Śakti** of the Lord. But the interpretation given by NM that **Prakṛti** is an aspect of Śrī is more welcome than the **śaktitva-vāda**, concludes ŚŚ.

In the next Kārikā[^188_87] NM quotes VD to the effect that Lord Vāsudeva emanates as **Saṅkarṣaṇa**, Pradyumna and others. In the same way, He assumes different forms like Sītā and Rukmiṇī. The difference between these two

[^188_86]: No. 70
[^188_87]: No. 71

***
[[P189]]
176

lies in this: (1) Aniruddha and others are emanations of the Lord in essence (**svarūpataḥ**). Lakṣmī, although she is essentially different from the Lord can still be understood as His aspect. Consequently Sītā, Rukmiṇī and others can also be stated to be identical with the Lord as the aspects of Lakṣmī. In this manner all passages which refer to Lakṣmī as the **Śakti**, **Saṁvit**, **Ahantā**,**Icchā** etc., can be accounted for. This is the gist of the succeeding Kārikā itself.[^189_88]

Commenting on this ŚŚ says that statements which identify Śrī with Viṣṇu's '**Icchā**', **Saṁvit**, **Ahantā** etc. can be interpreted as pointing out the essential nature of the Lord.[^189_89] Passages which speak of Lakṣmī as on par with Viṣṇu can be easily explained by virtue of external **dāmpatya** subsisting between them.[^189_90]

[^189_88]: No. 72
[^189_89]: Vide Deśika statement (No.p.363): 'vyūhavadavasth-abhedavādāstu avatāradiviṣayatā...' sarvasya bhagavadātmakatvena tasyā svechayā parechayā vā kāryadaśāpanna-syāpi bheda-vyapadeśatvāt. evamicchā-saṁvidahantādi-vyapadeśā api prāpyānuvidheyatvatsvayamprakāśatva-svarūpa-nirūpakatva-viśeṣa-rūpādimātrastāvyāḥ'.
[^189_90]: Cf. VP. "यथा सर्वगतो विष्णुस्तथैवेयं द्विजोत्तम -" (I.8-17)
Viṣṇusmṛti: > आग्नेय्या सर्वभूतानां यथा नित्योऽस्तिनिग्रहः। देवत्वे देवदेहेयं मनुष्यत्वेऽपि मानुषी।। [94.6]

***
[[P190]]
177

In the next Kārikā[^190_91] NM remarks that passages referring to Sītā, Rukmiṇī and others as different states of existence of the Lord, have already been explained and justified. But a few commentators avoided references to such passages and have not even explained the reason for their silence on this issue.[^190_92]

In the next Kārikā[^190_93] NM observes that Lord Viṣṇu in some texts is referred to as '**nārīmaya**' ('of the form of women'). This must be explained on the ground that He is the support of Lakṣmī herself who represents all womanhood. In the same way Lakṣmī is called **nārāyaṇātmikā** ('of the form of Lord Nārāyaṇa') and this must be interpreted on the basis of Her being the consort of the Lord.

Commenting on this ŚŚ observes that passages found in the **Brāhma**, **Kāśyapīya** and **Viṣṇu Vaibhava** are so far accounted for on the lines of interpretation shown by Deśika. He then enters into a very elaborate

[^190_91]: No. 73
[^190_92]: The scholar whom NM keeps in mind may be Viṣṇucitta, the commentator on Viṣṇupurāṇa.
[^190_93]: No. 74 ab.

***
[[P191]]
178

discussion on the exact import of the word **janakatva** found in the compound '**jagajjanakatva - śaraṇyatva**' etc. As a matter of fact this issue has already been discussed earlier to counter the view of VR that **janaktva** is not mere **pitṛtva** but **hitapravartakatva** ('conduciveness to bring about welfare'). ŚŚ points out that there is no need to resort to **Lakṣaṇā** here and the primary meaning can itself be accepted. Since NM in his introductory verse of this text says '**dampatī janakau vidheḥ**' there is nothing objectionable in accepting Lakṣmī as the **utpādikā** ('the one who gives birth to beings like Brahmā'). The important difference between VR and NM is that while VR accepts Śrī as the repository of **sāmarthya** ('capacity') to carry out all cosmic activities without any exception, NM believes that since she has no **nigraha** at all, and since > **sāmarthya** alone cannot be the criterion of activities, Lakṣmī can be said to form the direct cause of all functions involving **anugraha** and that she prompts the Lord to function through **sāmarasya** ('identity of taste'), and forms the indirect cause regarding cosmic functions involving **nigraha**. There is nothing wrong in accepting '**janakatva**' as **pitṛtva**, explains ŚŚ in his commentary on this Kārikā.

***
[[P192]]
179

ŚŚ also discusses the issue of Lakṣmī's being the ruler of the entire universe (**Īśvarī**) at length and on the authority of NŚ and other texts concludes that there is no 'fear of dvairājya' as a consequence. All this is possible because of the special status of Lakṣmī as the **patnī** of the Lord who is referred to as **Īśvara**. He again confirms that the definition of **Īśvara** given in NŚ '**svajñānasvetara-samastadravya-śarīratvam**' is intended to exclude Brahmā, Rudra and other gods from the scope, but not Lakṣmī.

The main thrust of ŚŚ's criticism in this elaborate commentary is against the ŚTS of VR, passages from which are taken and refuted sentence by sentence. The passage from the **Sāgārthasaṁkṣepa** of Śrīrāmaṁiśra referring to the **śeṣa-śeṣi-relation** between the Lord and His consort is also quoted by ŚŚ in support of the definition of **Īśvaratva** which is given as '**Vibhūtidvaya-śeṣitva**' (having the two **Vibhūtis** as subservient).

In the next Kārikā NM tries to explain the statement of the **Viṣṇuvaibhava**,[^192_94] which seems to refer[^192_95]

[^192_94]: No. 75
[^192_95]: CŚB. p.5: > यं यादृशोऽसि कं नामानि तादृशं ते

***
[[P193]]
180

to the **Svarūpaikya** of the divine couple. ŚŚ quotes Deśika's **Catuśślokī-Bhāṣya** which contains a reference to the **Viṣṇuvaibhava**. According to him **Svarūpaikya** is not possible literally. The **Viṣṇuvaibhava** passage refers to **Vigrahaikya** only and this can be explained through the mutual will of the couple. The concept of **Svarūpaikya** is opposed to the **Śrutis**.

Quoting profusely from the **Catuśślokī Bhāṣya** which establishes the difference in the **Svarūpa** of Lakṣmī, NM states in the next Kārikā (76ab) that the view of those who argue that Viṣṇu himself assumes the form of Lakṣmī, should be rejected. It is because of the difference between the Lord and His consort in terms of their essential nature, the latter becomes the body of the former. It is only on this ground that the **śruti** passage, '**na tat samaścābhyadhikaśca dṛśyate**' (**Śve.Up.**, 6-8) becomes justified. The Kārikā '**samādhika daridratvam**' etc.,[^193_96] proves that the characteristics of Brahman, such as not having any other being as equal or superior, controlling everything other than oneself, and being the refuge of those who are helpless are found only in the Lord but not in both.

[^193_96]: No. 77

***
[[P194]]
181

ŚŚ discusses the question whether the epithets used in this verse '**aśaraṇyaśaraṇyatva**' etc. can be applied to Lakṣmī or not and concludes that the kind of **śaraṇyatva** which is found in the Lord is characterised by conferring the full experience of **Ānanda** which is again marked by 'shedding His anger' caused by the violations of His command perpetuated by the **jīvas** from time immemorial. in the case of Lakṣmī however, the element of the **nigraha** is absent. The other aspect namely, granting Bliss in full and thus forming the object of refuge is present in Her. ŚŚ quotes profusely from Deśika's **Gadyabhāṣya** and **Catuśślokī Bhāṣya** to corroborate the points mentioned in the Kārikā.

The discussion then turns to Lord's becoming the object of refuge for those who are helpless. In the next Kārikā,[^194_97] NM points out that VD has explained the way in which Lakṣmī becomes the refuge for those who are unable to find any solace. She becomes helpful in bringing to fruition the **nyāsa** they do to the Lord for the sake of Mokṣa.

ŚŚ explains that those who, desirous of Mokṣa approach the Lord, there being no other **śaraṇya**, they

[^194_97]: No. 78

***
[[P195]]
182

have to resort to Lakṣmī first to attain their objective. The word of Trijatā in the **Rāmāyaṇa**, "**bhartṛsītāmāpi mahato bhayāt**" and those of Hanumān, "**alameṣā**" etc., are quoted in support.

The next Kārikā[^195_98] reflects the views of Vyāsārya who also confirms the view that those who cannot directly approach the Lord should first resort to Lakṣmī.

The next Kārikā[^195_99] declares that only the Supreme Brahman qualified by Śrī should be resorted to, on the authority of the definition of **Prapatti**, the Mantra which speaks of it, the Injunction which ordains it and the Āgama texts, **Śrī Bhāṣya** and the **Sampradāya**. The definition of **Prapatti** '**ananyasādhye**' etc.,[^195_100] is attributed to one Bharata Muni. According to this, entrusting one burden to the Lord with a prayerful request to protect, becomes **Prapatti**. According to a quotation from RTS, the Lord merely expects the **mumukṣu** to seek Him for protection ('**Rakṣāpekṣāṁ pratīkṣate**'). Therefore even **prārthanā**

[^195_98]: No. 79
[^195_99]: No. 80
[^195_100]: > अनन्यसाध्ये स्वाभीष्टे महाविश्वासपूर्वकम्।
> तदेकोपायता याच्ञा प्रपत्तिः शरणागतिः।।

***
[[P196]]
183

becomes an **aṅga** of **Prapatti**. The Mantra which ordains **Prapatti** is the **Dvaya** and the Vidhi which ordains it is the statement '**māmekaṁ śaraṇaṁ vraja**' of the **Gītā** (Ch.18-66). Other passages from scriptures and Rāmānuja's commentary on the Sūtra '**uṅgupattleścu**' etc.[^196_101] are cited by ŚŚ in support. The gist of the discussion is that Lord Nārāyaṇa alone has to be resorted to by those who are desirous of liberation.

The succeeding Kārikā[^196_102] explains the role of Lakṣmī as an attribute of the Lord, who earlier has been explained as the person to be resorted to. The whole process of the Lord's protecting the **jīvas** is likened to a sacrifice where the Lord forms the **Yajamāna** with Lakṣmī as His Patnī, and his qualities forming the **ṛtviks**. Lakṣmī becomes the attribute of the Lord like the **guṇas** and **vigraha** of the Lord which also attain the status of attributes only.

In the next Kārikā[^196_103] NM says that the Lord's qualities like **Vātsalya**, **Svāmitva**, etc., and the body (**śarīra**) have their own utility and application in the

[^196_101]: Śrī Bhāṣya: III.2.34.
[^196_102]: No. 81
[^196_103]: No. 82

***
[[P197]]
184

act of saving the devotees. The actual relationship of the **Patnī**, **ṛtviks** and others with the **Yajamāna** in the 'sacrifice of protection' is what is called the **upayoga** in the verse. In his commentary ŚŚ quotes from RTS and explains the exact application of this analogy as intended by NM.

Elucidating the idea, ŚŚ states that the Divine form of the Lord is useful in generating a steady love for Him and concentration on Him in His devotees. The utility of Lakṣmī lies in Her doing things favourable to the Lord, by giving Her consent to His activities. This is so because in a sacrifice, the acts of the **Yajamāna** should be supported by his **Patnī**. So when the Lord decides to protect the devotees, Lakṣmī's association with Him should result in Her consenting to this act.

ŚŚ quotes 3 verses which explain the exact role of Lakṣmī as a **viśeṣaṇa** of the Lord, being ever associated with Him. As a result of this she becomes the recipient of the **bhara** of those who surrender to the Lord also. According to these verses Lakṣmī's association with the Lord removes the unapproachability[^197_104]

[^197_104]: PM, p.167 [Nos.83,84,85]

***
[[P198]]
185

(**ādhṛṣyatva**) of the Lord and generates confidence in those who surrender. Even during the stage of **Nyāsa** she remains as an attribute, destroys the sins of the devotees, generates a taste in them for the Lord who forms the goal, produces a conviction that Lord alone is the **upāya** and ensures His grace for them. All this is the outcome of Lakṣmī's being the **Viśeṣaṇa** of the Lord. ŚŚ also gives all the etymologies of the word '**Śrī**' ('**śṛṇāti nikhilān doṣān**' etc) mentioned in the **Ahirbudhnya Saṁhitā** which reflect Her role of **Puruṣakāra** between man and God, Her position as the Mother of the beings and Her status as the consort to the Lord. Lines from Yāmuna's **Catuśślokī**, Deśika's **Bhāṣya** thereon,verses from ŚGRK, **Rāmāyaṇa**, **Viṣṇupurāṇa** and **Upaniṣads** like the **Kathā** are quoted in support of the contention that in **Nyāsa**, Lakṣmī remains as a **viśeṣaṇa**.

In the succeeding Kārikā '**lakṣmyā vidyā viśeṣatve**'[^198_105] NM raises the **pūrvapakṣa** that Lakṣmī may become the cause of universe if she is accepted as a **viśeṣaṇa** of **Vidyā** (**upāsanā**) and answers that it is not so.

[^198_105]: No. 86 ab

***
[[P199]]
186

Lakṣmī does not attain causality like the Lord merely on the ground of Her being the **Viśeṣaṇa** of the Lord. This is illustrated on the analogy of Indra and other gods mentioned in the **Pratardanavidyā** in the Upaniṣad.[^199_106] There Indra and others become mere **Viśeṣaṇas** of the Brahman who forms the on this account they do not become **jagatkāraṇa** like the Lord. Similar is the case with Lakṣmī also, but with a distinction - Indra and others cannot be associated with all cosmic functions and hence **Kāraṇatva** in their case is ruled out. But Lakṣmī who is associated with the Lord through similar activities, can become the **Kāraṇa** like the Lord whom she qualifies.

The next verse '**upalakṣaṇatvapakṣaṇ**' etc.,[^199_107] points out that VD in all his works justifies the role of Lakṣmī as a **Viśeṣaṇa** like the **guṇas** and **vigraha** of the Lord, after refuting the view that she forms merely an **upalakṣaṇa**.

The succeeding two Kārikās[^199_108] clarify the point that Lakṣmī is the **Viśeṣaṇa** of the Lord. Lakṣmī and the

[^199_106]: No. 86 c d.
[^199_107]: No. 87
[^199_108]: Nos. 88,89

***
[[P200]]
187

attributes of the Lord such as **Vātsalya** and **Svāmitva** do not have any direct relationship with the **Bhārasvīkāraṇa** ('accepting the burden') and **Rakṣāsaṅkalpa** ('the decision to protect') which are unique to the Lord. But still both have an intimate **upayoga** (purpose) in the activities of the Lord. She prompts the Lord to do those acts through a perfect identity of tastes (**sāmarasya**). Compared to other **guṇas**, however, **sāmarasya** is more in Lakṣmī than in the Lord.

Commenting, ŚŚ points out that even Lakṣmī can be the recipient of **Bhara** and have '**rakṣāsaṅkalpa**' which consists in bestowing unending Bliss through **anugraha**, since there is no contradiction in such a conception.

The following Kārikā[^200_109] point out that in the case of the Lord's cosmic activities, Lakṣmī is said to have **aikarasya** with the Lord. But this cannot be traced to '**ekasaṅkalpa**', regarding all the cosmic activities, she being known to be free from... ŚŚ points out that the word **aikarasya** in the Kārikā must be interpreted as '**sāmarasya**'. He refers to Deśika's quotation of

[^200_109]: No. 90

***
[[P201]]
188

a verse from Kūreśa[^201_110] where the word '**aikarasya**' is used to convey the idea of **Sāmarasya**.

In the following pages a very elaborate discussion is made regarding the views of VR on the exact status of Lakṣmī, whether she forms the **Puruṣakāra** alone, or the **upāya** also in addition to **Puruṣakāratva**. The RTS of Deśika is cited in support. ŚŚ states that the '**Sāmarthya**' of Lakṣmī which is acceptable to both VR and NM has a different connotation for NM. While VR directly tries to relate **Sāmarthya** to **Kriyā** and thus makes Lakṣmī '**sahakartrī**' in the act of protection and tries to establish Her as the **upāya**. ŚŚ argues that **Sāmarthya** must necessarily involve **kriyā** which in the case of Lakṣmī is not possible. That is to say, she cannot directly show **nigraha** and later shed it as the Lord does. It is better to accept **aikarasya** as explained by NM which means **sāmarasya** i.e. identity of tastes and through that Lakṣmī can indirectly be made a co-performer of the duties of Her husband which ultimately will establish Her in direct **upāyatva** also. ŚŚ makes a big issue of all of this and quotes profusely from Deśika

[^201_110]: **Śrīstava**, V.1: " ... रसादेकरस्यात् त्वाम् "

***
[[P202]]
189

to prove that his real intention is to establish the **upāyatva** of Lakṣmī through **sāmarasya** and not merely through **sāmarthya**. Even compared to Her role as the **Puruṣakāra**, Her prompting the Lord to carry out all the cosmic activities in the spirit of **sāmarasya** is more reasonable to accept, contends ŚŚ. When the exact role of Lakṣmī in granting complete bliss in the manner of Her Lord is beset with problems, it is logical and authoritative to establish that aspect through **paramparā-sambandha**, he concludes. ŚŚ quotes profusely from STŚ which criticises the opinion of NM on the status of Lakṣmī and refutes its sentence by sentence. The gist of this criticism is the same namely, Lakṣmī has both **Puruṣakāratva** and **upāyatva** according to NM and her **upāyatva** is characterised by **sāmarasya** but not **sāmarthya** as contended by VR. Another point stressed by ŚŚ is that apart from Lakṣmī, no other consort of the Lord is ever accepted as **Puruṣakāra** in the **Śrīvaiṣṇava** tradition.

Another discussion[^202_111] is that Lakṣmī a **Viśeṣaṇa** can never be equated with qualities which are themselves no

[^202_111]: See pp. 173 of the Text.

***
[[P203]]
190

conscious entities. On the other hand, her **Viśeṣaṇatva** consists in being of the nature of the Supreme Being Himself and thus she plays a distinct and significant role as **Puruṣakāra**.

The succeeding Kārikā[^203_112] clarifies the point which has already been mentioned before viz., that when Lakṣmī becomes the **Viśeṣaṇa** for the Lord, she becomes the **kāraṇa** also (indirectly). But as a **Viśeṣaṇa** she stands on a different footing from other gods like Indra and Brahmā who are also described as the **Viśeṣaṇas** of the Lord in the **Pratardana Vidyā**.

ŚŚ points out that objections raised by VR against NM do not stand to reason. NM has pointed out in several places that Lakṣmī, though dependent upon the Lord, can grant **mokṣa** also by granting **sāmya** etc., in Kārikās like '**sāmyapradāna saṅkalpaḥ**'.[^203_113]

In the following Kārikā[^203_114] it has been declared that those who are dependent on the Lord cannot have any

[^203_112]: Page 102.
[^203_113]: No. 97
[^203_114]: No. 92

***
[[P204]]
191

**saṅkalpa** to grant **Mokṣa** directly and that such a power lies only with **Nārāyaṇa**, the Lord of **Ramā**. This verse according to ŚŚ states that Lakṣmī cannot be equated with Brahmā, Rudra and other gods who are totally dependent on the Lord, since they cannot have **saṅkalpa** to grant **mokṣa**. According to RTS those gods may sometimes teach others **Nyāsa**, **Upāsanā** etc., as a means of **Mokṣa**, but Lakṣmī has a direct role to play in the scheme of **Mokṣa**. She becomes the **Sahakāriṇī** to the Lord when He desires to grant **Mokṣa**. This **sahakāritva** is the special prerogative conferred upon Her by the Lord.

NM never interprets texts like "**saṁsāraṁpravatariṇīṁ**," etc., relying upon pure logic, as alleged by VR. On the other hand all factors regarding Lakṣmī such as her unalloyed grace which is natural to Her motherly status, and the resultant bestowing of complete bliss which is called **Mokṣa**, are all explained on the basis of valid scriptural texts.

ŚŚ as usual, takes up certain passages from ŚTS (pp.50,51) which criticise the PM and answers them in all thoroughness. He tries to prove that the excellence of Lakṣmī is not natural (**svatassidha**) because it is

***
[[P205]]
192

admitted to be dependent upon the Lord, and this is also meant to please the Lord. Therefore it cannot be 'as natural as in the case of the Lord'. Even the traditional passage '**ananyādhīna-kalyāṇam**'[^205_115] fits in well with the spirit of PM, argues ŚŚ because the auspiciousness of Lakṣmī is dependent upon the Lord and from this view-point she may be said to be dependent upon the Lord. The **Guṇabhāva** (subordinate position) of Lakṣmī is the result of mutual will (**ubhayecchā**), even as the auspicious nature of Lakṣmī is dependent on Bhagavān. By this, however Lakṣmī's greatness cannot be vitiated. On the other hand such a thing adds to the excellence of Lakṣmī. The Divine couple forms the recipient of the offering in the form of the soul (**ātmahavis**) in such a way that they have equal share in it. ŚŚ quotes a passage from the **Siddhamidhyasodhādhikāra** of RTS and establishes that certain contradictions pointed by VR in the statements of NM do not really exist at all.

In the next Kārikā[^205_116] NM observes that if one carefully analyses the point whether Lakṣmī is **Viśeṣaṇa** or **upalakṣaṇa**,

[^205_115]: Parāśara's Lakṣmīkalyāṇapañcaka, opening verse.
[^205_116]: No. 100

***
[[P206]]
193

her status as **upāya** also would have been understood. Commenting on this ŚŚ says that Lakṣmī's **upāyatva** is clearly established in the **Mūlamantrādhikāra** of RTS, NŚ and the **Nyāsa Tilaka** of VD. Substantiating his statements with a number of quotations from these texts, he also points out the untenability of the objections raised by VR.

In the following verse[^206_117] NM states that Lakṣmī's being the **upāya** like the Lord is not 'heard' ('through any scriptural declarations') at all because she is free from **nigraha**. That she is capable of conferring the bliss of **Mokṣa** (**ānandānubhava**) through **anugraha** is accepted on all hands. Deśika in his RTS explains **kopanivṛtti** as '**pāpebhyaḥ mokṣaṇam**'. The fact that Lakṣmī makes one free from sins itself implies her absence of anger. It is this kind of **upāyatva** that is possible with Lakṣmī.

The following Kārikā[^206_118] explains the same point. The universal Mother can never afford to get angry. The Lord alone becomes the **daṇḍadhara**. This again has to be traced to the violation of the divine commands by the **jīvas** in some remote past. Deśika in his RTS has time

[^206_117]: No. 94
[^206_118]: No. 95

***
[[P207]]
194

and again declared that the **śeṣatva** of Lakṣmī covers every living being in the universe apart from the Lord and that Her grace is bereft of any trace of anger. By the statement '**na māturanapādyate**' (it does not behove the Divine Mother) what NM wants to convey is that Lakṣmī cannot be the means of liberation after '**shedding of anger**' (**kopanivṛtti-pūrvaka**) etc., which feature is unique with the Lord. '**viśiṣṭa-niṣedha**' has its import in **viśeṣaṇa-niṣedha** (when a substantive which is qualified is totally negated, the intention is to negate the attribute alone). Citing parallels from the sacrificial parlance such as "**lohitoṣṇīṣāḥ ṛtvijaḥ pracaranti**" (**ṛtviks**, wearing red turbans, move about) and '**dadhnā juhuyāt**',('one should offer curds in the fire') ŚŚ points out that the stress is on **lauhitya** (redness) in the first instance and on curds in the second, which form the **viśeṣaṇa**. Therefore **nigraha-nivṛtti** is of great importance in this context,argues ŚŚ. Deśika also cites the well-known passage '**yathā na kriyate jyotsnā**' to assert that removal of the impediments is the chief criterion of the **upāyatva** of Lakṣmī.

The Kārikā '**asyāśca**' etc., points out that the **pārārthya** of Lakṣmī ('that she exists exclusively for[^207_119]

[^207_119]: No. 147

***
[[P208]]
195

the Lord) is dependent upon the desire of Lord alone or on their mutual will. There are **śruti-passages** in favour of both of them being the rulers of this universe.

The Kārikā '**sā tu nārāyaṇasyaiva**'[^208_120] explains in clear terms that Lord Nārāyaṇa, consort of Ramā alone has the direct **Saṅkalpa** to confer **Mokṣa**, who is independent. The opening statement of the **Rahasyaratnāvalīhṛdaya** of Deśika illustrates this point, says NM.[^208_121]

The word **Nārāyaṇa** has been explained by ŚŚ as **Tatpuruṣa** and **Bahuvrīhi** compounds, bringing out the suzerainty of the Lord and his total independence.

The passage from RRI referred to,[^208_122] brings out the same idea that Lord Nārāyaṇa alone is totally independent in removing all the impediments and that He does not depend upon anybody else in this matter.

NM appeals to critics to analyse the statements of Deśika found in the RRI, **Catuśślokī Bhāṣya** and **Gadyabhāṣya**

[^208_120]: No. 92
[^208_121]: vide " 96
[^208_122]: RRI, p.99: "Śrīmannārāyaṇaṉ oruvaṉē sarvajīvargaḷukkum tañjam".

***
[[P209]]
196

and come to a conclusion regarding the essential nature of Lakṣmī. Lakṣmī can grant all rewards directly or indirectly. Her magnanimity is reflected in expression like '**Sarvakāmapradāṁ**' etc.

ŚŚ points out in his commentary that although complete experience of the Brahman is quite natural to **jīva** as brilliance is to a gem, it still depends upon the **Saṅkalpa** of the Lord. Though it is natural all the time, still the aspect of its leading to a continuous and unbroken service of the Lord has to be aspired for by the **jīvas**. Thus it becomes a **puruṣārtha** and God's **Saṅkalpa** becomes invariable for its attainment. Quoting a verse from RTS, ŚŚ says that like a father granting a share in property to his son after his formal request although he rightfully deserves it, the Lord grants **Kaiṅkarya** to an offending **jīva** only after his formal prayer. It is this kind of **Saṅkalpa** that is referred to before.

The discussion then shifts to the status of Śrī as the **Viśeṣaṇa** of the Lord who is called the '**siddhopāya**'. "How can anyone state that Śrī becomes an '**upalakṣaṇa**' (**Indicator**) in the first portion of the **Dvayamantra**?"

***
[[P210]]
197

asks Nārāyaṇa Muni in the next Kārikā.[^210_123] The **Siddhopāya-śodhanādhikāra** (of the RTS), the **Gadyabhāṣya** and the **Catuśślokībhāṣya** of Deśika do not prove Lakṣmī as either an **Upalakṣaṇa** or as an **upāya**. Their intention is to show Her as a **Viśeṣaṇa** of the Lord. ŚŚ objects to VR's allegation that NM equates Lakṣmī with other '**pāratantra-cetanas**' and makes her devoid of '**subhāśrayatva**'. What NM states is that Śrī has no direct desire to confer mokṣa like the Lord. He never denies her '**subhāśrayatva**'. The point to be noted is that the '**upāyatva**' of Lakṣmī lies in Her 'conferring the experience of complete bliss', whereas the '**upāyatva**' of the Lord consists in His conferring such an experience 'after shedding his wrath'. There is no question of any 'duality' of **upāyas**. NM has been consistent in this declaration, says ŚŚ in his commentary.

The next verse of the PM states that the '**pārārthya**' of Śrī is based on the will of the Lord. Since the **śrutis** declare that both the Lord and His consort are the 'rulers of all' (**sarvaiśvarya**), it must be concluded that the '**pārārthya**' of Śrī is dependent upon the will of both.[^210_124]

[^210_123]: 'īśādvarā bandhahāneḥ..' etc. [No.100]
[^210_124]: 'asyāśceśvara...' etc. [No.147]

***
[[P211]]
198
