Commenting on this ŚŚ explains the relation between the Lord and His consort, quoting the **Viṣṇusahasranāma-bhāṣya** (p.560) of Parāśara Bhaṭṭa, on the word '**Śrīdhara**'. The relation is comparable to the one subsisting between a gem and its radiance, a flower and its fragrance, the Moon and her beams and nectar and its sweetness, which are all natural (**autpattika**). Śrī is an '**apṛthaksiddha-dharma**' dependent upon the Lord. Her relation with the Lord exists as long as She exists, which means it is 'eternal' and 'natural'.

ŚŚ, as usual, takes up passages from the ŚTS,[^211_125] purporting to criticise the PM and answers that nowhere does NM contradict the statements of VD regarding the status of Lakṣmī as the inseparable '**Viśeṣaṇa**' of the Lord. He discusses at great length that Lakṣmī cannot have even the desire to set the beings free (**mokṣaṇa-saṅkalpa** of the form '**mokṣayiṣyāmi**') since that would imply Her 'binding' the **jīvas** first. He points out that Śrī can become the means of liberation by removing '**avidyā**' (**avidyānivṛttikartṛtvarūpa-mokṣopāyatvam**) in which aspect she is similar to the Lord. He illustrates

[^211_125]: pp. 40-41.

***
[[P212]]
199

this point by profuse quotations from Deśika's RTS (**Caramaślokādhikāra**) and **Śaraṇāgati-Dīpikā** (v.3).

ŚŚ also states that NM has not just advocated the '**puruṣakāratva**' of Lakṣmī. He has also proved that she becomes the '**upāya**' in a number of Kārikās (e.g., '**sakṣātparamparāto vā**'). He has also stated that She, like the Lord, becomes the object (**uddeśya**) of **Bharanyāsa**. He finds fault with VR that ascribing views to NM which are not actually stated by him, is unfair and unfounded.[^212_126]

It may then be asked as to how the definition of the term '**śrī**' as '**śṛṇāti nikhilān doṣān**' does not imply the desire on the part of Śrī to 'eschow **nigraha**'. The reply is that in the earlier portion of the **Dvayamantra**, the interpretations given for the word **śrī** become significant to establish the '**upāyatva**' of the Lord and this is clearly stated so in the RTS. 'Removing or destroying all the **doṣas**' means 'destroying karmas which stand as impediments in the path of those who aspire to practise the **Upāya**'. In other words, She destroys the impediments of **upāya** and contributes to the full emergence of '**upāya**'.

[^212_126]: See Text of PM, p. 239

***
[[P213]]
200

By the interpretation of Śrī as '**Śṛṇoti**' ('she listens to'), Her status as **Puruṣakāra** is established. Of the six interpretations for the term '**śrī**' given in the tradition, three are useful in establishing the Lord's '**upāyatva**', while three are useful to establish her '**prāpyatva**'. Since she does not have '**upāyatā**' characterised by the absence of '**nigraha**', she does not become the content of the word 'Brahman'. That is why this aspect has not been mentioned in the definitions of the term '**śrī**', contends ŚŚ.[^213_127]

Introducing the next Kārikā[^213_128] ŚŚ says that since the '**puruṣakāratva**' and '**nityayoga**' are acceptable on all hands, there would not have been any speciality about the PM if it were to repeat the same points. The special distinction of this work of NM lies in the fact that Lakṣmī has been explained as an **upāya** through Her status as **Viśeṣaṇa** but not as the chief **upāya** like the Lord. This kind of **Viśeṣaṇatva** has been illustrated by VD in his RTS and **Nyāsatilaka**.

[^213_127]: Vide pp.239 of the Text.
[^213_128]: See Text of PM, p. 241.

***
[[P214]]
201

The following verse[^214_129] states that Lakṣmī's status as **Viśeṣaṇa** has been clarified by Deśika with the help of illustrations taken from the **Śrutis**.

Explaining, ŚŚ points out that Deśika in his **Nyāsa Tilaka** (V.4) has given the example of the expression '**mahendra**' to illustrate Lakṣmī's relationship with the Lord as **Viśeṣaṇa**. The other illustration given by Deśika is of Agni and Viṣṇu who become the '**devatādvandva**' to receive the offerings in a fire-sacrifice called '**Āgnāvaiṣṇavam**'. The difference between those two examples is that in the first instance, '**mahat**', becomes the **Viśeṣaṇa** of Indra, and it is insentient. In the second illustration, Agni who becomes the **Viśeṣaṇa** of Viṣṇu is a conscious being (**Cetanā**). In the other example '**Vṛtro vṛtraṇighātināṁ**, **vṛtraḥ indraḥ**',Vṛtraḥ who is the Viśeṣaṇa of Indra is also a conscious being. Therefore Kumāra Varada, in his commentary on the verse under question states that on the same analogy Lakṣmī also can become an attribute of the Lord.

In the example of Agni and Viṣṇu by virtue of the **Dvandva** compound involving '**itaretara sambandha**', Agni

[^214_129]: No. 104.

***
[[P215]]
202

and Viṣṇu both receive equal importance. This is from the viewpoint of the **Samāsa**. But compared to Agni, Viṣṇu is superior and on this account between Agni and Viṣṇu the **Viśeṣaṇa-viśeṣya** relation can be established. This is obtained through the '**sense**' (**artha**).

The following verse **Vṛddhihrāsa**[^215_130] states that the same idea of Lakṣmī's **Viśeṣaṇatva** is reinforced by the **Brahmasūtra**,"**Vṛddhihrāsa**" etc (III.2.20). All the illustrations given to support Lakṣmī's **Viśeṣaṇatva** become justified on the analogy of the **dṛṣṭāntas**, discussed in '**Vṛddhihrāsa**' etc.

ŚŚ explains that in the **Brahmasūtra** the aphorism '**ambuvadagrahaṇāttu na tathātvam**' (III.2.19) raises an objection to the employment of illustrations like the reflection of the sun in reservoirs of water,and that of the face etc., in the mirror, to drive home the point that the Supreme Lord,though present in earth, water, etc., is not affected or associated with the defects found in those places. The subsequent sūtra,'**Vṛddhihrāsa**'

[^215_130]: No. 107

***
[[P216]]
203

etc.answers these objections that although there seems to be a disparity between the illustration (**dṛṣṭānta**) and the illustrated (**dārṣṭāntika**), strictly speaking there is no such thing when one takes the ultimate import of the illustrations.

Illustrations need not be taken to correspond to the illustrated in all aspects. Even a partial similarity will serve the purpose. Ether may be present in a big vessel or small vessel. Still it is not affected by bigness or smallness of the adjunct. The Sun may be reflected in reservoirs of water which may have different shapes, but still he cannot be associated with those shapes, small or big. It is in that aspect that the position of Lord as existing in **pṛthivī** etc., has to be understood. That partial similarity can also be employed is clear from the illustrations "**simho māṇavakaḥ**" ('student is a lion'). So the Lord who has **ubhayaliṅga**, ("freedom from defects and possession of perfections") can never be tainted by any defect by virtue of His physical presence in different locations.

ŚŚ points out in his commentary that on the analogy of these, one can also conclude that all the particulars

***
[[P217]]
204

mentioned in the illustrations by Deśika, such as '**mahendra**', '**āgnā-viṣṇū**' etc., need not be literally anticipated in the case of Lakṣmī. Mahattva is an attribute of Indra in one case. In the second case, '**āgnā-viṣṇū**' both Agni and Viṣṇu seem to be equally important but the importance of Viṣṇu compared to Agni is contextual and hence Agni becomes an attribute of Viṣṇu. On the same token, Lakṣmī also becomes a **Viśeṣaṇa** of the Lord, concludes ŚŚ.

The following verse[^217_131] stresses the adjectival character of Lakṣmī. ŚŚ in his commentary brings out the untenability of certain allegations made by VR against NM's depiction of Lakṣmī's importance. He quotes profusely from the RTS and Nyāsa Darpaṇa of Deśika to substantiate his argument. The point which he wants to drive home is that the **Viśeṣaṇatva** of Lakṣmī becomes firmly established if one subjects the PM to a careful examination. When the Lord and His consort are said to become the recipients of the **Ātmahavis**, Lakṣmī becomes an attribute to the Lord, and this is the position which NM sticks to throughout his work. There is no room for an alternative view.

[^217_131]: No. 108

***
[[P218]]
205

The next Kārikā[^218_132] confirms the same view and adds that the status of Lakṣmī as an attribute of the Lord has been clearly enunciated by Deśika in the **Īśvara** - section of **Nyāyasiddhāñjana**. ŚŚ points out that Lakṣmī's **Viśeṣaṇatva** does not imply any equality in status between Her and the Lord as may be construed from the examples given viz., "**Mahendra**" etc.

ŚŚ also refutes the criticism of VR that the third example given by Kumāra Varadācārya to his **Nyāsa Tilaka**-vyākhyā, namely, "**Vṛtraḥ vṛtra-nighātinaḥ**" is unwarranted. There is nothing wrong in giving three examples to drive home a point in argument. Another example is '**Indrasya putripe**' and the distinction between this and '**vṛtro vṛtra-nighātinaḥ**' lies in this: In the former illustration even when the son is referred to indirectly (in'**putriṇaḥ**) the **Viśeṣaṇatva** is not lost. But in the later example, Indra becomes an adjective as the 'killer of Vṛtra'. One is a direct reference and another is indirect.

In the passages '**makārastu tayordāsaḥ**', '**asya mama ca śeṣam hi**' and '**ubhayādhiṣṭhānaṁ ca**', on the face of it,

[^218_132]: No. 109

***
[[P219]]
206

the importance of Lakṣmī seems to be on an equal footing with that of the Lord. Therefore doubts about equality of Lakṣmī are possible at the time of one's offering one's essential nature to the divine couple (**svarūpa-samarpaṇa**). But such a question does not arise at the time of performing **Bharanyāsa** where Lakṣmī becomes an attribute of the Lord and only in that capacity becomes the **Uddeśya** of **Bharasamarpaṇa**. The status of Lakṣmī as an **upāya**, which prompts one's doing **Bharanyāsa** to the Lord is the result of Her being an attribute of the Lord only. It is this idea that is substantiated in the Kārikā-and-a-half that follow.

Explaining the Kārikā, ŚŚ states that although Lakṣmī and Viṣṇu seem to have equal importance in the **Yajña** involving '**ātmahavis**', Lakṣmī becomes an adjective to the Lord the '**śaraṇya**',at the time of **Bharanyāsa**. This is clear from a number of passages of the **Rāmāyaṇa**, **Sāttvatasaṁhitā**, **Viṣṇusahasranāma-stotra** and the **stotras** of Ācāryas like Yāmuna and Parāśara.[^219_133] ŚŚ clarifies that **Nyāsa** is of three kinds: **Svarūpanyāsa** (offering one's essential nature), **Bharanyāsa** (repositing one's burden)

[^219_133]: No. 110

***
[[P220]]
207

and **Phalanyāsa** (offering the fruit of one's endeavour). In all these, the PM proves that Lakṣmī is an Attribute of the Lord, but never the chief factor (**pradhāna**) like the Lord.

The question that is raised[^220_134] is whether there is any difference between **Bharanyāsa** and **Ātma** (**svarūpa**) **Nyāsa**. Answering in the positive, ŚŚ says that those who are desirous of **mokṣa** alone perform **Ātmanyāsa** (or **Svarūpanyāsa**) and **Phalanyāsa**, whereas all others (desirous of other fruits) perform **Bharanyāsa**. ŚŚ also criticises the view of 'some modern critics' ('**ādhunikaḥ**') that the Lord and Lakṣmī both become important as the **uddeśya** with regard to **Svarūpanyāsa** and that for **Bharanyāsa**, it is not so (i.e. only the Lord becomes the recipient and thus attains importance).

ŚŚ refutes the view of VR that the word '**Dampatī**' indicates the equal status of husband and wife forming the couple. Varadācārya in his commentary on **Nyāsatilaka** observes that with reference to people like us, both Śrī and Her Lord always become the **śeṣins**. But since the Lord is the master of all, He becomes the **śeṣin** for Lakṣmī also. So

[^220_134]: No. 111 ab.

***
[[P221]]
208

while the Lord is the Master of all, Śrī becomes the Mistress of all excepting One (i.e. the Lord)'. VR argues that both the Lord and Lakṣmī are equally important (**samaprādhānya**) while NM is in favour the relative importance of the Lord. The view of VR is against the view of Deśika, who refers to the Lord as '**śriyāḥpati**' thereby implying the secondary status of Śrī. In several sections of his RTS such as **Arthapañcakādhikāra**, **Tattvatrayādhikāra**, **Siddhopāyasodhanādhikāra**, **Paripūrṇabrahmānubhavādhikāra**, **Mūlamantrādhikāra**, **Dvayādhikāra** and the **Caramaślokādhikāra**, Śrī is shown as the **Viśeṣaṇa** of the Lord and hence her lesser importance (compared to the Lord) is established beyond all doubt, contends ŚŚ. He cites several passages from all these sections mentioned above, to corroborate his viewpoint. In his unduly elaborate criticism, he tries to vindicate his Ācārya's position in this way: His Ācārya i.e., NM nowhere accords equal importance to Śrī. She is only an Attribute of the Lord, in which capacity alone she can be the object of **Prapatti**, whatever type of **Prapatti** it be - **Svarūpa**, **Bhara** or **Phala**. Nowhere she becomes the '**Uddeśya**' like the Lord. Whether she is the **upāya** or **upeya**, She remains as the **Viśeṣaṇa** of the Lord only. What NM does not accept is the status of Lakṣmī as an **Upalakṣaṇa** of the Lord.

***
[[P222]]
209

In the next verse[^222_135] NM observes that even as Viṣṇu becomes the recipient of the offerings in the '**Āgnā-vaiṣṇava**' sacrifice being the Inner Controller of Agni, in the sacrifice of '**ātmahavis**' also, the Lord becomes the recipient, forming the inner controller even of His consort Lakṣmī.

The next verse[^222_136] anticipates another argument that when '**maudgacam**' is offered to Śrī, the recipient, viz., Śrī, becomes the '**Uddeśya**'. In the case of '**ātmahavis**' also let Śrī become the chief object of offerings. NM points out that even in the offering of '**maudgacam**', Śrī is not the chief recipient. Viṣṇu who is the inner controller of Śrī becomes the '**Uddeśya**' there. Even in the offering of '**caru**' to Aditi, Viṣṇu becomes the recipient of it as the inner controller of Aditi.

The next two verses[^222_137] anticipate the question that if Śrī has the Lord as her soul, it must be so stated by the Ācārya (Deśika) and that such a position is not clear from Deśika's work. For this the reply is

[^222_135]: No. 113 : 'guravo 'tra vadantyanve'
[^222_136]: No. 114 : 'viṣṇvātmāniyaḥ hi'
[^222_137]: Nos. 115,116 : 'lakṣmyantre ca' and "yantre saudarsane

***
[[P223]]
210

given that in the motif of Lakṣmī (**Lakṣmī-yantra**), Lakṣmī alone is considered to be more important than the Lord. In the same way in the **Sudarśana-yantra** also, **Sudarśana** (the chief weapon of the Lord Viṣṇu) is recognised as more important than Viṣṇu himself. But still Deśika in his NŚ has established that even these instances ultimately culminate in the Supremacy of Lord Viṣṇu alone who happens to be the '**antaryāmin**' of Lakṣmī, **Sudarśana** and others who are worshipped in different **yantras** for different purposes by different aspirants.

It may still be argued that Lakṣmī can be accepted as the direct recipient and **uddeśya** of '**Ātmahavis**' and that she need not be taken as forming the **uddeśya** through Viṣṇu, her Inner Controller.

ŚŚ introducing the next Kārikā[^223_138] answers the above objections by saying that at the very outset of the text PM, NM declared that Lord Viṣṇu the consort of Śrī alone forms the cause of the universe, that He alone has to be resorted to for liberation and that He becomes the

[^223_138]: No. 117

***
[[P224]]
211

protector as well as the goal along with Lakṣmī.[^224_139] The present Kārikā now concludes the discussion by driving home the same point in almost identical terms. ŚŚ quotes several earlier Kārikās of the PM and declares that Lakṣmī remains an attribute of the Lord in all manifestations (**avatāras**), that she is secondary to Him and that in that capacity alone she becomes the **upāya**. She becomes the recipient of '**ātmahavis**' along with Bhagavān as inner-controller, and not independently. In support of his contention, NM in the following Kārikā[^224_140] quotes the declarations of Vedānta Deśika. According to Deśika, the consort of Śrī (**Śrīmān**) is all-independent. He is the Master and in all conditions, He does not stand in need of anybody else. This kind of self-dependency or independence culminating in His **Svāmyam** cannot be found with anyboly else.

As contrasted with this, the position of Lakṣmī is always marked by dependence on the Lord, she being an attribute which is always subservient to the substantive. Her status as **upāya** can only be understood within the given framework of subservience to the Lord.

[^224_139]: No. 117
[^224_140]: No. 118, 119 ab

***
[[P225]]
212

The succeeding verse[^225_141] states that when the Lord wants to protect somebody, His grace qualified by His independence becomes the chief cause therefor. His being the **Svāmin**, the eligibility of the person, the '**nyāsa**' he performs etc, all become co-operative causes. ŚŚ comments that by referring to the Lord as **Puruṣārthashetu**, NM suggest that Śrī who becomes the **Viśeṣaṇa** is subordinate, and to that extent Her role becomes secondary.

The Kārikā[^225_142] quoted earlier clearly states that Brahman's **upāyatva** is emphasised in the definition of **Prapatti**, the **Mantra** which pertains to it (**Dvayamantra**), the sentence which ordains it (**Caramaśloka**), other passages, the commentaries and tradition. The word **upāyatva** of the Kārikā refers to the chief **upāya**. Brahman alone becomes the chief **upāya** and Lakṣmī the secondary **upāya**, points out NM.

The next verse[^225_143] confirms the same contention that Lakṣmī merely forms an attribute of the Lord like His **guṇas** and **vigraha** (divine body). The **Caramaśloka**

[^225_141]: No. 120
[^225_142]: No. 120
[^225_143]: No. 121

***
[[P226]]
213

(**Gītā** XVIII.66) has the word **ekam** which,according to some, refers to the numerical oneness of the person who is resorted to,namely the Lord. But even then Lakṣmī's presence as an Attribute cannot be denied, concludes ŚŚ.

Quoting Deśika's two verses,[^226_144] NM questions as to why critics do not relish the relation between Śrī and Her consort as an attribute and a substantive, who form a single **śeṣi-principle**, with identity of taste (**aikarasya**) in all functions. She becomes the **Viśeṣaṇa**, though devoid of the **Saṅkalpa** to protect, and devoid of the acceptance of **Bhara** (**Bhārasvīkāra**). In his commentary on these verses ŚŚ observes that the **Dvayādhikāra** of RTS proves this point. The **Dvayamantra** itself is the **pramāṇa** which corroborates this view.

The following two Kārikās[^226_145] are the verses of Deśika (RTS, p.362) which NM quotes in support of his own statements made in the next two verses.

The question whether Lakṣmī a **cetana** can form an attribute of another **cetana** has been answered by

[^226_144]: Nos. 122,123
[^226_145]: Nos. 124,125

***
[[P227]]
214

Deśika by referring to the **Pratardana Vidyā** of the Upaniṣad.[^227_146] Therein, Indra and others are said to be the attributes of the **Paramātman**, who exists as their indwelling spirit. Therefore even a **cetana** can become a **Viśeṣaṇa** like any other **Viśeṣaṇa** which normally is **acetana**.

But nowhere should Lakṣmī be denigrated to the level of an **upalakṣaṇa**. Even in the state of **Bharanyāsa** she becomes an attribute of the **śaraṇya**. This has been confirmed by a quotation from Deśika: '**svāmyupāya upeyāśca**' etc.[^227_147]

The distinction between the three kinds of **Nyāsa**, **Svarūpa**, **Bhara** and **Phala** which has been mentioned earlier is again stated for the sake of emphasis by NM.

That what Deśika has stated in the verse '**prāmuktānāṁ**' and '**api cādivaṁ**' in his commentary on the Catuśślokī[^227_148] has been quoted by NM to confirm the **Puruṣakāratva** of Lakṣmī and Her eternal relationship with the Lord which status she gets by mutual will.

[^227_146]: See Kauṣītaki Upaniṣad, 3-11.
[^227_147]: RTS, p. 581.
[^227_148]: CŚB, p. 19

***
[[P228]]
215

Another verse '**Jñānabhogaḥ**' of Deśika[^228_149] is quoted to show the distinction between Lakṣmī and **nityasūris**, a point which has already been referred to. The verse '**Nyāsānāṁ prasādam ca**'[^228_150] points out that **Nyāsa** becomes possible due to the **Saṅkalpa** of Her Lord which is confirmed by the verse '**upāyadānam etc**'. of Deśika.[^228_151] According to ŚŚ, the word **upāyadānam** indicates the **Puruṣa-kāratva** of Lakṣmī. He quotes the verse '**Arthasvabhāvā**' of **Nikṣeparakṣā** to support Lakṣmī's **Puruṣakāratva**. And in the succeeding verse '**Viśeṣaṇā-viśeṣeṇa**' etc.,[^228_152] NM states that only the Supreme Brahman qualified by Lakṣmī who has three aspects (**ākāratraya**) is accepted as **upāya** of **Mokṣa** in this system. ŚŚ clarifies that the three aspects of Lakṣmī (**ākāratraya**) are: (1) **niru-pādhika-śeṣitva** (being the mistress of everything without any limiting adjunct) which is a synonym of **Īśvaratva** (Lordship); (2) **Vibhūtidvaya-śeṣitva** (mastery over the two **vibhūtis**); (3) **Tanniyantṛtva** (being the controller of these **vibhūtis**). By these special features

[^228_149]: No. 131
[^228_150]: PM. p.167
[^228_151]: No. 132
[^228_152]: No. 133

***
[[P229]]
216

Lakṣmī becomes superior to the three kinds of **jīvas**, (**baddha**, **mukta** and **nitya**) who are servants of the Supreme Lord and also to the **ajīvatattva** (**acit**). This is the purport of the next, Kārikā '**nirupādhika-śeṣitva**' etc.[^229_153]

The next Kārikā '**yadicchayaiva**' etc.,[^229_154] declares that Lakṣmī belongs to **Īśvarakoṭi** and not **jīvakoṭi** because the Lord commands (rules) and chastises all the beings only according to the wish and for the pleasure of Lakṣmī. It is therefore logical to conclude that such a Lakṣmī for whose sake the Lord does all this must belong to a category different from that of the **jīvas**.

The following verse '**eketarā**'[^229_155] points out even if Lakṣmī becomes part of the **Īśvara** as His attribute, there is no fear of **dvairājya** (having duality of rulers). The problem of **dvairājya** arises only when rulership is vested in two different persons. But as pointed out in the next verse '**prabhāditya-prakāreṇa**',[^229_156] the relation

[^229_153]: No. 134
[^229_154]: No. 135
[^229_155]: No. 136
[^229_156]: No. 137

***
[[P230]]
217

between Śrī and the Lord is like the relation between radiance (**prabhā**) and the Sun. Here one adds to the excellence of another and there is no other entity which effects that excellence. There is therefore inseparable relationship (**apṛthaksiddhatva**) between the Lord and His consort which again confirms the adjectival character of Śrī.

The verse '**ananyadevatā**' etc.[^230_157] clarifies that one who is desirous of salvation has only one deity, one **upāya**, and one **sādhya** (the Lord Viṣṇu). But still, doing **Śaraṇāgati** to Lakṣmī is acceptable to Lord Himself and as such, supreme one-pointedness by Him is not affected. This is what Deśika says in his **Gadya Bhāṣya**. This is also illustrated by another analogy: worshipping **Ananta**, **Garuḍa**, **Viṣvaksena** etc., which are all attendants of the Supreme Lord does not mitigate the value of Supreme onepointedness towards the Lord. Such is the case of Lakṣmī also who is the **Viśeṣaṇa** of the Lord.

In the next verse[^230_158] NM states that all the verses so far quoted from "**Śrīmān** upto '**ananyadevatā**'

[^230_157]: No. 138
[^230_158]: No. 139

***
[[P231]]
218

etc., are taken from Śrī Deśika's RTS, **Catuśślokī-bhāṣya**, **Gadya Bhāṣya** and **Nikṣepa Rakṣā**. In his commentary ŚŚ shows which verses are taken from which text of Deśika and also adds a few more works from which NM. has quoted to substantiate his views. They are **Paramārthastuti**, **Śrīstuti** (of VD), **Śrīstava** (of Kūreśa), **Śrī Raṅgarāja-stava** and **Śrīguṇaratnakośa** (of Parāśara Bhaṭṭa).

The following fifteen verses from "**Catuśślokyādhikārānte**" upto "**upāyuktāṁśa-vaiśadyāt**" enumerate the five views stated by Deśika in his CŚB regarding the essential nature and status of Lakṣmī.

NM states that since five views are mentioned by Deśika, each preceding view being over-ruled by the succeeding one, ordinary people will be confused as to which particular view Deśika personally advocates. He adds that where more than two or three views have been expressed by authors, it is conventional to take the last mentioned one as the personal view of the author. This is the practice followed in the **Vākyānvaya-section** of **Śrī Bhāṣya**. The fact that Lord alone is the cause of the entire Universe is common to all these views. Still, since He engages in the cosmic activity for the

***
[[P232]]
219

pleasure of His consort Lakṣmī, she also, is considered to be the cause of the Universe.

Of these five views the first one holds that Śrī is **aṇu** (atomic) in size. The second, third and fourth views maintain that she is all-pervasive. The third and fifth views are mutually at variance regarding the subordinate status of Lakṣmī being caused by the will of the Lord, according to the will of the both. ŚŚ in his commentary goes into a very elaborate and detailed discussion (from p. to ) on these different views. He makes an in-depth study of these views, giving a logical introduction, and quoting relevant authorities in support of each view. He shows the logical developments of these views in the order of enumeration and points out the subtleties of each view, highlighting their differences and correspondences. It may be mentioned that the interpretation of five views made by ŚŚ forms his distinct contribution to the development of the concept of Śrī because as NM has already pointed out, the **Catuśślokī-adhikāra** of Deśika cannot be understood easily by people of ordinary intellect.

While explaining these views ŚŚ also refutes the criticism of ŚTS, levelled against NM's text. The chief

***
[[P233]]
220

objection raised by ŚTS is that PM of NM presents Lakṣmī as **Puruṣakāra** but not as an **upāya**. ŚŚ answers that this is wrong and unfounded because NM has, on the authority of Deśika, established Lakṣmī not only as **Puruṣakāra**, but also as **upāya**, **prāpya** and the like.

In the middle of this discussion there is a lacuna of twelve palm-leaves of the manuscript (folio 165 to 177) and we are therefore, not in a position to surmise what ŚŚ had discussed therein.

In the text of the **Maṇidīpikā** i.e. (available after the break) we find the reply given by ŚŚ to VR, regarding another point.[^233_159] It is regarding the **Sāmarthya** (capacity or power) of the Lord by virtue of which even the **Puruṣakāra** of Lakṣmī becomes feasible and possible. ŚŚ objects to this view on the ground that if such a **sāmarthya** is to be accepted in God, it should be applied even to the **jīvas** who experience good or bad as a result of the past karmas, only because the Lord has through His **sāmarthya** prompted them to do so. Then the nature of God namely, His being opposed to all evils (**heya-pratibhaṭatva**) will become extinguished. ŚŚ on the

[^233_159]: p.345 ff.

***
[[P234]]
221

authority of **Śruti**-texts concludes that the role of God in such a case is one of (**Prayojaka-kartā**), a prompting agent and **sākṣin** (witnessing self). Nowhere is the concept of **sāmarthya** accepted or justified.

The next point of criticism raised by VR against PM is that the latter has failed to project the image of Lakṣmī as **nirupādhikaśeṣiṇī** i.e., as one in whom mastery over the universe is natural and unconditioned. Kārikās like '**sarvaśeṣitayā Rāmā**'justify this point. ŚŚ cites the **Virodhaparihāra** of **Kumāravaradācārya** in support of this view.

He also answers another criticism raised by VR. NM states that Lakṣmī is totally dependent on Lord like **jīva** and also that she is self-dependent like the Lord. ŚŚ answers in the negative. Lakṣmī's dependence on the Lord is by mutual will, i.e., she deliberately has become subordinate to the Lord and the Lord also has accepted it. It is because of this, that the Lord has become the ruler of everything other than Lakṣmī and Lakṣmī has become the ruler of everything other than the Lord. He points out that the subordinate status of Lakṣmī has been explained by NM as arising out of the mutual will of the

***
[[P235]]
222

couple. The reason behind this is as follows: **Śruti** declares both the Lord and Lakṣmī as rulers. But still there is another **śruti** passage which mention Śrī as the consort of the Lord. Yet another text refers to the Lord as 'one without an equal or superior'. The only way all these texts can be justified is by making Lakṣmī subordinate as a result of mutual will, that is, Lakṣmī out of Her own free will has become subordinate to the Lord. This also has been accepted by the Lord and hence **ubhayecchā** becomes the criterion.

In what may be described as the quintessence of the **Puruṣakāra Mīmāṁsā**, ŚŚ enlists the following views as propounded by Nārāyaṇa Muni( p.361).

1. Lakṣmī is the direct agent in all the cosmic activities where **anugraha** or grace is involved.

2. In activities involving **nigraha** however, she becomes only a prompting agent, making the Lord the actual performer of those deeds.

3. Lakṣmī is the inner controller of all the living beings excepting the Lord.

4. She is the support of all (**sarvādhārā**) excepting the Lord.

***
[[P236]]
223

5. She prompts the **jīvas** to do only good deeds.
6. She controls (**niyamana**) everybody through pure love, motivated by their welfare.
7. Even regarding the control of **jīvas** involving **nigraha**, she has the **sāmarthya** or capacity latent within Herself.
8. She becomes the mistress (**śeṣiṇī**) of both **nitya** and **līlā Vibhūtis**.
9. She forms the **śeṣiṇī** quite naturally but not as a result of any adventitious condition (**nirupādhika-śeṣi-tvam**).
10. She is all-pervasive.
11. She is a Mediatrix (**Puruṣakāra**) between man and God.
12. She becomes the recipient (**Uddeśya**) of offering in the form of **ātman** (**ātmahavis**).
13. She has everything other than the Lord (including **cit** and **acit**) as her body.
14. She becomes an attribute (**viśeṣaṇa**) of the Lord.
15. She is the Mother of the entire creation.
16. She forms the means or **upāya** in granting unlimited Bliss.

***
[[P237]]
224

17. She removes all undesirable things through the grace of the Lord.

18. As a result of mutual will (ubhayecchā), She attains (a) **śeṣatva** to the Lord, (b) becomes controlled by the Lord (niyāmyatva), (c) dependence on the Lord (pāratantrya) and (d) she becomes supported by the Lord (ādheyatva).

19. She is the ruler of everyone other than the Lord.

In the following verse "Yayākrośī" NM states that Deśika by his powerful arguments rejected several views on Lakṣmī such as (1) That she is not a sentient being (acetanā), (2) That she is equal to the Lord in all aspects, and (3) That she is a mere bestower of wealth (dhanadā). ŚŚ in his commentary cites relevant passages from Deśika's Catuśślokī-Bhāṣya in support of His view.

In another one-and-a-half Kārikas "Catuśślokīsāram" etc.,[^237_160] NM appeals to those who want to ascertain in Deśika's view, whether or not Lakṣmī is equal to the Lord, to read his Catuśślokīsāra starting from the very nāndī-verse. The opening verse of CŚB is:

[^237_160]: No. 156.

***
[[P238]]
225

"svaseṣaśeṣārtho niravadhikanirbādhamahimā
phalānāṁ dātā yaḥ, phalamapi ca śarīraka-mitaḥ |
śrīyaṁ tatsadhricīṁ tadupāsadanatrāśasamānim
abhiṣṭautuṁ tutyamavitathamatiryāmuna muniḥ"

The verse which brings out the essence of Catuśślokī according to NM is the following verse:

"atra svāmitvasulabhya-phaladatva-phalatvatāḥ |
ānurūpyeṇa saṁbandhāḥ śrīpatau darśitāḥśriyaḥ"

It will be clear on an impartial analysis that these two verses bring out the mutual conformity (ānurūpya) of the divine couple. The word 'sadhricīm' point to the '**ānurūpya**' but not **sarvasāmya**. This is the major point of difference between NM and VR and according to ŚŚ, NM alone represents the views of Deśika, in the proper perspective.

The following two verses '**ananyādhīnā**' and '**nidānamekamjagataṁ**' are quotations from Parāśara;[^238_161] they,

[^238_161]: Nos. 159, 160 ab

***
[[P239]]
226

according to NM, explain the '**jagatkāraṇatva**' of Lakṣmī as it is really, in its full implication. "When the Divine Couple is said to be the **jagatkāraṇa**, **sāmya** seems to be the chief character of the couple; then how can it be argued by NM that there is only **sāmarasya** but not **sāmya**?" asks a **pūrvapakṣin**.

NM answers this question by a simple statement that all such passages have already been explained, since Lakṣmī is always known by **anugraha**. Being the Mother, she cannot create the universe in all its aspects, through **nigraha**. Only she becomes the **Kāraṇa** by making her husband do all these through an identity of taste, **sāmarasya**. It was also stated that even the capacity to punish the wicked is latent in her, although she never exercises it.

The text of PM assumes greater importance now when NM declares in another Kārikā, '**Lokācāryasya**' etc., that the views of VD explained so far with an opening declaration "**patnyāḥ pativadīdrktvam asti neti nirūpyate**" (No.5), are in tune with the views of "**Lokācārya**" (Piḷḷai Lokācārya)[^239_162] also. Though on the face of it, there seems to be a controversy between their views, one can still find after a careful analysis, similarity of thoughts which makes

[^239_162]: No. 161

***
[[P240]]
227.

for an identical system. This is all what wise men should look for, he argues.

Explaining this verse, SS points out that Deśika in his RTS and other texts has established that Lakṣmī is all-pervasive (Vibhu and **Īśvarī**), the means of liberation (**upāya**), Mother of the creation (**mātā**) and that in accordance with these is postulated the view that she is the **jagatkāraṇa**, the object of **Śaraṇāgati**, the object of meditation and attribute of the Lord. As contrasted with these, PL in his works established the view that Lakṣmī belongs to the category of the **jīvas**, she cannot be the **Kāraṇa** of the universe and that she can form the 'puruṣakāra'. As such how can there be identity of thought between these two Ācāryas? This question is answered by ŚŚ that in spite of these apparent differences both these Ācāryas are unanimous in their overall conception of Lakṣmī. As such, scholars should adopt the method of synthesis and concurrence, but not one of difference and confrontation. The remaining part of the text of PM, is devoted to identify such areas of apparent difference between PL and VD and attempts at finding compromise between them by appealing to the intention of the Ācāryas.

Once such instance is the 'giving up of all Dharmas' mentioned in the **Caramaśloka**. PL advocates literally giving

***
[[P241]]
228

up all the Dharmas, whereas VD refers to giving up of those **Vidyās** which are part of **Bhakti** as a discipline, and which cannot be actually performed by ordinary men. This is a point of difference between these two **ācāryas**. ŚŚ in his commentary on the verse '**dharmatyāga-vidhau**'[^241_163] quotes the relevant portions of the **Mumukṣuppaḍi** and **Parandapaḍi** of PL and also **Maṇavāḷa Māmuni's** commentary thereon alongside VD's RTS to show that strictly speaking, there is **aika-kaṇṭhya** only between these two writers, inspite of the apparent difference. While PL says the word '**vraja**' should be interpreted as '**buddhi-pappu**' (give up mentally) VD says, '**Vidhīprārthanāpūrvaka**' etc., where the word **Vidhi**, implies the same idea of "mental renunciation". The commentator MM explains this concept of '**vraja**' which implies the idea of Deśika himself, that only the difficult Dharmas are recommended to be given up.

Another point of concurrence between PL and VD is that a man should not prevent the Lord's grace flowing on him. Whatever is expected of him must be performed which results in his **Puruṣārtha**. Passages

[^241_163]: No. 162

***
[[P242]]
229

from the **Mumukṣuppaḍi** and RTS conveying this idea are quoted. This is the spirit in which NM declared:

> " लोकाचार्यप्रबन्धस्य प्रधीसारस्य चोभयोः।
> प्रायो बुधैरेककण्ठ्यं ग्राह्यं ग्रन्थज्ञ सम्मतम्।। 161।।

ŚŚ also, on the basis of NM's observation, explains that the apparent difference between VD and PL can be resolved by adopting the **anuvādapakṣa** of **Vaṅgi Vaṁśeśvara**.

ŚŚ quotes passages from RTS and **Mumukṣuppaḍi** (MMP) referring to the **anuvādapakṣa** of **Vaṅgi Vaṁśeśa**. Therefore both the Ācāryas are in favour of this **anuvādapakṣa**. What **Vaṅgi Vaṁśeśa** (p.363) meant is that since in the **Caramaśloka** Arjuna has been directed by the Lord to surrender to Him [**śaraṇaṁ vraja**] with a view to attain **Mokṣa** (Liberation), this **śaraṇāgati** can only be 'mānasika' (mental). This is so because **Mokṣa** is possible through **jñāna**. (**jñānān mokṣaḥ**). This is what is actually stated in the **Gītā**. This is the spirit of **anuvāda** (restatement) **pakṣa** as intended by **Gītā**. Therefore ŚŚ concludes that even if one notices certain differences between the Ācāryas one should try to reconcile them by taking their intention into consideration. Only thus the **aikakaṇṭhya** (the oneness) of the **darśana** can be preserved.

***
[[P243]]
230

The next verse '**yuktāpta-prabandhānāṁ**' repeats the same idea that while one should aim at the synthesis of works of our '**āptas**' by understanding their import, no such attempt need be made in the case of works of those who are not our '**āptas**' (well-wishers). The **Virodha** that is clear in their case (**anāptas**' works) need not be reconciled at all. The next verse also '**āpta-vākye virodha**' drives home the same point. The succeeding five verses[^243_164] illustrate this point by taking the statements of Rāmānuja on **Prapatti** found in his **Gadyas** and **Gītā-Bhāṣya**. It is common knowledge that while Rāmānuja makes **Prapatti** an independent means of salvation in his **Gadyas**,[^243_165] he makes it an **aṅga** to **Bhakti** in his commentary on the **Caramaśloka** (**Gītā** 18-66). But as explained by Deśika there is no contradiction here["**ārtopacchandanām gadyam**"](ŚG.p.137). The **Gadya**-statement is for these **ārta**'s (the impatient kind of prapannas, whereas his **Gītābhāṣya**-statement is to please those who are not favour of an independent status for **prapatti**. ŚŚ

[^243_164]: Nos. 163
[^243_165]: Cf. > तस्य वशीकरणं तच्छरणगतिरेव (śrībhāṣya 1.4)

***
[[P244]]
observes that even in the case of a single writer we have to adopt this kind of reading the intention when there is an apparent contradiction in his works. In the same way if there are two different writers one should try to get at their intention by overcoming seeming dissimilarities, provided they are known to be '**āptas**' (well-wishers), who are known for their zeal to safeguard the great tradition. Since both VD and PL are great teachers who are acknowledged as 'The Preserver of the System, we have to read their intention and draw parallels rather than highlight the apparent differences observes ŚŚ. Quoting the entire section on '**aikaśāstray samarthanam**' (II Chapter) forming part of Vātsya Varada's **Prameyāmālā**, ŚŚ points out that even as the **Pūrva-mīmāṁsā** of Jaimini and **Brahmasūtras** of Bādarāyaṇa are, inspite of the apparent differences in terms of the topics, authorship, and **adhikārins**, are treated as a single unitary **śāstra**, the works of VD and PL which constitute a single **śāstra** namely **Rahasyatraya**, should be treated as having a single goal or intention. The apparent distinct should be explained away by taking their ultimate import and intention.

***
[[P245]]
232

The succeeding 2-3 Kārikās[^245_166] of NM pay glowing tributes to the **Śrīvacanabhūṣaṇa** (ŚVB) and other **Rahasyas** of PL as **texts** known for their compactness and depth of thought. The RTS and other texts of VD also can be found to convey the same ideas when we take their import (**tātparya**) into consideration. The method of reading the **tātparya** of RTS is shown by Kumāra-varada in his **Tattvatrayacūlukā**.

ŚŚ in his commentary quotes profusely from the **Śrīvacanabhūṣaṇa**, RTS and **Cūlukā**.

The next Kārikā[^245_167] mentions that Varavaramuni, the celebrated commentator on the ŚVB adopts the views of Deśika to show the identity of thought between VD and PL in matters where an apparent contradiction seems to emerge.

ŚŚ quotes from the commentary of **Manavāḷamahāmuni** on MMP where he also refers to PL's **Parandapaḍi** and **Śriyāpatipaḍi** to explain some apparent contradictions

[^245_166]: Nos. 172, 173
[^245_167]: No. 174, 175

***
[[P246]]
233

in ŚVB. Therefore there should not be any hesitation in interpreting the works of Ācāryas belonging to our tradition in resolving the apparent contradiction by taking their intention into consideration.

The verse '**pradhānapratitantra**' clearly points that certain concepts which are unique to our system propounded by Śrī Rāmānuja (e.g. **Śarīraśarīri-bhāva**) cannot be altered by anybody including Brahmā.

The succeeding verse[^246_168] points out that one need not unnecessarily indulge in discussions which are unnecessary. It is enough if one takes the cue on the method suggested by **ācāryas** and arrives at **upāya** (means of Liberation) and **phala** (the actual result). Explaining ŚŚ says that the discussion on **Kaivalya** is a futile exercise and nobody can arrive at any definite conclusion. The question whether **Kaivalya** is **nitya** or **anitya** is not a new one. In the following 4 Kārikās[^246_169] NM observes that a few immediate disciples of Śrī Rāmānuja himself held **Kaivalya** to be eternal. Others thought that it is not eternal. Deśika in his NŚ and **Tātparyacandrikā**

[^246_168]: "upayuktāṁśaḥ" [Kā.176]
[^246_169]: Nos. 178, 179, 180, 181

***
[[P247]]
234

has referred to these two views and probably suggesting his reference in the second view that **Kaivalya** is **anitya**. ŚŚ explains the position by quoting profusely from a number of works of several other **ācāryas** like Yāmuna, Rāmānuja, Varada Viṣṇu Miśra, Ātreyarāmānuja and Parāśara Bhaṭṭa. He gives the view of the **Siddhāntin** that **Kaivalya** is not **Mokṣa**. The person who attains **Kaivalya** abides somewhere within this material universe itself and therefore **Kaivalya** cannot be eternal. Since Rāmānuja's views on **Kaivalya** mentioned in **Gītābhāṣya** seem to be confusing,some scholars maintain indifference regarding **Kaivalya**. NM says that the wise should give up the discussion of **Kaivalya**. He asks a very thought-provoking question: 'What does it matter, if **Kaivalya** is eternal or not'? Those who have a doubt, however, can refer to the works of Deśika.

Concluding his work[^247_170] NM makes a humble appeal in keeping with his great tradition and learning,that what he has discussed is on the lines shown by great **ācāryas** like Vedānta Deśika and that any statements of commission or omission must be pardoned by the Lord and His Divine wives.

[^247_170]: See Thesis, p. 416.

***
[[P248]]
235

The last verse '**Nārāyaṇa**' etc., mentions the name of the work as **Puruṣakāra Mīmāṁsā** and the name of the author as **Śrī-Vatsāṅka Nārāyaṇa Muni**.

Commentary of ŚŚ thereon, as pointed out, traces the great tradition of Ahobila Maṭha to Śrī Varada Viṣṇu Miśra who was the nephew of Great Rāmānuja and who occupied the **Śrī-Bhāṣya-Siṁhāsana**. He also quotes Kumāra Varada on the usage of the word '**Puruṣakāra**' which refers to Lakṣmī, which need not necessarily refer to Puruṣa, but it can be applied to any person who acts as a **ghaṭaka**. Deśika's definition of the terms '**Puruṣakāra**' '**sāpekṣānana**' etc., and thus the text thus comes to an end.[^248_171]

The details of the commentator and his parentage have already been discussed earlier.[^248_172]

***

[^248_171]: Vide p.418
[^248_172]: See ch.I

***
***
[[P250]]
236

## CONTRIBUTION OF ŚRĪŚAILEŚA
CONTRIBUTION OF ŚRĪŚAILEŚA TO ŚRĪVAIṢṆAVISM

An attempt has been made in the foregoing chapters to study 'The Concept of Puruṣakāra on the basis of the 'Puruṣakāra Mīmāṁsā' of Nārāyaṇa Muni with the help of the commentary Maṇidīpikā of Śrīśaileśa. A detailed analysis of the work has also been made in Chapter IV to understand the intricacies of the concept, highlighting some important shades of difference between ŚŚ and VR. It has already been noted that the ŚTŚ of VR was composed with the specific purpose of demolishing the PM. 

<details><summary>विश्वास-टिप्पनी</summary>

कथम् इदं सत्यम्??
</details>


It is in this context that the Maṇidīpikā of ŚŚ assumes greater importance because he has tried to answer all the objections raised by VR, quoting line by line and para by para, almost the entire text of ŚTŚ. It is really unfortunate that VR should have written ŚTŚ with the purpose of refuting the PM, root and branch. After all,both NM and VR claim to represent the great tradition of Śrī Rāmānuja as substantiated by Vedānta Deśika in his works.+++(5)+++ 

The contribution of ŚŚ must be viewed as a remarkable attempt to resurrect the image of his Guru Nārāyaṇa Muni, clearing up the doubts raised in the criticism of VR.

***

[[P249]]
237

It may be worthwhile to probe into the circumstances under which VR had to write the ŚTŚ against the PM of NM. Śrī Uttamoor Vīrarāghavāchār in the Preface to his Edition of ŚTS[^249_1] observes as follows: 

> 'Among the successors of Śrī Ādivanśaṭhakopa, the first pontiff of Ahobila Maṭṭ, was the author of Puruṣakāra Mīmaṁsā who was a Teṅgalai at the beginning. Having been in the Teṅgalai-sampradāya, he later embraced the Vaḍagalai tradition.[^249_2]
>
> Because of his earlier Teṅgalai learnings, he declared in his PM that Lakṣmī cannot be the means of **upāya** (liberation). But he tried to justify this through the texts of Deśika. Since the entire text of PM is composed in 'Anuṣṭubh' metre, NM's position on this mater is not quite clear. 
> 
> Still we may state that he maintained Lakṣmī to be **Vibhu** but not **aṇu**. Deśika tried to interpret some of the statements of earlier Ācāryas which are apparently controversial and contradictory in such a way that they fall within the traditional framework. 
> 
> The author of PM also, basing himself on the view that Lakṣmī cannot be the **upāya**, tried to interpret the statements of Deśika in such a way that the causal character (**kāraṇatva**) and **antaryāmitva** of Lakṣmī are relegated to secondary importance.

[^249_1]: Śrītattvasiddhāñjana, Ed. Uttamoor Vīrarāghavācārya, Preface, p.4.
[^249_2]: See also R.C.Lester,"Renunciation in Śrīvaiṣṇavism," JOR, Vol. LVI-LXII, p.94.

[[P251]]
238

> The same **ācārya** (NM) has composed later on another section to justify Lakṣmī as the **upāya** of **Mokṣa** and added it to his PM, the the end-portion has been destroyed by some people. All the ideas mentioned in the PM are contradictory to the views of Deśika. Sākṣātsvāmī (Vedānta Rāmānuja Muni) the preceptor of Śrī Gopāladeśika (alias Śrī Tirukkuḍandai Deśikan) composed the ŚTŚ to correct the views of the PM, after studying all the available texts on the concept of Śrī.

<details><summary>विश्वास-टिप्पनी</summary>

> परंतु एते प्रथमं तेन्गलै-संप्रदाये स्थिताः पश्चात् श्री-देशिक-संप्रदाय-निष्ठा बभूवुः। एतैः प्राक् पुरुषकार-मीमांसेति लक्ष्म्याः मोक्षोपायत्वं न अस्ति इति तेंगलै-संप्रदायार्थ एव श्री-देशिक-अनुष्टुप्-श्लोकैर् एव संग्रहेण सर्वार्थ-प्रतिपादनात् न अत्र सर्वं विशदम् नाणुत्वम्। … 

इति संस्कृतभूमिकानुवादो ऽत्र। 

He was misled by tenkalai polemicists -

> "एभिर् एव पश्चात् श्रिय उपायत्व-स्थापक-ग्रन्थ-भागो ऽपि व्यलेखी"ति,  
"स तु कैश्चित् लोपित" इति च श्री-लक्ष्मी-नृसिंहास्थान-मूर्धाभिषिक्तैः महाचार्यैः प्रत्यपादि  
इत्य् उभय-वेदान्त-ग्रन्थ-मालायाम् ईशोपनिषन्-मुद्रणावसरे भूमिकायाम् अस्माभिर् निर्दिष्टम् अपि द्रष्टव्यम्।

This error is shown below.
</details>


It is not known first of all whether the successors of Ādivan Śaṭhakopa were Teṅgalais or not to start with. It is worth noting that according to these critics the first five successors of Ādivan Śaṭhakopa were Teṅgalai learnings. But as made out in Chapter I of this thesis, NM the author of PM was the 14th Jeer of Ahobila Maṭṭ, but not the second.+++(5)+++ If he were to make an effort to reconcile between the views of Deśika and Piḷḷai Lokācārya any important critic and well-wisher of the Śrī Sampradāya should welcome such a move whole-heartedly without any reservation.

***
[[P252]]
239

It also does not appear reasonable to believe that NM refutes the idea of **upāyatva** of Lakṣmī. As has been explained by ŚŚ in his **Maṇidīpikā**, NM accepts Lakṣmī as the **upāya**, **upeya** and **jagatkāraṇa** through her unique status as the **Viśeṣaṇa** of the Lord. His understanding of Deśika's view might have been different from that of VR and others who accept total similarity between the Lord and Lakṣmī. 

That Lakṣmī cannot be the **upāya** of **Mokṣa** is no doubt accepted by the Teṅgalais. But the arguments made by NM and the elaborate explanations given by ŚŚ thereon make it clear that NM could not have been a Teṅgalai for that reason. 

The **Svarupa-vibhutva** of Lakṣmī has been justified by him in several places. It is true that NM towards the end of the text tries to reconcile Vaḍagalai and Teṅgalai traditions on certain issues. NM was eager[^252_3] to solve the dispute between these two sects in keeping with the great tradition of Śrī Rāmānuja.

[^252_3]: See Kārikās
> युक्तमाप्तप्रबन्धानामैक्य तात्पर्यवर्णनात्। नक्यार्थानासवाक्यानाभिरुद्धाद्यं वर्णनं ।। 163।। आसद्ग्रन्थोऽप्यर्थाऽप्यं विशेषधस्कुरुण यथा। तात्पर्यकृप्या निर्वाहो भिन्नकर्तृकयोरथा ।।170।। अतिगंभीरस्र्भश्री मद्रच भूषणम्। अन्यायाप्यरहस्यानि तादृशान्तएवहि।। 172।। रहस्यत्रयसारादौ तेषां तात्पर्यमूचिरे। आपातप्रतिपन्नार्थो ह्यापातोऽनुपपत्तिभिः।। 173।। प्रायेण सुन्दरस्वामुनि श्रुतिषु दृश्यते। प्रधानप्रति तन्त्रार्थं भाष्यकारैरूपादितम्। इत्थंमन्यथा वक्तुं वागधीशोऽपि न क्षमः।।175।।

***
[[P253]]
240

Those who feel that an author belonging to a particular tradition should not quote a renowned author of a different tradition should keep in mind that they are doing great disservice to the glorious system of Śrī Rāmānuja. Śrī Deśika himself detested such parochial tendencies among the followers of his system and prays that 'asūyā' the mother of mutual quarrels should leave them all.[^253_4]

The statement made by Uttamūr Vīrarāghavācārya that the author of PM wrote another section justifying the **upāyatva** of Lakṣmī and that it was destroyed or taken away by some also does not sound convincing.+++(4)+++ It is true however that folios 165 to 176 of the Palm-leaf manuscript No: R.3147 (GOML) has a lacuna towards the end of the text. The point where the break occurs is where ŚŚ explains the five **pakṣas** about Lakṣmī's exact nature mentioned by VD in his CŚB. However, there does not seem to have been any serious break in the argument of the text of the PM proper.

[^253_4]: Cf.
> आपातस्फुरद्रमपाणिने दर्शनेऽस्माशासनीयमपरेण विपश्चितं आपातशास्त्रज्ञानोन्मत्तान् बुद्धैर्न्यक्षेणनीचैश्च राजनननीविहितान्। [Saṅkalpa Sūryodaya, p.264. Commentary Prabhāvalī Part I.]

***
[[P254]]
241

Even the portion of **Maṇidīpikā** where this break occurs does not seem to have suffered much and the point where it resumes is almost a continuation of the earlier discussion. Therefore it seems reasonable to accept that there could not have been any serious gap in the text of PM although some traditional scholars mostly through hearsay, than after any practical examination of the manuscripts, pronounce that the PM suffers from lacunae. As the present study is based upon the PM with ŚŚ's MD which is preserved more or less in tact, it can safely be concluded that NM's work also represents the traditional view of Deśika on the status of Lakṣmī. As it is quite possible for two great thinkers belonging to one and the same tradition to differ from each other on certain doctrinal issues, one need not jump to conclusions that VR is the true representative of Deśika and that NM being a convert from the Teṅgalai tradition,represents Deśika in the wrong light.

Judged by his elaborate commentary **Maṇidīpikā**, ŚŚ is a great scholar in the Śrīvaiṣṇava (**Ubhaya Vedānta**) lore, apart from the usual erudition in the Sanskrit texts. His brilliant analysis of Deśika's works, especially the RTS and the NŚ and its commentaries, which he names and quotes, is quite amazing.

***
[[P255]]
242

He comments on the PM in the traditional fashion, explaining each word and substantiating the points with innumerable quotations, pointing out the **Pūrvapakṣa** advanced mostly by VR and giving suitable reply in the end.

He also tried to drive home the central theme of the PM, viz., the role of Lakṣmī as the '**Puruṣakāra**' between man and God -- with commendable ease. As is clear from the contents of the MD, the **Puruṣakāra** of Śrī is not the point of controversy between NM and VR. It is chiefly on Lakṣmī's role as the **upāya** that VR criticises NM and ŚŚ in his MD, tries hard to prove that the **upāyatva** of Śrī had been conceded by NM through Her '**Viśeṣaṇatva**' alone. All other prerogatives of Śrī are the outcome of her status as **Viśeṣaṇa** alone.

If the single aim of ŚTŚ is to demolish the PM, the chosen aim of MD was to project the image of NM as a true follower of VD. For a system which has suffered more from its own internal schisms than by any external factor, the healing touch should also come within. This healing touch was provided by ŚŚ. But for ŚŚ perhaps the text of NM could never have been recovered from the charge of being anti-Deśika or Teṅgalai or pro-Teṅgalai in spirit,

***
[[P256]]
243

It is also interesting to note that VR has been criticised not only by ŚŚ in his MD but also in another work called **Aupādhikaśeṣatva Bhaṅga**[^256_5] of an anonymous writer. 

Such differences of opinion between one writer and another within the same tradition has not become the sole instance of Śrīvaiṣṇavism since other systems also have the same problem. Since available works are in the form of manuscripts or printed texts which speak for themselves, scholars who look for facts and truths are always amply rewarded in their efforts if they are sincere and hardworking.

In the light of these observations, it is but reasonable to conclude that ŚŚ occupies a place of prominence in the commentorial tradition as one who tries to justify his Guru by interpreting his views as part of the genuine tradition. Śrīśaileśa's remarkable powers of comprehension, analytical approach, methodical interpretation, rational argumentation, and above all, the spirit of synthesis, make him a great commentator the Śrīvaiṣṇava tradition has produced in recent times.

* * * * * * * * *

[^256_5]: See Descriptive Catalogue of manuscripts (Adyar Library), p.244, Work No: 182.

***
[[P257]]
244

## NĀRĀYAṆA MUNI'S CONTRIBUTION
CONCLUSION:
NĀRĀYAṆA MUNI'S CONTRIBUTION TO ŚRĪVAIṢṆAVISM

One of the peculiar characteristics of Śrīvaiṣṇava system of thought is the concept of Śrī which has so far been studied in the foregoing chapters, tracing its origin to the Veda itself. There again the concept of Lakṣmī as the **Puruṣakāra** (Mediator) between God and man attains considerable importance, because redemption of erring souls has to be accounted for, in any theological system. Nārāyaṇa Muni in the **Puruṣakāra Mīmāṁsā** with commendable precision, eloquence and authority explains the position of Lakṣmī as the **Puruṣakāra**. Deśika and his works have been the mainstay for NM in explaining these concepts although he refers to other Ācāryas also like Yāmuna, Vātsya Varada, Ātreya Rāmānuja, Kūreśa, Parāśara Bhaṭṭa, Kumāra Varada, Piḷḷai Lokācārya Vyāsārya and others. He also refers to the works of Parāṅkuśa (Nammāḻvār) by name. Of the texts he has quoted, mention may be made of the **Rāmāyaṇa**, **Mahābhārata**, **Brahmāṇḍa**, **Kāśyapa** and the **Viṣṇupurāṇas**, all the **stotras** of Ācāryas on Lakṣmī, **Ātmasiddhi**, commentaries on the **Catuśślokī** and the three **Gadyas**, **Lakṣmī Kalyāṇa** of Parāśara Bhaṭṭa, **Lakṣmī Sahasranāma**, **Nikṣepa Rakṣā**, **Nyāsa Tilaka**, **Nyāya Kuliśa**, **Nyāyasiddhāñjana**, its commentaries,

***
[[P258]]
245

**Paramata Bhaṅga**, **Paramārthastuti**, **Prapanna Pārijāta**, **Pūrva** and **Uttara Mīmāṁsā**, **Rahasyaratnāvalī-hṛdaya**, **Rahasya-trayasāra**, **Sātvatasaṁhitā**, **Śrī Bhāṣya**, **Śrī Vacana Bhūṣaṇa**, **Tattva Traya**, **Tattvatraya Cūlukā**, **Tattva Ṭīkā**, **Tātparya Candrikā**,the **Upaniṣads**, **Viṣṇuvaibhavakāra**, **Viṣṇusahasranāma** and **Yatirāja Saptati**. It goes without saying that considerable interest was generated among scholars regarding the exact nature and role of Lakṣmī only after the advent of Piḷḷai Lokācārya and Vedānta Deśika. Their disciples and admirers took up various aspects of Lakṣmī found in their works and wrote independent treatises, elucidations and commentaries on specific aspects of Lakṣmī. Of these some of the works are incomplete and a few others are anonymous eg. '**Aṇutva Cūlukā**',[^258_1] '**Āṇutva-samarthana**',[^258_2] '**Lakṣmī Vibhutva samarthanaṁ**',[^258_3] '**Lakṣmīyupāyatva-nirāsa**',[^258_4] '**Lakṣmyupāyatva-samarthana**'[^258_5]; '**Lakṣmī Vibhutva-Khaṇḍana**',[^258_6] '**Śrī Brahmatva-Vyudāsa**',[^258_7] '**Śrī Brahmatva-samarthana**', '**Lakṣmyu-

[^258_1]: 70755 (Ad. Lib.)
[^258_2]: 70705 (Ad. Lib.)
[^258_3]: 70206 (Ed. Lib.)
[^258_4]: 70705 (Ad. Lib.)
[^258_5]: 69715.(Ad. Lib.)
[^258_6]: 71246 (Ad. Lib), 69715 (Ad) (2 manuscripts)
[^258_7]: 70755 (Ad. Lib.)
[^258_8]: 70755 (Ad. Lib.) 68447 (Ad. Lib.)

***
[[P259]]
246

**pāyatva-dīpa**,[^259_9] '**Śrī-Tattvadarpaṇa**',[^259_10] '**Śrī-Tattvaratna**';[^259_11] '**Lakṣmīmaṇidīpikā**',[^259_12] '**Lakṣmī-samārādhana-saṅgraha**',[^259_13] '**Śrī-prapatti**',[^259_14] '**Śrīyamupāyatva-samarthanam**',[^259_15] '**Lakṣmī śaraṇyatvam**',[^259_16] and '**Lakṣm yupāyatva-vicāra**'.[^259_17] It is quite probable that all these works are later to PM because even the ŚTŚ of Vedānta Rāmānuja himself was a subsequent work.

Irrespective of the differences between **Vaḍagalai** and **Teṅgalai** not withstanding the controversy between PM and ŚTŚ, the **Puruṣakāra Mīmāṁsā** has its own place of eminence in the post-Vedānta Deśika **Śrīvaiṣṇava** literature. Written in crisp and sweet style, the text of the PM conveys the ideas in a simple and unambiguous manner. It may be true that the ŚTŚ of VR is more popular than the **Puruṣakāra Mīmāṁsā** among the world of scholars. 

[^259_9]: D.5358 (GOML)
[^259_10]: TR 253 (Ad. Lib)
[^259_11]: R.1299 (GOML)
[^259_12]: R.3420 (GOML).
[^259_13]: D.5357 (GOML)
[^259_14]: D.1873; D5205 (GOML)
[^259_15]: R.2272 (a) (GOML)
[^259_16]: R.2272(b) (GOML)
[^259_17]: R.5731 (GOML)

***
[[P260]]
247

It is also surprising to note that while the ŚTŚ has been printed more than once or twice, the PM has not been printed more than once, and even that edition of PM is not available.+++(5)+++ Some traditional scholars are still of the opinion that it is incomplete - but it is not true. This atleast reflects the comparative neglect to which this important works has been subjected.

The great admirable feature of the PM is its catholicity of approach to the problem. He mentions Lokācārya by name and tries to reconcile the differences between him and Vedānta Deśika.[^260_18] NM is strongly in favour of seeing points of concurrence between these two Ācāryas. The **aikakaṇṭhya** which he mentions in the spirit of a great Ācārya cannot be merely brushed aside as statement of an enthusiast. It is backed by a genuine interest in presenting the system of Rāmānuja to the scholars at large in its pure spirit of tolerance and synthesis. According to NM both Piḷḷai Lokācārya and Deśika are **āptas** or benefactors of humanity. Their works should not be subjected to narrow interpretation and limited non-synthetic understanding. The Commentary

[^260_18]: See Text, p.367
> लोकाचार्यप्रबन्धस्य त्रयीसारस्य चोभयोः।
> प्रायो बुधैरेककण्ठ्यं ग्राह्यं ग्रन्थज्ञ सम्मतम्।। K161।।

***
[[P261]]
248

of ŚŚ turns the word **āpta**, the original, into a superlative **āptatama**. ŚŚ also points out that Maṇavāḷamahā-muni in his commentary on **Mumukṣuppaḍi** has accepted Deśika's views on certain aspects of Lakṣmī. In the spirit of great thinkers, ŚŚ goes to the extent of saying that there is '**ekaprabandhatva**' between the works of Deśika and Lokācārya in explaining the **Rahasyatraya** as in the case of **Pūrvamīmāṁsā** of Jaimini and **Brahmasūtras** of Bādarāyaṇa.[^261_19] NM refers to **Śrīvacanabhūṣaṇa** of PL by name and pays a glowing tribute to it as a work of depth and significance.[^261_20]

It is clear that PM of NM is a remarkable work, which tries to spread the message of Lakṣmī's infallible role as the Mediator between man and God, reflecting the highest traditions of the **Śrīvaiṣṇava** system of thought bearing the great name of Rāmānuja as its systematizer. Of the innumerable Ācāryas who try to project the image of the system in the eyes of others, Nārāyaṇa Muni's name deserves to be written in letters of gold. The spirit of

[^261_19]: > एवं प्रवृत्ते अत्यन्तमद्विकलोकाचार्यप्रबन्धयोर्द्वयोः रहस्यत्रयलक्षणप्रबन्धार्थं विवक्षया तान्निर्णयेऽत्यन्तैक-फलक तया द्वाकप्रबन्धाता मेधवात्। (P.382)
[^261_20]: > अतिगम्भीरसन्दभं श्रीमद्वचनभूषणम्।
> अन्यान्मापि रहस्यनि तादृशान्त एव हि।। (p.383)

***
[[P262]]
249

synthesis which he breaths into his work is in the best interests of **Śrīvaiṣṇava** community as a whole. It is also equally necessary to remember the name of Śrīśaileśa who presented the **Puruṣakāra Mīmāṁsā** in the proper perspective, in the spirit with which it was written by his great master NM. This work therefore deserves to be read in greater detail than it is being studied at present and the finer points appreciated not only in the light of itself, but also in that of **Maṇidīpikā**.

* * * * *

***
